## Fresh-Eyes Peer-Code Review - PDF Layout Width Cache and Script Safety Audit
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T00:32:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-width-cache-after-20260707T0022Z/`.
- Review scope: re-read AGENTS/README, applied `multi-pass-bug-hunting`, ran UBS against the dirty Rust diff and then narrowed to `src/pdf.rs`, manually traced the freshly modified PDF paragraph/token/segment flow, and sampled the peer-written run-id/archive-hardening scripts (`scripts/validate-run-id.sh`, artifact scripts, e2e scripts, `install.sh`, and `install.ps1`). The run-id validation is before artifact path construction/cleanup in the sampled scripts, archive extraction rejects traversal/link entries before install, changed Bash scripts parse with `bash -n`, and the source-shape tests for run-id ordering pass.
- Root cause fixed: the earlier single-token fast path removed one avoidable allocation but still left the dominant PDF layout stage repeatedly reshaping identical text fragments. Paragraph breaking, glue construction, hyphen penalty width, and final segment construction all asked `Faces::shaped_width` for the same `(font slot, font size, text)` values many times within one render. Because `Faces::shaped_width` performs deterministic GSUB/GPOS shaping and depends only on those inputs, the repeated calls were pure recomputation.
- Renderer change: `LayoutCx` now owns a render-local bounded `WidthCache` keyed by `(font slot, font size)` and text. PDF paragraph word measurement, interword glue, discretionary hyphen width, and positioned segment width calculation use the cache in the layout path. The fallback public/private helper path without a `LayoutCx` still calls `Faces::shaped_width` directly. The cache is dropped after each render, has a fixed entry cap, does not use globals or threads, and stores exactly the same `LayoutUnit` values returned by the old path.
- First-principles proof: the cache changes lookup mechanics only. It does not alter tokenization, hyphenation points, paragraph items, demerit scoring, selected breaks, segment grouping, floating-point coordinate math, emitted text, PDF object ordering, fonts, SVG rendering, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, or WASM portability. On a miss, it computes the old value first; on a hit, it returns that previously computed value for the same slot, size, and text within the same render.
- Behavior/performance proof: the fresh pre-cache profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0012Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 294.453 ms p95 with `layout` at 223.739 ms p95. The earlier single-token-only focused run was noisy/slower at 302.652 ms p95 and is superseded by the width-cache proof. The accepted focused 10-iteration after run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-width-cache-after-20260707T0022Z/` reports `pdf-large` p95 155.151 ms and mean 152.663 ms, with `layout` p95 79.993 ms. Its `golden/pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 is still `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, exactly matching the fresh pre-cache profile.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `SapphireCrane`; exclusive reservations for `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `src/pdf.rs`, and the relevant perf artifact directories; read-only peer recommendation from `Helmholtz` to add a render-local shaped-width cache; `ubs --diff --only=rust --format=jsonl --ci --skip-size-check`; targeted `ubs --files=src/pdf.rs --only=rust --format=text --ci --skip-size-check .`; `bash -n` over changed shell scripts; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test pdf_word_measurement --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_paragraph_builder_presizes_maps_from_token_count --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test script_sources_test -- --nocapture`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.

## Fresh-Eyes Peer-Code Review - Parser Reference Table Boundary Scan
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T00:43:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-local-table-after-20260707T0031Z/`.
- Review scope: applied `codebase-audit` and `multi-pass-bug-hunting` to the dirty shared checkout, with emphasis on high-risk peer-written parser/PDF/script surfaces rather than only the newest diff. UBS over the full dirty Rust diff emitted aggregate counts only; targeted text scans of `src/parse/mod.rs` and `src/pdf.rs` produced actionable output but the apparent criticals were triaged as false positives or test-only inventory. The `src/parse/mod.rs` "JWT" hit is a parser entity-decoder test named `valid_references_still_decode`, the `src/pdf.rs` "secret comparison" hit is a public PNG signature check, and the shown unwrap/panic hits are test assertions.
- Current profile context: fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z` ranked `pdf-large` first at 153.302 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 23.235 ms p95, `html-large` third at 12.937 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.365 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.990 ms p95. In `parser-large`, `reference_collection` remained a visible parser cost with p95 4.520 ms in the three-iteration fresh profile.
- Root cause fixed: reference-definition stripping still precomputed a full `table_end_boundaries(lines)` vector whenever any reference definition line was consumed. That helper tried every possible table start in the document to support one rare semantic case: preserving a blank line when a consumed reference-definition run separates adjacent table-like regions. On large documents with definitions, this added avoidable whole-document table probing to both normal parsing and spanned parsing.
- Parser change: replaced the eager global table-boundary sweep with a local `table_ends_at(lines, idx)` check that runs only on the first line of a consumed reference-definition run. The local check scans backward over the contiguous pipe-row region before the consumed run and tests each plausible table start with the same `table_extent` logic, so it preserves the table-boundary behavior without allocating or scanning unrelated document regions. `collect_top_level_spans` and `strip_consumed_references` now share this local check.
- Regression target: `local_table_end_detection_tolerates_prior_non_table_pipe_text` pins the important edge case where non-table pipe text precedes a real table, ensuring the local backward scan still finds the actual table start and does not confuse earlier pipe text with table structure. Existing `a_definition_between_adjacent_tables_preserves_the_table_boundary`, parser conformance, and span tests cover the user-visible behavior.
- First-principles proof: reference labels, title parsing, nested reference collection, paragraph-boundary semantics, table parsing, spanned source offsets, inline parsing, renderer output, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change removes an eager auxiliary allocation and broad scan; on the only branch that needs table-boundary knowledge, it asks the same table recognizer whether a table ends exactly at the consumed-run boundary.
- Behavior/performance proof: focused 10-iteration `parser-large` after-run reports p95 22.486 ms and mean 22.373 ms, with `reference_collection` p95 3.871 ms. The before/after samples are not directly identical in iteration count, so this is recorded as a focused directional improvement rather than a broad latency claim. The pre-change and post-change `parser-large.html` SHA-256 values are both `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`, and `sha256sum -c tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-local-table-after-20260707T0031Z/SHA256SUMS` validated the output and stage artifact.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `SapphireCrane`; exclusive reservations for `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and the two parser perf artifact directories; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z`; focused `release-perf` `fmd_perf_harness --scenario parser-large --iters 10`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test local_table_end_detection_tolerates_prior_non_table_pipe_text --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test a_definition_between_adjacent_tables_preserves_the_table_boundary --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_parser_matches_normal_ast_and_reports_required_stages --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --lib refdef_paragraph_tests -- --nocapture`; targeted UBS scans for `src/parse/mod.rs` and `src/pdf.rs`; Bash syntax check over changed shell scripts; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs .skill-loop-progress.md tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-local-table-after-20260707T0031Z`.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Pattern `href` Inheritance
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T01:13:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0109Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase.pdf`.
- Current profile context: fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0109Z` ranks `pdf-large` first at 148.346 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 21.883 ms, `html-large` at 12.614 ms, `pdf-showcase` at 11.159 ms, and `compress-corpus` at 4.994 ms. PDF stage evidence now shows `layout` at 83.725 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 35.054 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.830 ms p95, and page-stream compression at roughly 18.782 ms per render by total stage time. This pass advances the SVG/PDF renderer fidelity requirement rather than claiming a speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. The renderer already supported vector pattern tiling and gradient `href` inheritance, but generated SVGs commonly factor pattern geometry and tile content through `<pattern href="#base">` / `xlink:href`. Supporting that model reuses the existing dependency-free tiler and closes a common paint-server gap without adding external dependencies.
- Root cause fixed: `parse_svg_pattern_paints` parsed only direct, non-self-closing `<pattern>` elements that themselves declared `patternUnits="userSpaceOnUse"`, dimensions, and child geometry. A derived pattern such as `<pattern id="derived" href="#base" x="3"/>` therefore failed to inherit the base pattern's dimensions/body and could render as an unresolved solid fallback or disappear even though the base geometry was otherwise fully supported.
- Renderer change: added bounded pattern-definition collection and resolution, mirroring the existing gradient inheritance approach. Pattern definitions now resolve `href` / `xlink:href` chains up to a fixed depth, inherit missing attributes from the referenced pattern, inherit the referenced body only when the derived pattern has no child content, preserve first-definition-wins ordering, and then feed the resolved pattern into the existing vector child parser and tiler.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_patterns_inherit_attrs_and_body_via_href` pins `xlink:href` inheritance of base geometry/body, derived attribute overrides, and the case where a derived pattern supplies its own child body while keeping inherited geometry. The broader `pdf_svg` suite now includes 78 SVG/PDF tests covering patterns, gradients, masks, markers, text, CSS, transforms, opacity, and image handling.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase.pdf` with `SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH=1700000000`, copied it to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase.pdf`, rasterized pages 3-4 with Ghostscript, and visually inspected `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase-page-01.png` and `showcase-page-02.png`. The frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank and readable, with vector-looking colored boxes, routed arrows, the dashed edge, and legible labels; the following page still shows visible Rust/Python/JSON/shell syntax highlighting.
- Isomorphism proof: SVGs without pattern `href` still take the same direct pattern parse/draw path; unresolved or unsupported patterns still fail closed through existing fallback behavior; derived patterns only reuse attributes/body that SVG paint servers define as inherited through references; pattern tiling, child geometry parsing, CSS matching, PDF operators, floating-point formatting, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability remain on existing code paths.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `OliveDesert`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and the fresh profile artifact; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0109Z`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_patterns_inherit_attrs_and_body_via_href --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`; showcase PDF render plus Ghostscript rasterization and visual inspection; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo check --no-default-features`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG pattern paint-server gap while keeping the renderer dependency-free and visually verified against the real frankenmermaid showcase. The active goal remains open because broader world-class SVG coverage and continued profile-driven optimization are still larger than this focused pass.

- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. Source tracing and Beauvoir's read-only sidecar review both identified append-style page-content emission as a low-risk continuation target. The hottest text operator path still used `write!(..., "{:.2}")` three times per visible segment for font size and text matrix coordinates, even though the surrounding PDF writer already has append-only decimal and glyph writers.
- Renderer change: added a fixed-width append helper for the text segment operator and changed `append_text_segment_operator` to write size/x/y tokens directly into the existing page-content buffer. The helper preserves Rust formatter behavior, including signed zero, non-finite coercion, and decimal half-rounding edge cases, by falling back to the formatter only on near-half scaled values.
- Rejected intermediate: an earlier broader conversion routed the general `pdf_fixed2`/`pdf_fixed3` wrappers through the new helper. The comparable gauntlet caught a one-byte `pdf-showcase` drift: a decompressed text matrix changed `500.12` to `500.13`. That was rejected, narrowed back to the hot text-operator path, and covered with a half-rounding regression sweep before final proof.
- Regression targets: `streamed_text_segment_operator_matches_legacy_format_shape` keeps the emitted `BT /F... Tf ... Tm ... TJ ET` operator byte-identical for a kerning-sensitive fixture. `fixed_width_pdf_token_writers_preserve_finite_format_and_guard_non_finite` now also compares the append writer against Rust formatting over deterministic half-step values for both two- and three-decimal fixed tokens.
- Clippy cleanup: explicit Rust 1.95 verification surfaced unrelated clippy lints in existing SVG/text code (`collapsible_match`, `nonminimal_bool`, and `manual_range_contains`). The mechanical rewrites in `src/pdf.rs` and `src/text.rs` keep the same branch predicates while making the verification gate clean under the working toolchain.
- First-principles proof: glyph shaping, subset glyph maps, kerning adjustment math, font selection, fill-color state, segment order, annotation rectangles, structure marks, page ordering, compression, PDF object numbering, file IDs, SVG geometry, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted hot-path change only replaces repeated formatter dispatch with a formatter-compatible append helper for the same three numeric tokens.
- Behavior/performance proof: final comparable gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/postpush-fixed2-compatible-gauntlet-20260707T013122Z` validates every golden checksum. `pdf-large.pdf` remains SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, and `pdf-showcase.pdf` remains SHA-256 `02a709799164c3c76ffa1d957a9bd7b3f133e9c72944d6b367c437fa9b8f16d8`, both exactly matching the pre-change bundle. The final `pdf-large` p95 is 144.043 ms versus 146.391 ms before, which is inside the 3% whole-scenario noise envelope; the targeted `page_content_stream_generation` stage improved from 35.663 ms p95 to 28.825 ms p95.
- Toolchain note: the repo's `nightly` override temporarily reported `cargo` as not applicable, so final verification used `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu`, the installed working toolchain that successfully ran the same Rust gates and perf harness.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `RainyJaguar`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `src/text.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and the relevant perf artifact directories; Beauvoir sidecar read-only review; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id postpush-current-profile-20260707T013122Z`; focused `release-perf` `fmd_perf_harness --scenario pdf-showcase --iters 1 --out-dir tests/artifacts/perf/postpush-fixed2-compat-showcase-20260707T013122Z/golden`; final `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id postpush-fixed2-compatible-gauntlet-20260707T013122Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` in both final bundle `golden/` directories; explicit `sha256sum` comparison for pre/post `pdf-large.pdf` and `pdf-showcase.pdf`; `scripts/perf-compare.sh tests/artifacts/perf/postpush-current-profile-20260707T013122Z tests/artifacts/perf/postpush-fixed2-compatible-gauntlet-20260707T013122Z`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo fmt --check`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo check --all-targets`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs src/text.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.

The active broader performance/SVG goal remains open because `pdf-large` remains the top p95 hotspot and the renderer still has more SVG/PDF surface area to harden.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Layout Cache Trial Rejections
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T02:22:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. Two `src/pdf.rs` optimization trials were implemented, tested, measured, and fully reverted because both were performance-negative despite preserving PDF bytes.
- Current profile context: the fresh `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0202Z/` bundle ranks `pdf-large` first at 143.966 ms p95, with PDF `layout` at 83.738 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 28.629 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.473 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 260.252 us p95 per stream. `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 is `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Rejected trial 1: changed `build_segs_adjusted` to measure growing same-style line segment prefixes exactly without inserting those prefixes into the render-local width cache. Hypothesis: prefix strings are mostly unique and cache insertion is overhead. Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the 10-iteration baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-segbuild-baseline-20260707T0222Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 142.595 ms and layout p95 84.037 ms, while the post-change artifact `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-segbuild-after-20260707T0222Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 258.408 ms and layout p95 192.092 ms. Both artifacts kept `pdf-large.pdf` byte-identical at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, proving the rejection is performance-only. Conclusion: the growing-prefix width cache is materially useful for this corpus and must not be bypassed casually.
- Rejected trial 2: replaced the raw nested `WidthCache` map with a private struct that tracked total entry count in O(1), avoiding the old `cache.values().map(HashMap::len).sum()` on cache misses. Hypothesis: cache-size recounting was hot bookkeeping. Evidence did not support keeping it: the same baseline reported `pdf-large` p95 142.595 ms and layout p95 84.037 ms, while `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-widthcache-after-20260707T0222Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 144.566 ms and layout p95 88.033 ms. The output hash again stayed byte-identical at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. Conclusion: this bookkeeping change is inside the variance/noise envelope at best and slightly negative in the focused run; leave the simpler existing map shape in place.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `WildHill`; released stale self-reservations from `BlackCove`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-segbuild-*`; focused baseline and two focused `release-perf` post-change runs; focused PDF writer tests during each trial; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo fmt --check`; final `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` is empty after reverting both rejected trials.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS; no production code should be committed from these two attempts. The useful outcome is a negative hypothesis ledger that prevents future agents from repeating two tempting but harmful PDF layout/cache edits. The active goal remains open; next useful optimization work should target layout with deeper attribution than cache-shape guessing, or move to a different measured top-five surface.

## Active Goal Continuation - DEFLATE Match Symbol Lookup Tables
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T02:35:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf artifacts under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-*` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0202Z/` bundle ranks `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.034 ms p95 and shows PDF `page_stream_compression` at 260.252 us p95 per page stream, with 252 page streams over the three-iteration profile. This is below the dominant PDF layout work but is a clean low-hanging path shared by PDF page streams, embedded font streams, PNG fixture generation, and standalone compression users.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing showed every emitted LZ77 match searched the static DEFLATE length and distance base tables with reverse linear scans, even though the mapping from legal match length 3..=258 and distance 1..=32768 to RFC 1951 symbols is immutable.
- Compressor change: added compile-time lookup generation for match length symbols and a 32 KiB static distance-symbol table, then changed `emit_match` to index those tables instead of searching `LENGTH_BASE` and `DIST_BASE` for every match. The existing base and extra-bit tables remain the source of truth for emitted extra-bit payloads and for inflater decoding. No dependency, unsafe code, global mutable state, threading, filesystem, process, or native-runtime assumption was introduced.
- Regression target: `match_symbol_tables_preserve_search_mapping` exhaustively compares the new length and distance tables against the old highest-base-less-than-or-equal search for every legal value. The existing roundtrip sweeps still cover empty, text, binary, stored fallback, max-length matches, self-overlap, window-edge distances, and production inflater paths.
- First-principles proof: LZ77 match finding, literal emission, Huffman code tables, extra-bit values, stored-block fallback, zlib headers, Adler-32, decompression, PDF object ordering, page-content bytes before compression, font subsetting, SVG/image paths, parser behavior, HTML output, WASM portability, and deterministic output policy are unchanged. The accepted change only replaces a pure symbol-selection search with a table generated by the same search at compile time.
- Behavior/performance proof: the focused baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-baseline-20260707T0235Z/` reported `compress-corpus` p95 6.083 ms and mean 5.159 ms over 20 iterations, with output size 107098 B. The exact final-source longer sample `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-final100-20260707T0235Z/` reported p95 5.029 ms and mean 4.806 ms over 100 iterations, with the same output size, and `compress-corpus.lengths` is byte-identical to the baseline. A 20-iteration final-source sample had one high p95 outlier at 6.258 ms despite mean 5.020 ms, so the retained claim is based on the longer sample plus downstream PDF evidence rather than that noisy p95.
- PDF proof: the focused `pdf-large` baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-pdfbaseline-20260707T0235Z/` reported p95 141.320 ms and mean 140.256 ms over five iterations. The exact final-source `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-pdffinal-20260707T0235Z/` reported p95 137.765 ms and mean 135.988 ms over five iterations. `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`; `page_stream_compression` p95 moved from 274.088 us to 256.144 us and `font_stream_compression` p95 from 123.764 us to 68.960 us in the focused stage ledgers.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `WildHill`; exclusive reservations for `src/compress.rs`, `tests/*compress*`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-*`; focused baseline and final `release-perf` runs for `compress-corpus` and `pdf-large`; direct `sha256sum` comparison for pre/post `pdf-large.pdf`; direct diff of pre/post `compress-corpus.lengths`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo fmt --check`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo test compress::tests --lib`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo check --all-targets`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a byte-preserving, dependency-free compressor hot-path cleanup with exhaustive symbol-mapping coverage and measurable benefit in both standalone compression and PDF stream serialization. The active broader goal remains open because PDF layout is still the dominant measured hotspot and the requested SVG/mermaid renderer scope extends beyond this compression pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Object-Bounding-Box Clip And Mask Units
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T03:12:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the previous fresh broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0245Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` first at 143.455 ms p95 and shows SVG/PDF fidelity as a parallel project goal rather than the dominant CPU hotspot. This pass intentionally targets a correctness gap in the dependency-free SVG renderer: generated SVGs and authoring tools commonly use `clipPathUnits="objectBoundingBox"` and `maskContentUnits="objectBoundingBox"`.
- Root cause fixed: parsed clip paths and supported hard-mask geometry stored only raw path operations plus fill rule. At draw time every clip/mask path was emitted as user-space geometry, so object-bounding-box definitions stayed in 0..1 coordinates instead of being scaled and translated into the target element's bbox. That made common normalized masks/clips either invisible or far too small.
- Renderer change: added explicit unit metadata to parsed `SvgClipPath` definitions, parsing `clipPathUnits` for clip paths and `maskContentUnits` for masks with SVG-correct user-space defaults. Shape, embedded-image, and selectable-text clipping now pass target bboxes into a shared applicability/emission helper. User-space clips remain allocation-free; object-bounding-box clips clone and transform only the small referenced clip path, and degenerate target bboxes fail closed instead of emitting malformed PDF geometry.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_object_bounding_box_clip_and_mask_units_scale_to_target_geometry` pins exact PDF clipping geometry for normalized clip and mask definitions scaled onto rectangle targets. Existing user-space clip, mask, and transformed child clip tests were rerun to prove the old behavior stayed intact.
- First-principles proof: SVG parsing, style inheritance, fill/stroke paint, gradients, patterns, marker rendering, image embedding, selectable text emission, PDF object numbering, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change only alters the coordinate transform applied to already-supported clip/mask geometry when an SVG definition explicitly requests object-bounding-box content units.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `QuietBarn`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo test pdf_svg_object_bounding_box_clip_and_mask_units_scale_to_target_geometry -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_clip -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_masks -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG/PDF fidelity gap without adding dependencies or changing the fast user-space clip path. The active broader goal remains open because there are still larger SVG feature and PDF-layout performance surfaces beyond this focused pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Highlighter Dispatch Shortcut
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T03:22:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf artifacts under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T031157Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-highlight-dispatch-after-20260707T031641Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-highlight-dispatch-profile-20260707T031651Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-highlight-dispatch-showcase-20260707T031651Z/` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.

The public highlighter already returns one plain span for unknown languages, so the precheck was redundant for rendered output.

Unknown language behavior remains plain escaped text because `highlight` falls back to one `Tok::Plain` span over the full code block.

Direct checksums for `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, and `html-showcase.html` match the pre-change `continue-current-profile-20260707T031157Z` golden artifacts. The broad after-run reports `html-code-heavy` p95 2.760 ms versus 3.618 ms before; the focused 20-iteration after-run reports `html-code-heavy` p95 3.145 ms and byte-identical output. `html-large` moved only 2.0% in the broad p95 comparison, so this pass claims a targeted highlighted-code improvement rather than a material full-HTML-render speedup.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Plain Multiline Paragraph Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T03:47:24Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf bundles under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-multiline-*` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the current-main profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T032710Z/` ranked `parser-large` second at 23.460 ms p95, and parser stage attribution showed `inline_parse` at 4.158 us p95 per invocation with `paragraph_block` at 8.466 us p95. That made paragraph inline handoff a plausible lower-risk target after the recent PDF layout cache trials were rejected.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. Source tracing showed multi-line paragraphs always materialized a `Vec<char>` and entered the full inline parser solely to turn `\n` into soft/hard break inline nodes, even when each component line was otherwise plain text. The existing single-line `plain_inline_fast_path` already proved the syntax-free case can skip delimiter/link parsing.
- Parser change: `parse_lines_as_inlines` now detects multi-line paragraphs whose component lines individually need no full inline parse, then emits the exact `Inline::Text`, `Inline::SoftBreak`, and trailing-two-space `Inline::HardBreak` sequence directly. It preserves full parser fallback for any line containing inline syntax, escapes, links, bare URLs/emails, entities, HTML/autolinks, code spans, emphasis, strike, or images. Non-final line trailing spaces are stripped exactly like the existing newline branch in the full parser; the final line is preserved.
- Regression targets: `plain_multiline_paragraph_preserves_soft_and_hard_breaks` pins soft-break trimming plus two-space hard-break behavior. `multiline_paragraph_with_inline_syntax_uses_full_inline_parser` pins that mixed paragraphs still resolve emphasis after a soft break. The pre-existing `multiline_paragraph_inline_handoff_preserves_soft_breaks_and_references` fixture was rerun as an additional guard.
- Behavior/performance proof: the focused after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-multiline-plain-after2-20260707T0340Z/` reported `parser-large` p95 19.550 ms and mean 19.170 ms over 50 iterations, with `parser-large.html` byte-identical to the current-main profile (`951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`). To control for current host drift, a detached clean-HEAD worktree at `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_baseline_20260707T0340Z` rebuilt the old source and reported `parser-large` p95 23.407 ms and mean 22.894 ms over 50 iterations. The same clean-HEAD cross-check showed `html-large` p95 16.835 ms versus current-source p95 15.394 ms, confirming the earlier 3-iteration broad HTML p95 noise was not caused by this parser change.
- Broad profile proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-parser-multiline-plain-profile-20260707T0340Z` completed, validated all golden checksums, kept `pdf-large` as the top p95 hotspot, and reported `parser-large` p95 22.551 ms versus 23.460 ms in the current-main bundle. `scripts/perf-compare.sh` flagged unrelated 3-sample p95 noise in pre-parsed HTML/PDF showcase scenarios; the focused clean-HEAD cross-check above is the stronger attribution evidence for this one-lever parser change.
- First-principles proof: block parsing, reference collection, table/list/blockquote logic, inline syntax semantics, HTML/PDF renderers, SVG/Mermaid paths, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, filesystem behavior, WASM portability, and deterministic output policy are unchanged. The accepted change only replaces a pure syntax-free multi-line paragraph tokenization path with direct construction of the same inline nodes.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Font Usage ASCII Bitset
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T04:02:50Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf bundles under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-font-bitset-*` and the detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_html_bitset_baseline_20260707T0357Z` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-multiline-plain-profile-20260707T0340Z/` ranks `html-large` third overall at 15.459 ms p95, behind `pdf-large` and `parser-large`. Recent PDF table-width cache and parser reference-candidate trials were rejected by measurement, making the pre-parsed HTML/font path a lower-risk top-five target for this pass.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. Source tracing showed HTML font usage collection stored the ASCII subset as `[bool; 128]` plus a separate `has_ascii` flag. Large documents repeatedly OR character membership into that array before every HTML font subset. A compact bitset should reduce per-slot state size and write traffic while preserving the same deterministic ASCII-before-non-ASCII character ordering.
- Renderer change: `FontCharSet` now stores ASCII membership as a `u128` mask and keeps non-ASCII membership in the existing `BTreeSet<char>`. ASCII text extends a local mask and ORs it into the slot once; `to_chars` emits set ASCII bits in ascending byte order, then extends with the ordered non-ASCII set exactly as before.
- First-principles proof: font slot selection, seed characters, non-ASCII ordering, `@font-face` emission, TrueType parsing/subsetting, base64 encoding, HTML body rendering, syntax highlighting, PDF output, SVG/Mermaid paths, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, filesystem behavior, and WASM portability are unchanged. This changes only the internal set representation used to compute the same per-slot keep-character lists.
- Behavior proof: clean-baseline `html-large.html` and trial `html-large.html` both have SHA-256 `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`; clean-baseline `html-code-heavy.html` and trial `html-code-heavy.html` both have SHA-256 `e7ac126b62e87ea39051f2eee4f1d5031fd2f998bec3a115d951843e54544b40`. Direct `cmp -s` checks reported `html-large-identical` and `html-code-heavy-identical`.
- Performance proof: initial current-source `html-large` baseline over 50 iterations reported p95 15.805 ms and mean 14.700 ms. The first trial run over 50 iterations was flat/slightly worse at p95 15.851 ms and mean 14.828 ms, so a stronger clean-baseline comparison was taken. A detached clean `HEAD` worktree at `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_html_bitset_baseline_20260707T0357Z` reported `html-large` p95 15.335 ms and mean 14.465 ms over 100 iterations; the trial reported p95 14.942 ms and mean 13.871 ms over 100 iterations. `html-code-heavy` clean baseline reported p95 2.507 ms and mean 2.413 ms; the trial reported p95 2.440 ms and mean 2.417 ms. This is accepted as a byte-preserving directional cleanup, not a major latency claim because the p95 movement is below the 10% variance threshold.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `QuietBarn`; exclusive reservations for `src/html.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-font-bitset-*`; focused current and clean-baseline release-perf harness runs; direct SHA-256 and `cmp -s` output comparisons; `cargo test --lib html::tests::font_char_set_keeps_btree_character_order -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --lib html::tests -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test smoke_test default_html_embeds_deterministic_subset_font_faces -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test highlight_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; full `cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes small but avoidable ASCII set memory traffic from the top-five pre-parsed HTML path while keeping generated HTML bytes identical. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` remains the top measured hotspot and the requested dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer scope remains broader than this internal HTML cleanup.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Marker Child Paint Order
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T04:32:27Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0428Z/` and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-marker-paint-order-visual-20260707T0435Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0428Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 147.863 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 21.917 ms, `html-large` third at 15.692 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.145 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 7.588 ms. PDF stage attribution keeps `layout` first at 85.147 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 29.767 ms p95, `page_stream_compression` at 261 us per stream, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.589 ms p95. The bundle's golden checksums all validated.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. A parser reference-candidate shortcut was explicitly avoided because the ledger already records that carried-flag variant as a rejected performance trial. This pass instead targets the active SVG renderer objective with a small correctness gap: outer line/path/poly marker layers honored `paint-order`, but child shapes inside a referenced `<marker>` still painted through the legacy combined fill/stroke operator.
- Root cause fixed: `append_svg_marker` resolved marker-context paint and shadow/transform state for each marker child, then always called `append_svg_style`, `append_svg_path_ops`, and `append_svg_paint_operator`. That path ignores `SvgStyle.paint_order`, so a marker child such as `<path fill=... stroke=... paint-order="stroke fill">` rendered like default fill-then-stroke in PDF even though browser SVG paints stroke before fill.
- Renderer change: marker child rendering now delegates to `append_svg_marker_shape_paint`. The default marker path stays byte/logic equivalent and keeps the compact combined `B`/`B*` operator. Only marker child shapes with non-normal `paint-order` and both fill and stroke expand into ordered fill and stroke layers; the marker-layer token itself is ignored inside marker children because nested markers are not a valid paint layer there.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_paint_order_applies_inside_marker_child_shapes` proves a marker child with `paint-order="stroke fill"` emits the blue stroke layer before the red fill layer, while a sibling marker child without custom paint-order still emits the compact fill+stroke `B` operator.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` through the normal file-input PDF path, relying on automatic sibling SVG loading for `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, then rasterized page 3 via Ghostscript using a `/tmp` copy because this Ghostscript build rejects direct `/data/...` reads under `-dSAFER`. Visual inspection of `page-03.png` shows the frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank, centered, colorful, and readable; node labels, routed arrows, arrowheads, the dashed Mermaid edge into `PDF`, the Mermaid source block, and the following `Blockquotes` section all remain visible. Artifact hashes: `showcase.pdf` SHA-256 `946f220cf76d725ca8d40f22cef78b5efdf305714406416fea39d2688fc06015`; `page-03.png` SHA-256 `739fc2e3b8cf955587042f5f1b877fb23f2641cf64a55187133c9bc8202176ba`.
- First-principles proof: the change is restricted to painting marker child paths after marker placement, viewBox, markerUnits, orient, context-paint, shadows, and graphics-state prefixing have already been resolved. Default marker children still use the same compact paint operator, so ordinary frankenmermaid marker output and normal shape rendering are unchanged. SVG parsing, marker placement/orientation, line/path/poly outer paint-order, gradients, patterns, masks/clips, PDF object numbering, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `QuietBarn`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0428Z/**`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-marker-paint-order-*`, and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-marker-paint-order-visual-20260707T0435Z/**`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0428Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the profile bundle's `golden/` directory; `cargo test pdf_svg_paint_order --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_marker --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; showcase PDF render; Ghostscript page-3 rasterization; visual inspection; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete paint-order fidelity gap in the dependency-free SVG-to-PDF marker renderer without changing the compact default path. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout remains the dominant measured hotspot and the requested world-class SVG/Mermaid surface is still broader than this focused pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Markers On Unstroked Referencing Shapes
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T04:58:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T044336Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-unstroked-marker-after-20260707T0449Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-unstroked-marker-visual-20260707T0452Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T044336Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 149.585 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 24.757 ms, `html-large` third at 16.467 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.142 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.783 ms. PDF stage attribution kept `layout` first at 85.790 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 29.185 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.892 ms p95, and page-stream compression at 260 us per stream. The bundle's golden checksums all validated.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. This pass intentionally targets the active dependency-free SVG renderer objective rather than forcing another small scalar optimization into the already noisy top-five profile. Source tracing found a concrete SVG fidelity gap in marker placement: explicit marker shapes disappeared when the referencing line/path/polyline had no stroke.
- Root cause fixed: `draw_svg_line` returned immediately when `line.style.stroke` was `None`, and the path/poly marker emission lived under `if let Some(stroke) = style.stroke`. That made `marker-start`, `marker-mid`, and `marker-end` depend on the referencing element's own stroke paint even when the referenced marker child had explicit fill/stroke paint. It also meant marker `context-stroke` could not accurately represent the absence of a referencing stroke because `SvgMarkerPaint` stored stroke as a mandatory color.
- Renderer change: marker placement is now gated by marker references plus child paint, not by the referencing element's stroke. `SvgMarkerPaint.stroke` is optional, line/path/poly renderers can emit marker-only geometry, and the generic fallback arrowhead only appears when a real referencing stroke color exists. Marker `context-stroke` now resolves to `None` for unstroked shapes instead of inventing black, while explicit marker fills and `context-fill` still render.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_markers_render_on_unstroked_referencing_shapes_when_marker_has_own_paint` covers an unstroked line, unstroked path, unstroked polyline with mid/end markers, a fill-only polygon using `context-fill`, and an unstroked line using `context-stroke`. The test pins four explicit green marker placements, proves fill-only context paint reaches marker children, and proves missing context-stroke does not emit a synthetic black marker.
- Behavior proof: the focused new regression passed; all existing SVG marker tests passed; all paint-order tests passed; and the full PDF SVG suite passed with 83 matching SVG-focused tests. The comparable after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-unstroked-marker-after-20260707T0449Z/` validated every golden checksum. Direct pre/post hashes for representative golden outputs stayed byte-identical: `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, and `html-large.html` SHA-256 `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` through the normal file-input PDF path, relying on automatic sibling SVG loading for `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, then rasterized page 3 with Ghostscript from a `/tmp` PDF copy. Visual inspection of `page-03.png` showed the frankenmermaid diagram was nonblank, centered, colorful, and readable; labels, routed arrows, arrowheads, dashed edge, Mermaid source block, and the following `Blockquotes` section were visible without overlap. Artifact hashes: `showcase.pdf` SHA-256 `946f220cf76d725ca8d40f22cef78b5efdf305714406416fea39d2688fc06015`; `page-03.png` SHA-256 `739fc2e3b8cf955587042f5f1b877fb23f2641cf64a55187133c9bc8202176ba`.
- First-principles proof: SVG parsing, marker lookup, marker orientation, viewBox scaling, markerUnits scaling, marker child `paint-order`, line/path/poly outer paint-order, shadows, gradients, patterns, clips/masks, PDF object numbering, compression, HTML output, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change only lets already-supported marker placement proceed when the referencing geometry has no stroke and preserves absence of context-stroke as absence rather than as a fallback color.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `CopperIvy`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T044336Z/**`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-unstroked-marker-*`, and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-unstroked-marker-visual-*`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T044336Z`; `cargo fmt`; focused new regression; `cargo test pdf_svg_marker --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_paint_order --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; after-change perf gauntlet and `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt`; direct pre/post golden SHA-256 comparisons; showcase PDF render; Ghostscript page-3 rasterization; visual inspection; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a real marker fidelity defect in the dependency-free SVG-to-PDF renderer without adding dependencies or changing existing golden outputs. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout is still the dominant measured hotspot and the requested world-class SVG/Mermaid scope is larger than this focused marker pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Bare Autolink Probe Gate
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T05:18:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T045851Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-autolink-gate-baseline-20260707T0503Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-autolink-gate-after2-20260707T0503Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-autolink-gate-profile2-20260707T0503Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted. Detached clean-HEAD baseline worktree `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_inline_autolink_baseline_20260707T0503Z` is also evidence only.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T045851Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 141.882 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 23.043 ms, `html-large` third at 16.176 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.147 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.089 ms. Parser stage attribution showed `inline_parse` at 34.221 ms total over three profiled iterations, with p95 2986 ns per inline parse, and `paragraph_block` at 31.981 ms total.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. This pass targets a parser hot path outside the recent PDF/SVG work. Source tracing showed the full inline parser tried `parse_bare_url_autolink` and `parse_bare_email_autolink` in the ordinary-character branch for every character, even when the current character could not begin any supported bare URL or email and when the run contained no `@` at all.
- Parser change: the full inline parser now gates bare URL probing to positions that start the supported lowercase `http://`, `https://`, or `www.` prefixes. Bare email probing is skipped entirely unless the inline run contains `@`, and even then is tried only at characters that the existing email parser already accepts as a local-part start (`[A-Za-z0-9._+-]`). The parsers themselves still perform the authoritative boundary and full-address validation, so the new checks are conservative prefilters rather than new syntax rules.
- Refined implementation note: an earlier local version used one broader pre-scan for all bare-autolink candidates. After measurement and source tracing, that was narrowed before commit so URL probing is position-gated and only the cheap email `@` presence check remains global. This avoids paying a whole-run URL prefix scan on short syntax-bearing inline runs.
- Regression target: `bare_autolink_candidate_gate_matches_supported_bare_forms` pins the URL-start and email-local prefilter predicates. Existing public parser conformance fixtures for bare URLs, bare emails, and the profiled plain-inline fast path were rerun to prove supported links still render and non-boundary/autolink-conservative cases remain text.
- Behavior/performance proof: a detached clean-HEAD baseline at `2b0ece6` reported focused `parser-large` p95 20.405 ms and mean 19.854 ms over 50 iterations. The refined current source reported p95 19.835 ms and mean 18.996 ms over the same 50-iteration scenario, with byte-identical `parser-large.html` SHA-256 `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`. Stage attribution shows the intended local effect: `inline_parse` p95 moved from 3046 ns to 2565 ns, while parser output remained identical. The broader three-iteration after-run validated every golden checksum and kept `parser-large.html` and `pdf-large.pdf` byte-identical to the pre-change profile; its `parser-large` p95 moved from 23.043 ms to 21.153 ms. The broad compare also flagged `html-code-heavy` noise, but harness tracing confirmed that scenario parses before timing and measures only pre-parsed HTML rendering, so it is not attributable to this parser-only edit.
- First-principles proof: Markdown block parsing, reference collection, bracket matching, URL/email syntax validation, left-boundary rules, trailing punctuation trimming, entity decoding, emphasis resolution, HTML/PDF rendering, SVG/Mermaid paths, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, filesystem behavior, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change only skips bare-autolink parser calls at positions where those same parsers would immediately return `None`.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `CopperIvy`; exclusive reservations for `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T045851Z/**`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-autolink-gate-*`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T045851Z`; focused behavior tests for the new predicate, GFM bare URLs, bare emails, and the profiled plain-inline fast path; release-perf focused clean-baseline/current parser samples; direct SHA-256 and `cmp -s` comparisons for focused `parser-large.html`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-inline-autolink-gate-profile2-20260707T0503Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from that after-run golden directory; `scripts/perf-compare.sh` on pre/post broad profiles; direct pre/post SHA-256 comparisons for `parser-large.html` and `pdf-large.pdf`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`.

## Active Goal Continuation - Compressor Match-Length Chunk Prefix
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T05:49:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T054254Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchlen-baseline-20260707T054439Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchlen-after-20260707T054612Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchlen-pdfafter-20260707T054728Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.

PDF stage attribution showed `page_stream_compression` at 262.244 us p95 across 252 page streams, with `page_content_stream_generation` and `pdf_object_serialization_total` still ahead of it.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. The compressor remains a top-five standalone scenario and also feeds PDF page/font streams. Source tracing showed `match_len` still compared every candidate byte-by-byte even when long LZ77 matches share whole aligned prefixes.
- Compressor change: `match_len` now advances over matching 8-byte slice chunks before falling back to the original byte-by-byte scalar tail. If a chunk differs, the fallback resumes from the same offset rather than after the chunk, so it still reports the exact first mismatch position. A focused regression pins mismatches inside the first chunk, immediately after two full chunks, and in a short scalar tail.
- First-principles proof: LZ77 candidate order, best-match strict-greater tie-breaking, match length results, literal/match emission, fixed-Huffman symbol selection, stored-block fallback, zlib header/trailer bytes, Adler-32, decompression, PDF object ordering, HTML/parser/SVG paths, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change only reduces the work needed to prove equal prefixes inside the existing match-length oracle.
- Behavior/performance proof: focused 50-iteration baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchlen-baseline-20260707T054439Z.jsonl` reported `compress-corpus` p95 5.616 ms and mean 5.001 ms, with `compress-corpus.lengths` SHA-256 `25fb004e36ad26dd0d8031152d3aa49dde799fe852d8fcae8fd5806d479e2e65`. The after run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchlen-after-20260707T054612Z.jsonl` reported p95 4.849 ms and mean 4.528 ms over the same 50-iteration scenario, and its `compress-corpus.lengths` file is byte-identical with the same SHA-256. Downstream `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical to the fresh pre-change profile at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`; the focused PDF after run reported `page_stream_compression` p95 247.828 us.

- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a byte-preserving, dependency-free compressor hot-path cleanup with focused p95/mean improvement and downstream PDF byte proof. ## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Table Token Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T06:09:25Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T055815Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-table-token-reuse-after-20260707T060159Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-table-token-reuse-ab-20260707T060336Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted. - Current profile context: fresh broad profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T055815Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 138.730 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 21.402 ms, `html-large` third at 12.911 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.014 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.860 ms. PDF stage attribution kept `layout` first at 78.495 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 28.804 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.078 ms p95.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Table-heavy PDFs are part of the dominant layout stage and remain directly relevant to the performance-plan table quality work. Source tracing showed table cell inline/style tokenization happened twice per cell: once while computing table min-content, max-content, and wrapping-badness metrics, then again while wrapping and emitting physical row lines.
- PDF layout change: `layout_table` now tokenizes header and body cells once into `head_toks` and `row_toks`, then reuses those same styled token vectors for `table_cell_measure` and `wrap_cell_styled`. The row construction closure now accepts token slices instead of rebuilding tokens from `Inline` cells.
- First-principles proof: header bolding, link preservation, strikethrough, code/italic/bold face selection, table width allocation, alignment, zebra striping, table structure tagging, page-break behavior, PDF object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change removes duplicate pure token construction and feeds the existing measurement and wrapping functions the same token stream they already consumed.
- Behavior/performance proof: a focused after-run for `pdf-large` produced a byte-identical PDF to the fresh pre-change profile with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. Broad `pdf-large` p95 stayed effectively flat, so this pass does not claim a meaningful full-document latency win. A same-host table-heavy A/B against detached clean `HEAD` showed the intended local benefit: baseline `fmd table-heavy.md --to pdf` averaged 555.5 ms over 20 runs, current averaged 544.4 ms, Hyperfine reported current as 1.02 +/- 0.01 times faster, and both PDFs were byte-identical with SHA-256 `1ecdd3cf5b56c7bc555c4f50005b653513231c71a38dbedc7cb3947fd648d052`.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration/reservation was attempted but failed with a malformed database error, so no reservation was acquired for this pass. Fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T055815Z`; golden checksum validation for the fresh profile; focused `release-perf` `pdf-large` after-run; direct pre/post PDF `cmp -s` and SHA-256 comparison; detached clean-HEAD table-heavy Hyperfine A/B; `cargo test table_wrap_tests --lib`; `cargo test pdf_table --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a small byte-preserving PDF table layout optimization with a focused table-heavy win and neutral broad-pdf behavior. The active broader goal remains open because larger `pdf-large` layout costs and the full dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer objective still have remaining surface area beyond this focused cleanup.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Shape Cache Single Lookup
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T06:45:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-lowfruit-profile-20260707T063059Z/` and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-shape-cache-after-20260707T063354Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-lowfruit-profile-20260707T063059Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 140.063 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 18.458 ms, `html-large` third at 13.068 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 9.944 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.822 ms. PDF stage attribution kept `layout` first at 81.066 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 33.241 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.584 ms p95, `page_stream_compression` at 260.683 us p95 per stream, and `glyph_collection_and_shaping` at 6.292 ms p95.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Source tracing showed glyph collection used `contains_key` followed by `get` for every shaped segment and SVG text run in the per-render shape cache. Cache hits therefore performed two map lookups before collecting the same glyph and ligature metadata.
- PDF serialization change: glyph collection now uses a single borrowed `get` on cache hits and only shapes/inserts on misses. A small `collect_shaped_run_glyphs` helper centralizes the unchanged copy of shaped glyph ids and ligature ToUnicode source strings.
- First-principles proof: segment ordering, font-slot ordering, cache key text, shape-run construction, glyph seed collection, ligature ToUnicode mapping, subset glyph ordering, PDF object serialization, page content streams, compression, HTML output, parser behavior, SVG/Mermaid rendering, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change only removes a redundant lookup before using the same cached or newly shaped run.
- Behavior/performance proof: focused `pdf-large` after-run over 10 iterations produced a byte-identical PDF to the fresh pre-change profile with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. The target stage moved from `glyph_collection_and_shaping` p95 6.292 ms in the fresh 5-iteration profile to 3.514 ms in the 10-iteration after-run. Whole `pdf-large` p95 stayed within the broader PDF variance envelope at 139.462 ms after versus 140.063 ms before, so this pass claims a local support-stage cleanup rather than a major end-to-end latency win.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `MagentaBrook` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 5 --run-id continue-lowfruit-profile-20260707T063059Z`; focused `release-perf` `pdf-large` after-run; direct pre/post `pdf-large.pdf` `cmp -s` and SHA-256 comparison; stage-summary comparison for `glyph_collection_and_shaping`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a small byte-preserving PDF support-stage cleanup with a clear local stage movement and no dependency or portability cost. The active broader goal remains open because larger `pdf-large` layout/page-content costs and the dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer objective still have remaining surface area beyond this focused cache-lookup cleanup.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Reference Prefilter Split Trial Rejection
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T06:56:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. A `src/parse/mod.rs` trial was implemented, behavior-tested, measured twice, and manually reverted because focused performance evidence rejected keeping it.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T064754Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 133.931 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 17.857 ms, `html-large` third at 12.751 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 9.865 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.870 ms. Parser stage attribution showed `reference_collection` at 17.802 ms total over five profiled iterations with p95 3.605 ms per parse, behind `inline_parse` and `paragraph_block` but still a top non-PDF substage.
- Rejected opportunity: split `reference_collector_needs_block_scan` so ordinary non-`[` lines only scanned for tab/pipe table-indentation triggers, while the `]:` pair check ran only for lines whose first non-indent byte was `[`. Hypothesis: current prose lines pay a useless previous-byte branch for reference-definition detection even though that result can only change behavior for leading-bracket candidates.
- Behavior proof during the rejected trial: `cargo test reference_collector_fast_path_ignores_inline_only_punctuation --lib -- --nocapture` and `cargo test refdef_paragraph_tests --lib -- --nocapture` passed with additional assertions that ordinary prose containing `[text]:` remains paragraph text and a leading bracket without a destination stays on the fast path.
- Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the focused 50-iteration baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-prefilter-baseline-20260707T065132Z.jsonl` reported `parser-large` p95 18.530 ms and mean 18.231 ms. The first after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-prefilter-after-20260707T065310Z.jsonl` reported p95 19.733 ms and mean 18.238 ms. A second clean after-run without rebuild heat, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-prefilter-after2-20260707T065414Z.jsonl`, reported p95 19.878 ms and mean 18.521 ms. Both after-runs were worse on p95 and did not show a meaningful mean improvement.
- First-principles diagnosis: the split removed one previous-byte branch from ordinary prose, but introduced a first-byte branch and a second loop shape that the optimizer/branch predictor did not reward on this corpus. The original single-pass scan is simpler and faster or at least less noisy for the measured parser-large source.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `MagentaBrook` for `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; fresh broad `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 5 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T064754Z`; golden checksum validation for the fresh profile; focused 50-iteration baseline and two after-runs; behavior tests listed above; manual `apply_patch` revert of the trial; final `cargo fmt --check`; final `git diff -- src/parse/mod.rs` is empty.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS; do not split `reference_collector_needs_block_scan` into separate ordinary-line and leading-bracket loop shapes without stronger same-host evidence. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content costs and the world-class dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer scope still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Marked-Content BDC Append Trial Rejection
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T06:59:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. A `src/pdf.rs` trial was implemented, behavior-tested, measured twice, and manually reverted because focused performance evidence rejected keeping it.
- Current profile context: the same fresh current-HEAD profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T064754Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 133.931 ms p95. PDF stage attribution showed `page_content_stream_generation` at 136.837 ms total over five profiled renders with p95 27.645 ms, behind `layout` and ahead of `pdf_object_serialization_total`.
- Rejected opportunity: replace the two hot-loop `format!` calls that emit marked-content begin operators (`/{tag} <</MCID n>> BDC\n`) with an `append_marked_content_begin` helper that pushes the tag and decimal MCID directly into the page stream. Hypothesis: avoiding tiny temporary strings for table cells and normal content lines would reduce page content stream generation without changing PDF bytes.
- Behavior proof during the rejected trial: `cargo test marked_content_begin_appends_the_exact_pdf_operator --lib -- --nocapture`, `cargo test pdf_writer_tests --lib -- --nocapture`, and `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture` passed. Focused `pdf-large` after-runs stayed byte-identical to the fresh baseline PDF at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the first focused 10-iteration after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-bdc-append-after-20260707T065706Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 135.762 ms and mean 134.383 ms. Stage attribution showed `page_content_stream_generation` p95 28.833 ms, worse than the fresh profile's 27.645 ms. A second no-rebuild after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-bdc-append-after2-20260707T065823Z/` reported p95 136.280 ms and mean 135.137 ms. Both after-runs were byte-identical but performance-negative.
- First-principles diagnosis: the helper removed allocation from two BDC sites, but those strings are small relative to surrounding draw operations, segment emission, annotation construction, and compression. The extra helper call and manual decimal append did not move the measured stage and slightly worsened p95 on this corpus.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `MagentaBrook` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused tests listed above; focused 10-iteration PDF after-run plus byte comparison; second no-rebuild after-run plus byte comparison; manual `apply_patch` revert of the trial; final `cargo fmt --check`; final `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` is empty.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS; do not replace the marked-content BDC `format!` calls with a direct append helper unless a stronger profile identifies those exact allocations as material. The active broader goal remains open because larger PDF layout/page-content costs and the world-class dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer scope still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Text Decoration Fidelity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T08:02:20Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-decoration-profile-20260707T0810Z/` and `/tmp/fmd-showcase-svg-decoration*` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: fresh gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-decoration-profile-20260707T0810Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 143.708 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 21.350 ms, `html-large` third at 17.382 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.194 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.852 ms. PDF stage attribution kept `layout` first at 84.089 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 30.249 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.141 ms p95. The profile recommendation still points at layout/page-content assembly for the next performance slice.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing showed the dependency-free SVG PDF renderer already supports text font selection, anchors, dominant-baseline, letter-spacing, `textLength`, transforms, opacity, clip/mask, markers, gradients, and stroke styling, but silently ignored SVG/CSS `text-decoration` and `text-decoration-line`. That is a visible fidelity gap for generated diagrams and label-heavy assets.
- Renderer change: `SvgStyle` now carries an inherited `SvgTextDecoration` bitset through the existing SVG cascade. Presentation attributes, stylesheet rules, and inline declarations parse `text-decoration` and `text-decoration-line` for `underline`, `overline`, `line-through`, and `none`, with `var()` resolution matching the surrounding text-style parser. Unsupported shorthand parts such as style/color/thickness are ignored instead of pretending to support them. PDF text rendering now emits decoration as vector stroke lines beside the selectable text object using the final text matrix after anchor and `textLength` adjustments.
- Fresh-eyes correction during implementation: the first draft applied presentation `text-decoration` and `text-decoration-line` through an `or_else`, which would have ignored a valid `text-decoration-line` when an unsupported shorthand was also present. The final implementation applies both declarations in order, and the regression test pins that case with `text-decoration="wavy"` plus `text-decoration-line="underline"`.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF normal text decoration for Markdown strikethrough, SVG shape rendering, SVG text selectability, font subsetting, ToUnicode generation, glyph shaping, image fitting, frankenmermaid SVG asset loading, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The new work is isolated to SVG style parsing plus PDF vector decoration strokes inside the same graphics state, alpha state, clipping, and text transform as the decorated label.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_text_decoration_draws_vector_lines_without_flattening_text` proves CSS-variable underline, `text-decoration-line` overline plus line-through, parent presentation-attribute underline, `tspan text-decoration="none"` reset, inline `tspan` line-through re-enable, and the invalid-shorthand/valid-line-property ordering case. It also confirms decorated labels remain real selectable PDF text. The full SVG PDF subset still passes 84/84 tests.
- Profile/visual proof: fresh profile golden checksums validated with `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt`. Rendering `examples/showcase.md` to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-svg-decoration.pdf` produced SHA-256 `5bf17b893e628147bb381717ede6ec630adbc71e782fe3d203376c1f05030b4c`, matching the previous Mermaid-highlight proof because the showcase SVG has no text-decoration. Ghostscript rasterized page 3 to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-svg-decoration-page-3.png` with SHA-256 `473a03b5571ee890b3fbbd065ace3e1494b4529ffb327c1df3f321c27f214def`; visual inspection showed the frankenmermaid diagram, highlighted Mermaid source, and following blockquote remain correctly framed with no overlap.
