## Active Goal Continuation - HTML URL Scheme Borrowing
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T08:15:34Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs`, `tests/smoke_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-urlscheme-profile-20260707T081534Z/` and temporary comparison artifacts under `/data/tmp/fmd-urlscheme-*` and `/data/tmp/fmd-url-heavy*` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the preceding profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-decoration-profile-20260707T0810Z/` ranked `html-large` third at 17.382 ms p95, behind `pdf-large` and `parser-large` but ahead of several support scenarios. The canonical `html-large` harness renders a pre-parsed 1 MiB generated document, so HTML emitter overhead is isolated from parser cost.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Source tracing showed `safe_url` parsed every link/image scheme into a temporary `String` and then allocated a second lowercase `String` before comparing against the allow-list. This happened in the HTML emitter's hot inline path even though the rendered URL always borrowed the original trimmed destination.
- Renderer change: `UrlScheme::Scheme` now borrows the original scheme slice. Scheme validation scans bytes, keeps the existing gap/obfuscation rejection semantics, and compares allowed schemes with `eq_ignore_ascii_case` instead of allocating lowercase text. Link and image allow-lists remain unchanged: links allow `http`, `https`, `mailto`, and `tel`; images allow only `http` and `https`.
- Fresh-eyes correction during implementation: the first patch accidentally passed `&&str` into `valid_url_scheme`; this would coerce, but it was noisy and easy to misread. The final code passes the borrowed `&str` directly.
- Behavior proof: `unsafe_markdown_url_schemes_are_neutralized` now also pins mixed-case unsafe `javascript:`, mixed-case allowed link schemes, mixed-case HTTP image schemes, and rejection of link-only `mailto:` for images. Existing tab-obfuscated `java\tscript:` and `data:` image rejection remain covered.
- Performance proof: a frozen pre-change `release-perf` CLI and harness were copied to `/data/tmp` before editing. The URL-heavy 2.75 MiB Markdown fixture rendered byte-identical before/after with SHA-256 `1863e296c4e489cfc5d890af6057f3c4abc5c5c7c07483cf78cf7d6080ac88f1`; Hyperfine over 25 CLI runs reported current at 142.6 ms mean versus baseline 144.0 ms mean, or 1.01 +/- 0.07 times faster. The canonical in-process `html-large` A/B over 40 iterations produced byte-identical output with SHA-256 `4f7d950c66aaaadbae7235b737070469ed45deba98144ce312957ec7037f72a5`; p95 moved from 15.287 ms to 13.348 ms on this host. The follow-up gauntlet recorded `html-large` p95 at 13.636 ms and validated all golden checksums.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, inline destination parsing, HTML escaping, CSS generation, PDF output, WASM portability, dependency policy, and unsafe-code policy are unchanged. The accepted change removes per-URL allocation from scheme detection while preserving the same trimmed destination slice for emitted attributes.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/html.rs`, `tests/smoke_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; frozen pre-change `release-perf` CLI/harness build; focused smoke test; `cargo fmt`; focused URL-heavy byte comparison; focused URL-heavy Hyperfine A/B; canonical `html-large` in-process A/B; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-html-urlscheme-profile-20260707T081534Z`; profile golden checksum validation.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a small behavior-preserving HTML emitter cleanup with byte-identical outputs and favorable measured `html-large` movement. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid renderer work still dominate the remaining roadmap surface.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF URL Scheme Borrowing Trial Rejection
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T08:25:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `tests/pdf_test.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. A `src/pdf.rs` trial changed the PDF URL-scheme detector from allocating/lowercasing into borrowed byte scanning, then tightened the allow-list dispatch by scheme length. Both production variants were manually reverted because focused same-host performance evidence rejected keeping them.
- Current profile context: fresh gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-urlscheme-profile-20260707T081534Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at 144.304 ms p95, with page-content generation, object serialization, and page-stream compression all materially larger than the tiny PDF URL sanitizer. The trial targeted a low-effort PDF-path allocation hypothesis inspired by the productive HTML URL-scheme cleanup, but required measurement before landing because PDF layout/serialization dominates.
- Rejected opportunity: remove the temporary scheme `String` and lowercase allocation inside `pdf_url_scheme`. Hypothesis: link-heavy PDFs would benefit from borrowing the original scheme slice while preserving the same safe URI policy.
- Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the lowercase URL-heavy 1.17 MiB Markdown fixture rendered byte-identical before/after with SHA-256 `866c80b0e9fb4dd861f968ddafd4e50b7610c80a44317805d74f27b5ffb4530d`, but Hyperfine over 20 CLI runs reported the frozen baseline faster: 614.0 ms mean versus 619.6 ms mean for the borrowed-scheme trial. A reversed-order rerun repeated the result: baseline 614.0 ms mean versus current 619.9 ms mean. The length-dispatched allow-list variant also stayed byte-identical but measured worse: baseline 612.3 ms mean versus current 621.2 ms mean.
- First-principles diagnosis: the original PDF sanitizer already lowercased schemes before allow-list matching, so mixed-case safe/unsafe behavior was already correct. The removed allocation is too small compared with PDF annotation construction, text layout, page content emission, compression, and final object serialization; the byte-scan plus case-insensitive comparisons did not move the real bottleneck and was measurably worse on the focused fixture.
- Coverage retained: `pdf_external_links_emit_safe_uri_annotations` and `pdf_svg_anchor_links_emit_safe_uri_annotations` now explicitly pin mixed-case safe schemes and mixed-case unsafe scheme rejection for Markdown links and SVG anchors. This guards the existing correct semantics even though the optimization was rejected.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; frozen pre-change `release-perf` CLI/harness build; focused Markdown/SVG PDF link tests during the trial; URL-heavy PDF byte comparison; three focused Hyperfine A/B runs; manual production-code revert; final `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` empty.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS with retained tests; do not replace the PDF URL-scheme lowercasing parser with the borrowed HTML-style parser without stronger profiler evidence. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content work and broader dependency-free SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

- First-principles proof: word normalization, non-ASCII rejection, minimum-left/right policy, output ordering, TeX-pattern fallback, paragraph breaking, PDF layout, HTML output, parser behavior, compression, dependency policy, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The only release behavior change is replacing a linear exception search with an equivalent direct dispatch for the same built-in English exception set.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Width Cache Count Trial Rejection
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T09:02:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. A `src/pdf.rs` trial replaced the shaped-width cache type alias with an internal `WidthCache` struct carrying an exact entry counter, then reverted it because focused same-host evidence rejected keeping the change.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0902Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at p95 141.443 ms, followed by `parser-large` at 21.216 ms, `html-large` at 20.928 ms, `pdf-showcase` at 10.527 ms, and `compress-corpus` at 4.995 ms. PDF stage attribution still put `layout` first at p95 84.268 ms, then `page_content_stream_generation` at 27.967 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 22.946 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 53.313 ms total across 252 page streams.
- Rejected opportunity: `cached_shaped_width` recomputes `cache.values().map(HashMap::len).sum()` on every miss before deciding whether the render-local width cache is below `WIDTH_CACHE_MAX`. The trial replaced that per-miss bucket scan with an exact `len` field incremented on insert, while keeping the same `(slot, font-size)` outer key, string inner key, cached `LayoutUnit`, and admission cap.
- Behavior proof during the trial: `cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture` passed. Focused `pdf-large` renders stayed byte-identical to the frozen pre-change PDF at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the frozen 10-iteration baseline reported `pdf-large` p95 143.973 ms and mean 142.119 ms. The first after-run reported p95 145.192 ms and mean 142.208 ms. A second no-rebuild 20-iteration baseline reported p95 143.947 ms and mean 142.020 ms, while the matching after-run reported p95 146.550 ms and mean 142.102 ms. The change was byte-identical but did not improve mean and regressed p95 on the same host.
- First-principles diagnosis: the avoided bucket-count sum is not material for the current cache shape; the cache has few `(slot, font-size)` buckets, and the real `layout` stage cost remains dominated by paragraph construction, shaping/measurement, line-breaking, and segment assembly. Carrying a separate counter made the type less direct without moving the measured bottleneck.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; fresh broad `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0902Z`; focused frozen harness baseline; focused PDF profiling regression; focused 10-iteration after-run plus byte comparison; focused 20-iteration baseline/after rerun plus byte comparison; manual `apply_patch` revert of the production trial; final `cargo fmt --check`; final `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` is empty.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS; do not replace the PDF shaped-width cache type alias with a counted wrapper unless a more targeted profile proves the per-miss cache length sum is material. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer work still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG CSS Rect Radius Fidelity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T09:28:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0902Z/` remains proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh current-HEAD gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0902Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at p95 141.443 ms, followed by `parser-large`, `html-large`, `pdf-showcase`, and `compress-corpus`. This pass deliberately targeted the active dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer objective rather than forcing a noisy scalar optimization into the dominant PDF layout stage.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing through `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` and the SVG parser found that frankenmermaid emits CSS geometry declarations such as `rx` and `ry` on rectangles, while the PDF renderer only read `rx`/`ry` presentation attributes. Browser SVG rounded those labels and clusters, but the PDF vector path could silently render them as sharp-corner rectangles.
- Renderer change: `parse_svg_rect` now resolves a small, geometry-only `SvgRectRadius` from presentation attributes, matching author CSS rules, and inline style declarations using the same selector order and custom-property scope used by SVG paint/style parsing. The existing one-radius renderer is retained for compatibility: `rx` wins when present, `ry` is the fallback, and final drawing still clamps the radius to the rectangle dimensions. Invalid CSS radius declarations are ignored instead of erasing a valid lower-priority attribute or rule.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_css_rect_rx_ry_rounds_rectangle_geometry` covers stylesheet `rx`, stylesheet `ry` through `var()`, inline style override, and an invalid stylesheet `rx: var(--missing)` preserving a valid `rx` attribute. The test proves those four rectangles no longer emit sharp `re f` operators and instead emit cubic rounded-corner path segments.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF normal text and table layout, SVG paint cascade, gradients, markers, text, clipping/masking, object ordering, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change is isolated to non-inherited SVG rect geometry parsing and reuses the existing rounded-rect PDF path emission.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css_rect_rx_ry_rounds_rectangle_geometry -- --nocapture`; focused SVG/CSS subset `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete frankenmermaid/SVG fidelity gap without new dependencies and keeps the dependency-free PDF SVG renderer aligned with browser CSS geometry for rounded rectangles. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML ASCII Font Mask Table
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T09:18:27Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T091011Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-ascii-mask-profile-20260707T091606Z/`, and temporary `/data/tmp/fmd-ascii-mask-*` comparison artifacts is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.

This pass deliberately targeted `html-large`, a non-PDF low-fruit renderer path, while leaving the dominant PDF layout work for a separate lever.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Source tracing showed HTML font-usage collection scans large ASCII text runs and computed `1u128 << byte` for every byte before OR-ing into a per-font character mask. That work is pure deterministic classification and repeats heavily in the 1 MiB pre-parsed HTML scenario.
- Renderer change: `ascii_char_mask` now uses a compile-time 256-entry `u128` lookup table, with masks populated for ASCII bytes and a debug assertion preserving the private ASCII invariant. The 256-entry shape lets a `u8` index address the table directly while keeping non-ASCII callers out through the existing `is_ascii` gates. The emitted character ordering, stability seed, font-subset inputs, CSS, HTML body, escaping, parser behavior, PDF output, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Behavior/performance proof: a frozen pre-change `release-perf` harness reported focused `html-large` p95 14.908 ms and mean 13.265 ms over 50 iterations, with `html-large.html` SHA-256 `4f7d950c66aaaadbae7235b737070469ed45deba98144ce312957ec7037f72a5`. The accepted table version remained byte-identical with the same SHA-256 and reported p95 13.368 ms and mean 12.578 ms over 50 iterations. A reverse-order frozen-baseline rerun stayed slower at p95 14.227 ms and mean 13.512 ms. The broad after gauntlet recorded `html-large` p95 13.659 ms and mean 12.808 ms, and every golden checksum validated.
- Regression target: `ascii_char_mask_table_matches_shift_definition` pins each ASCII table entry to the original shift expression, while the existing `font_char_set_keeps_btree_character_order` continues proving deterministic ASCII/non-ASCII character ordering.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/html.rs`, `tests/smoke_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; focused `cargo test html::tests --lib -- --nocapture`; frozen-baseline and current focused 50-iteration `html-large` A/B runs; byte comparison and SHA-256 checks for `html-large.html`; reverse-order frozen-baseline rerun; broad `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-html-ascii-mask-profile-20260707T091606Z`; broad golden checksum validation; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes a small repeated scalar cost from HTML font-use scanning with byte-identical output and no new dependency or portability cost. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Asymmetric Rect Radii
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T09:31:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-asymmetric-radii-profile-20260707T093059Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the post-HTML-mask gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-ascii-mask-profile-20260707T091606Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 141.335 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 20.454 ms, `html-large` third at 13.659 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.120 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.850 ms. The follow-up gauntlet for this pass recorded `pdf-large` at 141.633 ms p95, `parser-large` at 22.436 ms, `html-large` at 13.346 ms, `pdf-showcase` at 10.163 ms, and `compress-corpus` at 5.025 ms. Parser classification remains visible in the profile, but recent same-host parser trials rejected the obvious scalar loop variants, so this pass targeted a concrete SVG/Mermaid fidelity gap rather than forcing noisy parser churn.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing through the PDF SVG parser found that `rect` geometry had already learned CSS `rx`/`ry`, but storage and path emission still collapsed both axes into one scalar radius. That rendered `rx="6" ry="2"` as circular-corner geometry, and clip-path rectangles used the same one-radius shortcut.
- Renderer change: `SvgRect` now stores both `rx` and `ry`. `SvgRectRadius::resolved` applies SVG fallback semantics by copying the present axis to the missing axis, while keeping genuinely asymmetric radii distinct. Painted rectangles and clip-path rectangle operations clamp each axis independently to half the rectangle width or height and emit elliptical cubic corner paths when both radii are positive. Unclamped equal-radius output keeps the same path formulas and numeric formatting, while oversized radii now follow the SVG per-axis clamp instead of collapsing both axes to the smaller scalar.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_rect_rx_ry_emit_asymmetric_elliptical_corners` covers a painted rect and a `clipPath` rect with `rx=6` and `ry=2`, proves the emitted path uses the distinct vertical control points, and rejects the old collapsed circular path. Existing CSS radius coverage still passes, including stylesheet, custom-property, inline-style, and invalid-declaration fallback cases.
- Output/performance proof: the follow-up gauntlet `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-asymmetric-radii-profile-20260707T093059Z` validated all golden checksums. Representative existing equal-radius outputs `pdf-showcase.pdf` and `pdf-large.pdf` are byte-identical to the prior profile run under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-ascii-mask-profile-20260707T091606Z/`, proving the new asymmetric support does not perturb current showcase or large-document PDF bytes.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF text/table layout, SVG paint cascade, CSS geometry lookup, gradient rendering, markers, masks, link annotations, compression, PDF object ordering, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change only preserves an already-parsed second rect-radius axis through the existing dependency-free SVG vector path renderer.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_rect_rx_ry_emit_asymmetric_elliptical_corners -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css_rect_rx_ry_rounds_rectangle_geometry -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; broad profile gauntlet above; golden checksum validation from the profile bundle; direct `cmp -s` comparisons for pre/post `pdf-showcase.pdf` and `pdf-large.pdf`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes an SVG rect geometry correctness gap for Mermaid-style output without new dependencies, unsafe code, or byte drift in existing representative PDFs. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content, parser classification, and broader dependency-free SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Alpha Resource Scan Trial Rejection
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T10:20:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. A `src/pdf.rs` trial was implemented, behavior-tested, measured, and manually reverted because whole-scenario and serialization-stage evidence did not justify keeping it.
- Current profile context: the accepted parser-finalization profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-finalize-final-20260707T1002Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 139.843 ms p95 and mean 137.301 ms, followed by `parser-large` at 17.248 ms p95 and `html-large` at 13.744 ms p95. PDF stage attribution showed `layout` first at 81.540 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 27.806 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.345 ms p95, `serialize_total` at 56.118 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 258.248 us p95 per stream.
- Rejected opportunity: replace the existing `tail.windows(4).position(|window| window == b"/GSa")` scan in `collect_svg_alpha_states` with a helper that first searches for `G` bytes and then checks the surrounding `/GSa` resource-name shape. Hypothesis: SVG-heavy PDFs with sparse alpha-state resource names might skip most four-byte window comparisons while preserving the existing permissive name policy.
- Behavior proof during the rejected trial: focused unit coverage pinned the scanner's current resource-name policy, including the existing behavior where `/GSa10001000x` still contributes the `/GSa10001000` state. Existing opacity and drop-shadow PDF tests passed. Stable golden outputs from the pre-change and after-run were byte-identical for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-alpha-scan-after-20260707T1012Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 141.402 ms and mean 139.979 ms, worse than the fresh baseline's 139.843 ms p95 and 137.301 ms mean. The targeted `pdf_object_serialization_total` stage moved only from 23.345 ms p95 to 23.305 ms p95, while `serialize_total` regressed from 56.118 ms p95 to 56.317 ms p95 and `page_content_stream_generation` regressed from 27.806 ms p95 to 28.155 ms p95. That is too small and too noisy to accept, especially with an end-to-end regression.
- First-principles diagnosis: alpha-state resource discovery is not a dominant serialization cost in the current corpora. The helper reduced some four-byte window comparisons but added a second loop shape and branch pattern around each `G` byte. A trial-only off-by-one bug also showed the helper was easier to get wrong around `from` positions inside an existing marker. The original compact window scan is clearer and effectively neutral at this scale.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused scanner, SVG opacity, and CSS drop-shadow tests during the trial; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; focused `release-perf` after gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons; stage-summary comparison; manual `apply_patch` revert of the trial; final `cargo fmt --check`; final `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` is empty.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS; do not retry the `G`-first SVG alpha-state scan without a corpus where alpha resource discovery is proven material. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and dependency-free SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Symbol Use ViewBox Sizing
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T10:39:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-symbol-use-final-20260707T1045Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest accepted profile before this pass, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-finalize-final-20260707T1002Z/`, ranked `pdf-large` first at 139.843 ms p95 and `parser-large` second at 17.248 ms p95. The immediately preceding alpha-scan trial was rejected because it did not produce a meaningful measured win, so this pass targeted a concrete dependency-free SVG fidelity gap instead of forcing another noisy scalar micro-optimization.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 4, effort 2, score 6.0. Source tracing showed `SvgReusableDef` preserved only raw attributes/body, and `parse_svg_use_elements` expanded `<symbol>` bodies like ordinary groups. As a result, `<use href="#symbol" width="..." height="...">` ignored the symbol `viewBox`, ignored the use-site viewport dimensions, and rendered the symbol at raw group coordinates.
- Renderer change: reusable definitions now cache parsed symbol `viewBox` and `preserveAspectRatio` metadata. When a `<use>` expands a symbol body, the renderer composes the existing use-site x/y/style transform with a viewBox-to-viewport transform before parsing the referenced children. The transform honors `preserveAspectRatio="none"` with non-uniform scaling and the default `meet` mode with centered uniform scaling. Symbols without a usable viewBox keep the existing group-like expansion path, and symbols without explicit width/height fall back to their viewBox dimensions to preserve the renderer's practical natural-size behavior.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_use_symbol_viewbox_scales_to_use_viewport` covers a stretched symbol (`preserveAspectRatio="none"`, `viewBox="0 0 10 10"`, `use width="20" height="10"`) and a default meet-scaled symbol (`viewBox="0 0 20 10"`, `use width="20" height="4"`). The test asserts the exact PDF matrices (`2 0 0 1 5 2 cm` for stretch and `0.4 0 0 0.4 11 16 cm` for centered meet) and rejects the old unscaled `q 1 0 0 1 5 2 cm ...` output.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, non-symbol `<use>` expansion, recursive use aliases, anchor links, style cascade, marker rendering, gradients, patterns, masks, clipping, text, embedded images, PDF object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change only adds a deterministic affine transform before parsing children of referenced symbols with a valid viewBox.
- Output/performance proof: the final short follow-up gauntlet `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-symbol-use-final-20260707T1045Z` validated representative outputs. Stable golden files were byte-identical to `continue-inline-finalize-final-20260707T1002Z` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The final gauntlet reported `pdf-large` p95 145.312 ms, `pdf-showcase` p95 10.242 ms, `parser-large` p95 17.704 ms, and `html-large` p95 13.209 ms over three iterations; this pass claims fidelity and byte-stability, not a performance win.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_use -- --nocapture`; broader `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; post-cleanup rerun of the focused symbol regression; post-cleanup full gate sequence; final release-perf build plus short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a real SVG symbol/use correctness gap in the no-dependency PDF renderer while keeping existing representative outputs stable and preserving WASM/core constraints. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Odd Dasharray Normalization
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T10:37:01Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-dasharray-final-20260707T103436Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest reference profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-symbol-use-final-20260707T1045Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at p95 145.312 ms, followed by `parser-large` at 17.704 ms, `html-large` at 13.209 ms, `pdf-showcase` at 10.242 ms, and `compress-corpus` at 4.829 ms. PDF-large stage attribution still put layout, page-content generation, object serialization, and compression ahead of tiny SVG dash serialization, so this pass targeted dependency-free SVG fidelity rather than claiming a runtime win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing found that SVG `stroke-dasharray` values were copied directly into PDF dash arrays. SVG requires an odd-length dash list to repeat so the effective list has even length, while PDF consumes the list as-is. That made common patterns such as `stroke-dasharray="2 3 4"` render with the wrong on/off phase in PDF. A fresh-eyes check also found that the old fixed-buffer loop could stop before validating later values, so an overlong declaration with a late negative value could be silently truncated into a valid-looking partial dash pattern.
- Renderer change: the dash parser now validates the complete numeric declaration before storing it in the fixed inline dash buffer. Negative values and overlong declarations are rejected as a whole instead of partially emitted, all-zero lists still normalize to no dash, and `none` keeps the existing reset semantics. PDF emission now repeats odd-length valid dash lists at serialization time, preserving compact style storage while emitting an even dash pattern as SVG requires.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_css_class_stroke_styles_apply_to_vector_shapes` now covers an odd presentation-attribute dash list and asserts the emitted PDF operator contains `[2 3 4 2 3 4] 0 d`. The same test also covers an overlong dash list with a late negative value and asserts it renders as an undashed cyan stroke with no partial `[1 2 3 4 5 6 7 8 ...]` PDF dash pattern.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF text/table layout, SVG paint cascade, class specificity, dash reset through `none`, even-length dash arrays, dash offsets, line caps/joins/miter limits, gradients, markers, masks, clipping, object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The only accepted production behavior is validating dash declarations atomically and bridging SVG's odd-list repetition rule when writing the PDF stroke options.
- Output/performance proof: the follow-up gauntlet `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-dasharray-final-20260707T103436Z` completed successfully. Representative stable golden files were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-symbol-use-final-20260707T1045Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The final gauntlet reported `pdf-large` p95 133.654 ms, `parser-large` p95 17.642 ms, `html-large` p95 13.493 ms, and `pdf-showcase` p95 10.000 ms over three iterations; this pass claims SVG correctness and byte-stability, not a performance win.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css_class_stroke_styles_apply_to_vector_shapes -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; release-perf build; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG stroke fidelity bug and hardens dash declaration parsing without new dependencies, unsafe code, or representative-output byte drift. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader dependency-free SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Inherited Text Size And Anchor
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T10:48:20Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-text-inheritance-final-20260707T104558Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest short gauntlet for this pass still ranked `pdf-large` first at p95 148.175 ms, followed by `parser-large` at 18.334 ms, `html-large` at 17.672 ms, `pdf-showcase` at 10.882 ms, and `compress-corpus` at 4.933 ms. The remaining clear opportunities are mostly SVG renderer fidelity issues rather than reliable scalar hot-path wins, so this pass targeted a high-confidence frankenmermaid/SVG text-label correctness gap identified by read-only agent review.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 4, confidence 5, effort 2, score 10.0. Source tracing showed `SvgStyle` inherited font weight, slant, family, dominant baseline, letter spacing, and text decoration, but not `font-size` or `text-anchor`. `parse_svg_text_elements` therefore resolved child `<text>` elements from hardcoded `12.0` and `start`, so generator-style markup such as `<g font-size="20" text-anchor="middle"><text ...>` rendered too small and left-anchored in PDF.
- Renderer change: `SvgStyle` and `SvgStylePatch` now carry `font_size` and `text_anchor` as first-class inherited style properties. `parse_svg_style_with_ancestors` resolves presentation attributes, matched CSS rules, and inline styles for both properties in the same cascade as the rest of SVG style, while `<text>` and `<tspan>` parsing now consumes the resolved style instead of running a separate text-only cascade. Presentation `font-size` attributes intentionally keep the existing numeric-attribute parser so values like `20em` still use their leading number; stylesheet and inline-style `font-size` declarations keep CSS length semantics, including `em`, `ex`, percent, and custom properties relative to the parent text size.
- Fresh-eyes correction during implementation: the first patch reused CSS length parsing for presentation `font-size` attributes. The broad `pdf_svg` suite caught this as a regression in `pdf_svg_numeric_attributes_accept_e_prefixed_unit_suffixes`, where `font-size="20em"` inflated to the clamp instead of preserving the prior leading-number behavior. The final patch split presentation-attribute parsing from CSS declaration parsing and reran the full SVG suite.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_text_stylesheet_font_size_and_anchor_affect_selectable_text` now covers both a CSS-styled parent `<g>` and a direct presentation-attribute parent `<g>`, proving their child text inherits the expected 20-point size and middle anchoring. Existing tspan CSS `0.5em` inheritance, inline style priority, local text CSS rules, text length handling, and numeric-attribute compatibility remain covered and passing.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF table/layout code, non-text SVG paint, transforms, clipping, masks, gradients, markers, `use` expansion, text selectable encoding, PDF object ordering, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted behavior only moves two already-supported SVG text presentation properties into the inherited style state so group-authored diagram labels resolve like browser SVG.
- Output/performance proof: the follow-up gauntlet `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-text-inheritance-final-20260707T104558Z` completed successfully. Representative stable golden files were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-dasharray-final-20260707T103436Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. This pass claims SVG text fidelity and byte-stability on current representative corpora, not a performance win.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_text_stylesheet_font_size_and_anchor_affect_selectable_text -- --nocapture`; broad `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; release-perf build; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a common generator-output SVG text-label inheritance gap in the no-dependency PDF renderer while preserving existing numeric-attribute compatibility and stable representative outputs. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader dependency-free SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Modern Color Tokens
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T10:59:19Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-color-tokens-final-20260707T105927Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the previous accepted gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-text-inheritance-final-20260707T104558Z/` still showed the dominant work in `pdf-large`, but recent high-confidence opportunities were SVG/Mermaid fidelity issues rather than repeatable scalar hot-path wins. This pass targeted a concrete parser correctness gap that affects generated SVG from modern tools and CSS-heavy diagram renderers.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. Source tracing showed `parse_svg_color` only handled 3/6 digit hex and old numeric `rgb()/rgba()` parsing through a generic number list. That meant `#rgba`, `#rrggbbaa`, `rgb(100% 0% 0%)`, and `rgb(255 0 0 / 50%)` were either ignored, mis-normalized, or painted opaque because alpha never reached the existing PDF ExtGState path.
- Renderer change: SVG color parsing now returns RGB plus optional alpha through one shared internal helper. It supports 3/4/6/8 digit hex, case-insensitive `rgb()` and `rgba()`, comma alpha, slash alpha, percentage alpha, and percentage RGB channels with CSS-variable resolution. Paint parsing treats zero-alpha colors as `none`, while nonzero color alpha flows into the existing fill/stroke opacity plumbing. The transparent-color shortcut used by `color-mix()` now consults the same parser so modern zero-alpha color tokens do not behave differently in mix/compositing paths.
- Fresh-eyes correction during implementation: the first patch introduced a duplicate top-level whitespace splitter even though an existing helper already preserved parenthesized function tokens. Focused test compilation caught the duplicate symbol before broader gates. The final patch reuses the existing splitter and keeps the new helper surface limited to top-level slash splitting for modern color syntax.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_treats_fully_transparent_rgba_paint_as_none` now covers old `rgba(...,0)`, modern `rgb(... / 0%)`, shorthand `#rgba`, and long `#rrggbbaa`, proving transparent modern colors do not paint red or fall back to default black. `pdf_svg_partial_opacity_uses_native_pdf_extgstate_resources` now proves 8-digit hex alpha emits `/GSa05021000`, modern slash alpha emits `/GSa05001000`, and percentage RGB channels normalize `0%, 50%, 100%` to `0.000 0.500 1.000 rg` instead of dividing the percentages by 255.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF text/table layout, SVG geometry, transforms, masks, markers, gradients, patterns, text selection, PDF object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted change only replaces ad hoc old-`rgba` alpha detection with a shared dependency-free SVG color parser and routes its optional alpha through already-existing opacity machinery.
- Output/performance proof: the follow-up gauntlet `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-color-tokens-final-20260707T105927Z` completed successfully. Representative stable golden files were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-text-inheritance-final-20260707T104558Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The final short run reported `pdf-large` p95 137.534 ms, `parser-large` p95 17.403 ms, `html-large` p95 14.217 ms, and `pdf-showcase` p95 10.124 ms over three iterations; this pass claims SVG color fidelity and representative byte-stability, not a standalone performance win.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_treats_fully_transparent_rgba_paint_as_none -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_partial_opacity_uses_native_pdf_extgstate_resources -- --nocapture`; broad `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; release-perf build; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a modern SVG/CSS color parsing gap in the no-dependency PDF renderer while preserving existing representative outputs and all portability constraints. ## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Display And Visibility Cascade
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T11:10:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-visibility-cascade-final-20260707T1110Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest accepted SVG/color profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-color-tokens-final-20260707T105927Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at 137.534 ms p95, with parser/html work behind it. A read-only frontier scan identified a higher-confidence SVG fidelity gap than another noisy scalar micro-optimization: the style model collapsed `display:none`, `visibility:hidden`, and zero opacity into one `visible` bit, so `visibility:visible` descendants could not render inside hidden groups.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. SVG/CSS semantics make `display:none` an irreversible subtree suppression, but `visibility:hidden` is inherited and can be overridden by descendants. The old one-way bit was correct for `display:none` and group opacity, but wrong for generated diagrams that hide a container while explicitly re-showing selected children or labels.
- Renderer change: `SvgStyle` now carries separate `display_visible` and `visibility_visible` cascade state while retaining `visible` as the derived draw/link bit used by existing render call sites. Presentation attributes, matched stylesheet declarations, and inline style declarations parse display and visibility independently. Non-`none` display values restore only to the inherited display gate, so a child `display:inline` cannot revive a `display:none` ancestor. `visibility:visible` restores the inheritable visibility state, so a child shape or tspan can render inside a `visibility:hidden` ancestor when display and opacity still allow it.
- Fresh-eyes correction during implementation: after the first focused rect/CSS regression passed, a diff review found the text parser still returned early for an invisible parent `<text>`, which would incorrectly drop `<tspan visibility="visible">` descendants. The final patch skips text parsing only for irreversible display suppression or zero opacity, and `svg_text_element` now enforces the final effective visibility per emitted text run.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_visibility_visible_descendants_render_inside_hidden_groups` covers a direct `visibility="hidden"` group with a visible child rect, a stylesheet-hidden group with a `.css-visible` child rect, a `display:none` group whose child tries `display:inline`, and a hidden `<text>` whose visible cyan `<tspan>` must still emit selectable PDF text. The test asserts the green, blue, and cyan visible children render and the red/magenta hidden content does not paint.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF table/layout code, SVG geometry, color parsing, gradients, masks, markers, symbol/use expansion, link filtering, text shaping, object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted behavior only separates inherited visibility from subtree display/opacity suppression in the existing dependency-free SVG style cascade.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-visibility-cascade-final-20260707T1110Z` completed successfully and ranked `pdf-large` first at 135.494 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 17.190 ms, `html-large` at 13.761 ms, and `pdf-showcase` at 9.854 ms. Representative stable golden files were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-color-tokens-final-20260707T105927Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_visibility_visible_descendants_render_inside_hidden_groups -- --nocapture`; broad `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG cascade correctness bug in the no-dependency PDF renderer while preserving existing representative outputs and all portability constraints. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - Nested SVG Tspan Cascade
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T11:30:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-nested-tspan-final-20260707T1130Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest short gauntlet ranked `pdf-large` first at 142.073 ms p95 and 141.654 ms mean, followed by `parser-large` at 17.329 ms p95, `html-large` at 15.871 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` at 10.210 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` at 4.837 ms p95. This pass deliberately targeted a concrete SVG/Mermaid text fidelity gap rather than claiming a performance win from noisy short-run PDF numbers.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. Source tracing showed `parse_svg_text_elements` handled only direct child `<tspan>` elements. When a tspan contained nested tspans, `strip_svg_tags(child_body)` flattened all nested markup into the first-level tspan style, so nested class selectors such as `.outer .inner` and nested `visibility:visible` recovery inside a hidden tspan were ignored.
- Renderer change: SVG text parsing now keeps the no-tspan fast path unchanged, then uses a depth-limited recursive helper for tspan-bearing text bodies. The helper preserves selector ancestry, inherited text style, x/y/dx/dy placement, direct-tspan `textLength`, and parent textLength adjustment for contiguous same-line fragments. A depth cap of eight falls back to the previous safe flattening behavior instead of risking unbounded recursion on hostile or malformed SVG.
- Fresh-eyes correction during implementation: the first recursive shape would have skipped a first-level `visibility:hidden` tspan before inspecting its descendants. The accepted code skips only irreversible `display:none` suppression and zero effective opacity at that point, then lets `svg_text_element` enforce final effective visibility on each emitted text run. That allows a nested `visibility:visible` child to render while still preventing `display:none` or transparent subtrees from producing output.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_nested_tspan_children_apply_their_own_style` covers red outer text, a blue first-level tspan, a green nested tspan selected by `.outer .inner` with its own larger font size, and a cyan nested visible tspan inside a hidden parent tspan. The test rejects the old flattening behavior where nested text inherited only the first-level style.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF table/layout code, non-text SVG geometry, paint parsing, gradients, masks, markers, symbol/use expansion, object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted behavior only improves the dependency-free SVG text walker so nested text fragments retain their own cascade and visibility semantics.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-nested-tspan-final-20260707T1130Z` completed successfully. Representative stable golden files were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-visibility-cascade-final-20260707T1110Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_nested_tspan_children_apply_their_own_style -- --nocapture`; broad `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes another real SVG text cascade correctness gap in the no-dependency PDF renderer while preserving representative outputs and all portability constraints. A read-only peer review found a separate next target around terminal `!important` normalization for SVG paint/color declarations, but this pass kept the nested-tspan lever isolated. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Important Paint Normalization
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T11:38:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-important-paint-final-20260707T1138Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest short gauntlet ranked `pdf-large` first at 136.192 ms p95 and 135.936 ms mean, followed by `parser-large` at 17.769 ms p95, `html-large` at 13.974 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` at 10.058 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` at 4.845 ms p95. The pass therefore remains a renderer-fidelity improvement rather than a standalone runtime win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. A read-only peer scan found that keyword-like SVG style parsers stripped terminal `!important`, but paint/color paths could still pass values such as `#00ff00 !important` or `rgb(0 128 255 / 50%) !important` directly into color parsers. That made stylesheet or inline-style paint declarations fail parsing and fall back to lower-priority presentation attributes.
- Renderer change: `clean_svg_css_keyword_value` now strips a terminal `!important` token case-insensitively and allocation-free. The shared cleanup is reused for CSS variable values and at SVG paint/color parser boundaries: `currentColor`, context paint, paint values, gradient references, pattern references, paint alpha, and color parsing. This intentionally does not implement CSS priority; it only normalizes the terminal syntax so the existing cascade and parser decisions receive the intended value.
- Fresh-eyes correction during verification: a stronger alpha assertion initially expected the older fill-only ExtGState name, but the renderer's current text alpha resource encodes both fill and stroke alpha slots. The final regression asserts the actual emitted `/GSa05000500` state next to the normalized modern RGB paint, proving slash-alpha survives cleanup instead of only checking RGB channels.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_css_important_paint_and_color_values_are_normalized` covers stylesheet fill/stroke declarations, inline-style fill/stroke declarations with uppercase `!IMPORTANT`, stylesheet `color` feeding `currentColor`, and inline modern `rgb(... / 50%)` fill. The test proves the green/blue and magenta/cyan paints render, the modern RGB text color renders twice, alpha survives through a native PDF ExtGState, and the old red presentation-attribute fallback does not remain.
- First-principles proof: Markdown parsing, HTML output, PDF table/layout code, SVG geometry, selector matching, cascade ordering, CSS specificity, full CSS priority semantics, gradients/pattern storage, masks, markers, text selection, object serialization, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The accepted behavior only strips a terminal CSS annotation before existing dependency-free SVG paint and color parsers run.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-important-paint-final-20260707T1138Z` completed successfully. Representative stable golden files were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-nested-tspan-final-20260707T1130Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Descartes` for the bounded patch; `cargo fmt`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css_important_paint_and_color_values_are_normalized -- --nocapture`; broad `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete CSS/SVG paint parser correctness gap in the no-dependency PDF renderer while preserving representative outputs and all portability constraints. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining surface area.

This intentionally does not implement CSS priority semantics, selector reordering, or presentation-attribute priority changes; it only removes the terminal annotation so the current cascade layer can parse the value it already won.

- Renderer change: `build_cell_line` became an owned-token helper accepting `impl IntoIterator<Item = Tok>`. Normal wrapped lines are sealed with `std::mem::take(&mut cur)`, so token text/link ownership moves into `CellRun`. A fresh-eyes correction avoided allocating a one-token `Vec` for hard-split oversized word chunks by passing `std::iter::once(tok)` into the same owned helper.
- Behavior proof: wrapping decisions still use the same `cur_w`, pending-space width, word width, hard-break, overflow, and oversized-word character-split branches. Run merging still uses the same slot/link/strike equality predicate, and final `CellRun.width` is still measured after text merging with `text_width(&run.text, size, run.slot, faces)`, preserving cross-token shaping behavior for emitted table runs.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Stroke Geometry CSS Variables
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T13:05:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-stroke-vars-final-20260707T1305Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh profile at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T1245Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 136.147 ms p95, then `parser-large` at 17.180 ms p95, `html-large` at 14.295 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` at 9.694 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` at 4.830 ms p95. Two candidate micro-optimizations were rejected after measurement: the blockquote reference-collection candidate guard made `parser-large`/`reference_collection` worse, and fixed-deflate output preallocation made the final gauntlet's `compress-corpus` and `pdf-large` timings worse. This accepted pass therefore targets a concrete SVG/Mermaid fidelity gap rather than claiming a speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. Source tracing showed SVG paint, opacity, font, text, and several geometry values already resolved scoped CSS custom properties, but stroke geometry declarations still used raw numeric parsers for `stroke-width`, `stroke-miterlimit`, `stroke-dasharray`, and `stroke-dashoffset`. That meant a frankenmermaid or hand-authored SVG theme could drive stroke paint through `var(...)` while silently losing the matching width, dash, phase, or miter-limit variable.
- Renderer change: stylesheet patches, inline style declarations, and presentation attributes now route stroke width, dash array, dash offset, and miter limit through CSS-variable-aware helpers. The helpers reuse the existing whole-value `var(...)` resolver, existing terminal `!important` cleanup for CSS values, existing dash-pattern validation, existing odd-dash repeat behavior, existing miter-limit minimum, and the already scoped custom-property cascade collected for each element. No new dependency, unsafe code, CSS expression evaluator, or cascade-order change was introduced.
- Fresh-eyes correction: the implementation also covers presentation attributes such as `stroke-width="var(--w)"` when the variable is supplied by a matching selector or inline style. This is safe because `svg_css_vars_for_element` collects ancestor, selector, and inline custom properties before presentation attributes are parsed, so the change makes presentation attributes consistent with existing paint/opacity variable behavior without reordering author CSS.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_svg_css_variables_drive_stroke_geometry_declarations` pins exact PDF operators for three cases: a stylesheet rule with local custom properties, an inline `style` attribute with local custom properties, and presentation stroke attributes fed by selector-scoped custom properties. The assertions prove width, miter limit, dash pattern, and dash offset are all resolved before vector stroke emission.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-stroke-vars-final-20260707T1305Z` completed successfully. Representative rendered goldens were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-text-operator-append-final-20260707T1235Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The short timing run reported `pdf-large` p95 143.190 ms and mean 141.267 ms with layout still dominant at 90.765 ms p95, so this pass claims fidelity plus stable bytes, not an end-to-end performance improvement.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css_variables_drive_stroke_geometry_declarations -- --nocapture`; broad `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct rendered-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a real custom-property stroke-geometry gap in the no-dependency SVG-to-PDF renderer, directly improving themed frankenmermaid-style SVG handling while preserving representative outputs and all portability constraints. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/object serialization and broader SVG/Mermaid surface still have remaining opportunities.

## Active Goal Continuation - Page Stream Dictionary Direct Write
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T13:15:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-page-stream-dict-final-20260707T1315Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the previous accepted profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-stroke-vars-final-20260707T1305Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 143.190 ms p95 and showed serialization-side work as a persistent target: `page_stream_compression` had 252 stream operations over 4.8 MB of page operators, `pdf_object_serialization_total` was 74.612 ms total across three iterations with 26.466 ms p95, and `xref_trailer_writing` was 5.700 ms total. The selected lever targets object/stream serialization, not the already rejected parser and fixed-deflate preallocation experiments.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing found that each page content stream built a temporary dictionary `String` inside `page_stream`, then the object loop built another temporary formatted header string before appending the compressed bytes. Uncompressed stream fallbacks also copied raw page bytes into a new `Vec<u8>` even though the caller immediately wrote the borrowed page buffer.
- Renderer change: `PdfStream` now carries borrowed-or-owned bytes through `Cow<[u8]>`, the decoded length, and a FlateDecode flag instead of a preformatted dictionary string. The page-content object loop now appends the existing PDF object header directly, writes the stream dictionary with `append_decimal_usize`, and writes borrowed raw bytes when compression is skipped. The compression decision, `/Length`, `/Filter /FlateDecode`, `/DL`, stream bytes, object numbering, offsets, xref rows, and file-id inputs are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `stream_dict_writer_preserves_raw_and_flate_shapes` pins exact raw and FlateDecode dictionary bytes. The committed golden-output test passed, proving representative HTML/PDF output bytes are unchanged. The final gauntlet's representative rendered goldens were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-stroke-vars-final-20260707T1305Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-page-stream-dict-final-20260707T1315Z` completed successfully. The overall short run was noisy and worse across unrelated parser/html/PDF scenarios, so this pass does not claim an end-to-end latency win. Within the targeted profiled stage, `pdf_object_serialization_total` total time moved from 74.612 ms to 73.265 ms across three iterations and p95 was essentially flat at 26.404 ms versus 26.466 ms; the honest claim is allocation cleanup and byte-stable serialization, not a statistically broad speedup.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --lib stream_dict_writer_preserves_raw_and_flate_shapes -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --lib pdf_writer_tests -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct rendered-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes avoidable per-page stream dictionary/header allocation and raw fallback copying in the profiled PDF serialization path with exact byte preservation, no new dependencies beyond `std::borrow::Cow`, no unsafe code, and no WASM portability cost. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression and broader SVG/Mermaid rendering still have remaining opportunities.

## Active Goal Continuation - Inline Resolver No-Delimiter Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T13:44:49Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-no-delim-final-20260707T134449Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the prior accepted profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-page-operators-final-20260707T133338Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 135.223 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 17.594 ms p95 and `html-large` at 16.920 ms p95. Parser stage attribution showed `inline_parse` still accounted for 56,619 invocations across three iterations, 29.329 ms total, and 1,020,390 approximate allocations.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing found that every full inline parse called `resolve_emphasis`, allocating delimiter resolver state even when tokenization emitted no `InlineEl::Delim`. Full parsing is still required for code spans, character references, links, images, inline HTML, URI autolinks, bare email autolinks, and strikethrough, so no-emphasis full parses were paying for a resolver that could not pair anything.
- Parser change: tokenization now tracks whether it emitted any `*` or `_` emphasis delimiter elements. Runs with delimiter elements keep the existing `resolve_emphasis` path unchanged. Runs without delimiter elements finalize the flat token list directly through the existing move-based `emit_inline_el_owned` logic, preserving node order, adjacent text merging, and the literal handling policy for opaque nodes.
- Fresh-eyes correction: inert delimiter runs, such as intraword underscores, remain buffered as literal text and do not trigger the resolver. That is intentional: no `InlineEl::Delim` means there is no CommonMark delimiter-stack state to resolve. The profiler allocation estimate now charges resolver state only when a resolver can actually run, while still counting the full-parser char/token/output work for no-delimiter parses.
- Behavior proof: `profiled_full_inline_parse_without_emphasis_skips_resolver_state` forces full inline parsing with a code span, entity, URI autolink, bare email autolink, and inline HTML but no emphasis delimiters. It pins the exact AST and the lowered no-resolver allocation estimate. The full parser conformance test file passed 104/104, and the full Rust test suite passed.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-inline-no-delim-final-20260707T134449Z` completed successfully. Representative rendered goldens were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-page-operators-final-20260707T133338Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The short run reported `parser-large` p95 18.117 ms and mean 17.427 ms, `html-large` p95 13.595 ms, and `pdf-large` p95 141.841 ms; those end-to-end numbers are noisy. The concrete targeted proof is that `parser-large` inline allocation count dropped from 1,020,390 to 733,560 across three iterations with identical parser-rendered HTML, and the spanned parser inline allocation count dropped from 340,130 to 244,520 for its one-iteration scenario.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --test parser_conformance profiled_full_inline_parse_without_emphasis_skips_resolver_state -- --nocapture`; full `cargo test --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct rendered-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes avoidable emphasis resolver state from full inline parses that contain no `*` or `_` delimiter elements, with byte-identical representative outputs, no new dependencies, no unsafe code, and no WASM portability cost. The active broader goal remains open because larger PDF layout/compression and additional SVG/Mermaid fidelity/performance surface remain.

## Active Goal Continuation - Table Layout Width Cache Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T13:55:59Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-table-width-cache-final-20260707T135559Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the prior accepted profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-inline-no-delim-final-20260707T134449Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 141.841 ms p95. Within that scenario, `layout` dominated at 82.041 ms p95 and 245.564 ms total across three iterations. Source tracing found that paragraph layout already used the per-render shaped-width cache, but PDF table measurement and final cell wrapping still called uncached `text_width`, so repeated table words/spaces were shaped once for min/max/wrap-badness measurement and again when final visual cell lines were built.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The lever is narrow: reuse the existing render-local width cache for table text measurement/wrapping rather than adding a table-specific cache or changing the allocator. The cached value is the same deterministic `Faces::shaped_width` result already used by paragraph layout, keyed by font slot, font size, and text.
- Renderer change: `layout_table` now receives `LayoutCx`'s per-render `width_cache` and threads it through `table_cell_measure`, `wrap_cell_styled`, and `build_cell_line_owned`. Table min-content/max-content measurement, column-width allocation, over-wide word splitting, final run widths, alignment offsets, links, strikethroughs, header bolding, zebra striping, and tagged table structure are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `table_cell_measure_reuses_the_layout_width_cache` pins that table measurement populates the shared cache while producing exactly the same measured line count, min-content width, and max-content width as a fresh uncached measurement. Full table-wrap tests, focused PDF table tests, committed golden-output tests, and the full Rust test suite passed.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-table-width-cache-final-20260707T135559Z` completed successfully. ## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Direct Body Render
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T14:14:33Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-direct-body-final-20260707T141433Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the prior accepted profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-code-width-cache-final-20260707T140706Z/` ranked `html-large` third overall at 18.172 ms p95 and 14.021 ms mean, behind `pdf-large` and `parser-large`. After several PDF layout/cache passes, this was a distinct low-hanging HTML path: `render()` built the entire body in a separate `String`, then allocated the final HTML document and copied the multi-megabyte body into it.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. The lever is a single allocation/copy removal in a top-three scenario. It does not change parsing, escaping, heading id state, CSS generation, custom CSS sanitization, syntax highlighting, or the document envelope; it only streams block rendering into the already allocated final HTML buffer after the header has been written.
- Renderer change: `render()` now computes title and CSS as before, allocates the final document string with header/CSS plus the existing body-capacity estimate, writes the header, renders blocks directly into that final buffer with a fresh `RenderState`, then appends the unchanged footer. The previous body `String` allocation and `html.push_str(&body)` copy are gone.
- Behavior proof: `render_writes_body_between_document_envelope` pins an exact custom-CSS HTML document envelope, escaped body text, and heading id placement without depending on generated font CSS. Existing HTML unit tests, the smoke test suite, and committed golden-output tests passed, and the final gauntlet's representative rendered goldens were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-code-width-cache-final-20260707T140706Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-html-direct-body-final-20260707T141433Z` completed successfully. The targeted `html-large` scenario improved from 18.172 ms p95 / 14.021 ms mean in the prior artifact to 11.320 ms p95 / 10.074 ms mean in this short run. `html-showcase` stayed essentially flat at 0.666 ms p95, while unrelated `parser-large` and `pdf-large` samples drifted worse in the same short run; this pass claims the targeted HTML allocation/copy reduction and byte identity, not a broad project-wide p95 improvement.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --lib render_writes_body_between_document_envelope -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --lib html::tests -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --test smoke_test -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct rendered-golden byte comparisons.

- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The target is small but direct: the collector only needs temporary borrowed views of the original source lines, and `strip_blockquote_marker` already returns exactly the borrowed slice that `strip_blockquote` previously copied into a `String`.

The main blockquote parser still keeps its owned `Vec<String>` path unchanged because it retains inner block text for AST construction.
- Fresh-eyes proof: `blockquote_lazy_continuation` still receives the previous stripped inner line, now via `inner.last().copied()` instead of `inner.last().map(String::as_str)`. The same line order and text are passed to the reference map and recursive collector, with no change to paragraph-boundary, HTML-block, indented-code, table, list, or inline parsing rules.

- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T15:11:02Z.

Page content generation owns MCID assignment through a dense, monotonically incremented `next_mcid` counter and pushes each `StructMark` at the same point the marked content is emitted, so the later sort duplicates an invariant the renderer already controls.

In debug builds, `struct_tree_debug_checks_render_order_dense_mcid_invariant` verifies the new invariant trips on out-of-order MCIDs before such state could silently produce a malformed tree.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-struct-mark-order-final-20260707T1518Z` completed successfully.
