This pass deliberately targeted a parser allocation cleanup outside the recent PDF serialization/cache passes.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing showed the main blockquote parser still copied every stripped quoted line into an owned `String`, copied lazy continuations with `trim_start().to_string()`, then immediately built borrowed views for reference stripping and recursive parsing. Recursive block parsing returns an owned AST and needs the inner lines only during the call, so those temporary line copies were unnecessary.
- Parser change: the main blockquote branch now stores borrowed `&str` slices from `strip_blockquote_marker(lines[i])` and `lines[i].trim_start()`, reuses those slices for the reference-definition removal pass, and passes them directly into bounded recursive parsing. The now-unused owning `strip_blockquote` helper was removed. Lazy continuation rules, reference-definition stripping inside blockquotes, nested-reference discovery, block ordering, rendered HTML/PDF, spans, and parser AST semantics are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: existing focused blockquote and reference tests cover definitions inside blockquotes, same-blockquote reference use, plain blockquotes, lazy-continuation reference-looking lines that must not resolve, and nested list/block quote interactions. `parser_spans` passed to guard source-span behavior, and committed golden-output tests passed.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-parser-bq-main-borrow-final-20260707T152023Z` completed successfully. Representative rendered/stable goldens were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T151324Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The targeted `blockquote_block` total time moved from 2.106 ms to 1.883 ms across three iterations, with p50 1.713 us to 1.523 us and p95 2.024 us to 2.094 us. End-to-end `parser-large` was noisy/worse at 18.069 ms p95 versus 17.355 ms pre-change, so this pass claims byte-preserving removal of owned blockquote line copies with narrow stage evidence, not a demonstrated parser-wide speedup. The existing parser allocation counter is approximate and did not expose the removed temporary `String` allocations directly.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `CopperCoyote` for `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Einstein` for the bounded implementation; focused `cargo test blockquote -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --lib refdef_paragraph_tests -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --test parser_spans -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-golden byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE ALLOCATION CLEANUP; this removes avoidable per-blockquote line string copies from the parser hot path with exact byte preservation, no new dependencies, no unsafe code, and no WASM portability cost. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/compression and broader SVG/Mermaid fidelity/performance surface remain.

- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing found that PDF tokenization allocated an owned `" "` payload for every breakable whitespace token and every soft break even though layout semantics are carried by `tok.space`/`tok.hard_break`, while measurement paths already explicitly measure `" "`. In prose-heavy PDFs this creates avoidable heap churn inside the dominant layout stage.
- Renderer/layout change: whitespace and soft/hard-break tokens now store an empty `String` payload. A small `token_visible_text` helper supplies the semantic visible text (`" "` for breakable/soft spaces, `""` for hard breaks, and `tok.text` for words) to measurement and rendering consumers. Segment building, table-cell line building, cached/uncached word measurement, and greedy fallback width measurement were updated to consume visible token text. Rendered spaces, selectable spaces, hard-break line splitting, table wrapping, list markers, justification, link/strike grouping, and PDF bytes are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_space_tokens_store_empty_payloads_but_segments_render_spaces` proves repeated spaces store empty payloads but still render/select as visible spaces with the same shaped width. `pdf_soft_break_tokens_render_one_space_but_hard_breaks_do_not` pins soft-break visible-space behavior and hard-break non-rendering behavior. - Timestamp: 2026-07-07T16:42:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Source tracing found that `process_emphasis` stored CommonMark opener-bottom bounds in a `BTreeMap<(char, usize), Option<usize>>` even though the key space is fixed and tiny: delimiter character is only `*` or `_`, and the closer slot is always `0..=5`. Each emphasis-resolution pass only performs keyed lookup and overwrite, never ordered iteration.
- Parser change: opener-bottom state now uses a 12-entry `[Option<usize>; 12]` plus `opener_bottom_index`, mapping `*` slots to `0..5` and `_` slots to `6..11`. The initial `None` state preserves absent-key behavior, storing `prev[c]` preserves both inserted `None` and inserted `Some(index)` behavior for the same delimiter char and slot, and all delimiter traversal, rule-of-three matching, back-walk budgeting, nesting-depth caps, output ordering, and text emission remain unchanged.

## Active Goal Continuation - Reusable Highlight Span Buffer
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T16:47:30Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/highlight.rs`, `src/html.rs`, `tests/highlight_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T1648Z/` and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-highlight-reuse-20260707T1650Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh pre-change gauntlet ranked `html-code-heavy` as a small but targeted non-PDF/non-parser hotspot at 2.297 ms p95 and 2.246 ms mean. Source tracing showed every highlighted HTML code block called `highlight(lang, code)`, allocating a fresh `Vec<Span>` even though the HTML renderer already owns per-render state that can safely retain scratch storage across blocks.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The optimization is allocation-focused and output-preserving: span values are byte offsets and token kinds only, so they can be cleared and reused without borrowing code text or carrying source lifetimes across blocks.
- Highlighter/API change: `highlight_into(lang, code, spans)` now clears and fills caller-owned span storage for generic, HTML, CSS, Markdown, Mermaid, and unknown-language cases. The existing public `highlight(lang, code) -> Vec<Span>` remains as the compatibility wrapper. Unknown languages still produce one `Plain` span covering the whole input, including empty input, and supported empty input still produces no spans.
- HTML renderer change: `RenderState` now owns a reusable `highlight_spans` scratch vector and passes it into code-block highlighting. Repeated fenced code blocks therefore reuse span capacity during one HTML render while preserving escaping, token classes, language class attributes, and emitted markup bytes.
- Behavior proof: `highlight_into_matches_highlight_for_supported_and_unknown_languages` pins wrapper equivalence across Rust, HTML, CSS, Markdown, Mermaid, SQL, and unknown languages. `highlight_into_clears_stale_spans` proves stale spans cannot leak across calls. `highlight_into_preserves_reusable_capacity` proves the intended allocation reuse path. Full highlighter fixtures, HTML escaping tests, committed golden-output tests, and the full project test suite passed.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-highlight-reuse-20260707T1650Z` completed successfully. Representative stable payload artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T1648Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The short run reported `html-code-heavy` p95 2.065 ms and mean 2.041 ms versus 2.297 ms p95 and 2.246 ms mean pre-change. Because this is a three-iteration sample, the honest claim is byte-preserving removal of per-code-block highlight vector allocation with favorable targeted evidence, not a statistically broad whole-render latency guarantee.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `GreenHarbor` for `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Poincare` using Agent Mail identity `PlumCarp` for the bounded implementation in `src/highlight.rs`, `src/html.rs`, and `tests/highlight_test.rs`; focused `cargo test --test highlight_test highlight_into -- --nocapture`; full `cargo test --test highlight_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE ALLOCATION CLEANUP; this removes avoidable repeated highlighter span-vector allocations from HTML code-block rendering with exact byte preservation, no new dependencies, no unsafe code, and no WASM portability cost. - Highlighter change: `language_key` now returns `Cow<'_, str>`, borrows already-normalized lowercase key segments, strips `language-` with ASCII case-insensitive semantics, and allocates only when the actual key segment contains ASCII uppercase that must be folded. Existing alias match arms and supported-language coverage are unchanged.

## Active Goal Continuation - Compression Stored-Fallback Early Abort
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T17:19:56Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-hyphen-exception-fastpath-20260707T1710Z/` and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-early-stored-20260707T1720Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the prior accepted gauntlet ranked `compress-corpus` as the largest non-PDF/non-parser remaining target at 4.883 ms p95 and 4.879 ms mean. Source tracing showed `zlib_compress` always completed the fixed-Huffman LZ77 encoding before comparing its body length against the cheaper stored-block fallback, even for deterministic incompressible payloads where the fixed body had already grown beyond the stored body and therefore could no longer win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. The optimization is a constrained algorithmic shortcut: once the byte length of the partial fixed-deflate body exceeds the known stored-block body length, monotonic future output can only make fixed larger, while the existing selection rule already chooses stored whenever stored is smaller.
- Compressor change: fixed-deflate generation now has an internal limit-aware helper. `BitWriter::pending_byte_len` accounts for a partially filled byte, `FixedDeflate` records whether its body is complete, and `zlib_compress` computes the stored body length up front, aborts fixed encoding when the fixed body can no longer win, and emits stored blocks for incomplete fixed results. Complete fixed results still use the exact old fixed body, incomplete results are never emitted, and all results carry the Adler-32 of the original uncompressed input.
- Behavior proof: `fixed_deflate_limit_aborts_lcg_data_and_zlib_still_roundtrips` pins that deterministic LCG input triggers the incomplete fixed path, retains the correct Adler-32, uses the stored-body length, and round-trips through the production inflater. `fixed_deflate_limit_completes_and_matches_full_fixed_body_when_smaller` pins that compressible text completes under the limit and matches the unlimited fixed body byte-for-byte.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-compress-early-stored-20260707T1720Z` completed successfully. Representative stable payload artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-hyphen-exception-fastpath-20260707T1710Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The targeted `compress-corpus` scenario improved from 4.883 ms p95 and 4.879 ms mean to 4.664 ms p95 and 4.623 ms mean in the short run.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `BlackDesert` for `.skill-loop-progress.md` and final `src/compress.rs` refinement; serial worker pass using Agent Mail identity `BlackForest` for the bounded `src/compress.rs` implementation; focused `cargo test --lib compress -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE TARGETED COMPRESSION OPTIMIZATION; this skips provably unnecessary fixed-Huffman/LZ77 work for stored-fallback payloads with exact output preservation, no new dependencies, no unsafe code, and no WASM portability cost. The active broader goal remains open because larger PDF layout/serialization and broader SVG/Mermaid fidelity/performance surface remain.

Source tracing showed `collect_nested_references` built a temporary `ReferenceMap` for each blockquote or list-item body, then immediately merged that temporary map into the shared document map.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The change is behavior-local: the existing scanner already has an insertion point for reference definitions, and first-definition-wins semantics are exactly `entry(label).or_insert(reference)` whether insertion targets a fresh temporary map or the final shared map.
- Parser change: `collect_link_reference_metadata` now delegates to `collect_link_reference_metadata_into`, which scans the same lines and inserts directly into a caller-supplied `ReferenceMap`. Nested blockquote and list-item reference collection now uses that helper directly against the shared map, removing the temporary map allocation and merge loop. The unused private map-returning wrapper was removed during fresh-eyes cleanup.
- Behavior proof: new focused tests pin that a top-level definition wins over nested duplicates, the first sibling nested definition wins over later siblings, and an outer nested definition wins over a deeper duplicate. Existing reference-definition boundary tests, parser conformance tests, parser fuzz/metamorphic tests, committed golden-output tests, and the full Rust suite passed.

Source tracing found that each page ran four separate capacity-only scans over the same placed lines before the actual page-content generation passes.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. The lever is small but directly inside the second-largest PDF generation stage: fuse background byte, body byte, link annotation, and structure-mark capacity estimates into one pass while preserving the existing formulas exactly.
- Page-content change: `estimate_page_content_capacity` now computes all four estimates in a single traversal and returns a `PageContentCapacityEstimate`. The old background/body/annotation/mark helper scans were removed. The main page loop still reserves the same capacities and emits the same body, background, annotations, marks, and structure tree.
- Behavior proof: `page_content_capacity_estimate_combines_legacy_counts` pins the fused formulas, including whitespace text counting as visible content, mono code chips requiring non-empty trimmed text, struck/linked text contributing to body capacity only when the text payload is non-empty, and linked zero-length segments still contributing to annotation capacity when they carry a positive width.

## Active Goal Continuation - Recorded SVG Alpha Resources
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T18:28:48Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-alpha-metadata-20260707T1815Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after the page-content capacity fusion pass, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-page-capacity-fusion-20260707T1805Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at 135.743 ms p95 and 135.034 ms mean. A focused source trace found that PDF serialization rebuilt SVG alpha `/ExtGState` resources by scanning every already-generated page stream for `/GSaNNNNNNNN gs` names, even though the renderer knows the exact alpha states at each operator emission site.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 3, score 2.7. The lever is modest but principled: replace a post-hoc byte scan over page content with resource metadata recorded at the write sites, then write the resource dictionary directly from that per-page set. The current `pdf-large` artifact has no SVG alpha resources, so this mainly removes unconditional common-case scan overhead and improves the correctness structure for SVG pages that do use opacity.
- PDF/SVG change: `PageContent` now stores a sorted per-page SVG alpha-state set. Alpha-state operator emission records into that set through one helper, and PDF page resource writing builds `/ExtGState` directly from the set instead of scanning `page.stream`; the PDF buffer estimate now accounts for those alpha resource entries alongside shading resources. The old scanner remains compiled only for tests as a compatibility oracle. Fresh-eyes lint review found the initial alpha-state threading had bloated several SVG helper signatures; the follow-up refactor introduced `SvgPageResources` for page-local shadings plus alpha states and `SvgPlacedMarker` for marker placement, removing the clippy argument-count failures without adding broad allow attributes.
- Behavior proof: new PDF writer tests pin direct alpha-state name/resource writers against the legacy format shape, including zero-padded and over-9999 names, and keep the scanner as a test-only oracle for name-boundary compatibility. Existing opacity, marker, gradient, pattern, SVG, PDF structure, golden-output, WASM, and corpus tests passed.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-alpha-metadata-20260707T1815Z` completed successfully. Representative stable payload artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-page-capacity-fusion-20260707T1805Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The targeted `page_content_stream_generation` stage moved from 87.297 ms total and 29.114 ms p95 to 80.244 ms total and 26.931 ms p95. `pdf_object_serialization_total` moved from 65.325 ms total and 22.116 ms p95 to 62.637 ms total and 20.953 ms p95. Whole `pdf-large` moved from 135.743 ms p95 and 135.034 ms mean to 132.626 ms p95 and 132.018 ms mean in this short run. Because this is a three-iteration sample and the large fixture has no `/GSa` resource names, the honest claim is byte-preserving removal of page-stream alpha rescans with favorable stage evidence, not a statistically broad latency guarantee.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `BlackDesert` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial sidecar review by `Sagan` identified the direct resource-metadata pass as the better next target; focused `cargo test --lib svg_alpha_state -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --lib pdf_writer_tests -- --nocapture`; focused `cargo test --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PDF RESOURCE-METADATA CLEANUP; this replaces an unconditional page-stream scan with first-class alpha-resource tracking at the SVG rendering sites, preserves exact rendered bytes, keeps the scanner only as a test oracle, adds no dependencies, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression remain dominant and broader SVG/Mermaid fidelity/performance work remains.

Source tracing found that top-level reference collection stripped consumed reference-definition lines, then immediately rescanned the kept line stream with `lines.iter().any(|line| line.contains("]:"))` only to decide whether the nested-reference collector might need to run.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. The optimization is a local redundant-scan removal: the existing strip pass already visits every kept line, so it can carry the "kept lines still contain a reference-definition candidate" bit out with the kept line vector.

- Behavior proof: the existing boundary-definition test now asserts that an unconsumed paragraph-continuation `[b]: /y` still reports a kept candidate, and a new test pins the opposite case where all boundary definitions are consumed and only non-candidate lines remain. ## Active Goal Continuation - Width Cache Entry Count
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T19:35:18Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-width-cache-count-20260707T1931Z/` and visual proof artifacts under `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/showcase-render-20260707T1929Z/` are proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `continue-quote-extents-gate-20260707T1921Z`, `pdf-large` remained dominant at 135.999 ms p95 and 135.004 ms mean. The PDF stage ledger showed `layout` at 232.494 ms total and 78.605 ms p95 across three iterations, with repeated text width cache misses inside paragraph, table, code, and list layout.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Source tracing found that `cached_shaped_width` summed `cache.values().map(HashMap::len).sum()` on every miss only to enforce the fixed cache cap. A render-local cache can carry the entry count incrementally, preserving the same cap and lookup keys while removing the full-cache count from the miss path.
- PDF layout change: `WidthCache` is now a tiny render-local wrapper around the same per-font-size shaped-width maps plus an entry counter. Cache hits return the same `LayoutUnit`; misses compute the same shaped width and insert the same `(slot, size, text)` entry while `len < WIDTH_CACHE_MAX`. Once the cap is reached, misses continue to compute without inserting exactly as before.
- Behavior proof: `width_cache_tracks_entry_count_and_reuses_widths` pins repeated-hit reuse, per-slot/per-text entry counting, and per-font-size slot length. The existing table, code-block, and list-marker cache reuse tests now assert through the wrapper API without loosening their expectations. Committed golden output and direct stable-payload byte comparisons stayed identical.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-width-cache-count-20260707T1931Z` completed successfully. Representative stable payload artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-quote-extents-gate-20260707T1921Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The targeted `layout` stage moved from 232.494 ms total and 78.605 ms p95 to 224.153 ms total and 75.314 ms p95. Whole `pdf-large` moved from 135.999 ms p95 and 135.004 ms mean to 134.261 ms p95 and 131.564 ms mean in this short run; unrelated parser and HTML scenarios drifted slower, so the honest durable claim is byte-preserving layout miss-path cleanup with favorable target evidence.
- Mermaid/showcase proof: `scripts/verify-showcase-mermaid.sh --run-id showcase-mermaid-visual-20260707T1928Z` regenerated the checked-in frankenmermaid SVG byte-for-byte. `cargo run --bin fmd -- render examples/showcase.md --to both --out tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/showcase-render-20260707T1929Z/showcase.html --json` wrote fresh showcase HTML/PDF. - Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-shaped-cache-slots-20260707T2006Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `continue-width-cache-count-20260707T1931Z`, `pdf-large` remained dominant at 134.261 ms p95 and 131.564 ms mean. The same stage ledger showed 43,533 shaped-segment cache hits, 1,425 misses, `glyph_collection_and_shaping` at 12.805 ms total, `page_content_stream_generation` at 83.939 ms total, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 63.293 ms total across three profiled renders.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Serial worker `Curie` found that `ShapedRunCache` used an outer `BTreeMap<u8, ...>` even though PDF font slots are a fixed five-value domain already mapped by `pdf_font_slot_index`. Replacing the outer tree with a five-bucket array removes repeated tree lookup/entry work while leaving each per-slot text-key map unchanged.
- PDF serialization change: `ShapedRunCache` is now `[BTreeMap<String, ShapedRun>; PDF_FONT_SLOT_COUNT]`. Glyph collection writes the slot cache through the existing `pdf_font_slot_index` bucket, and `draw_seg`/`draw_svg_text` read the same bucket before falling back to one-off shaping. Slot order, subset lookup, glyph shaping, ligature recording, PDF object order, layout, pagination, and emitted text operators are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: focused tests `profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages` and `pdf_reuses_shaped_segments_within_one_render_without_changing_bytes` passed. The committed golden-output test and direct stable-payload comparisons stayed byte-identical against `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-width-cache-count-20260707T1931Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-shaped-cache-slots-20260707T2006Z` completed successfully. `pdf-large` moved from 134.261 ms p95 and 131.564 ms mean to 133.580 ms p95 and 132.780 ms mean in this short run. The directly relevant `glyph_collection_and_shaping` stage moved from 12.805 ms total to 12.578 ms total, and `page_content_stream_generation` moved from 83.939 ms total to 80.606 ms total. `layout` was noisier/worse, so the durable claim is targeted shaped-cache lookup cleanup with exact output preservation and favorable stage evidence, not a statistically broad end-to-end guarantee.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `BlackDesert` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Curie`; focused `cargo test -q profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages`; focused `cargo test -q pdf_reuses_shaped_segments_within_one_render_without_changing_bytes`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; committed golden proof `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; full `cargo test`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE SHAPED-CACHE DATA-STRUCTURE CLEANUP; this removes an avoidable outer `BTreeMap` from hot PDF text shaping/drawing cache access with exact output preservation, no new dependencies, no unsafe code, and no WASM portability cost. - Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 2, score 4.0. Serial worker `Ramanujan` found a narrow table-delimiter lever: delimiter rows are already gated by `is_table_delimiter`, so escaped pipes and code-span pipes are invalid there. The parser can count delimiter cells and derive alignments with a direct pipe split instead of allocating an intermediate delimiter `Vec<&str>` through the full row splitter.

Header/body rows still use `split_table_row`, so escaped pipes, code spans, trimming, padding, truncation, and inline parsing rules for real cells are unchanged.

Existing table-row splitter tests, reference/table boundary tests, parser conformance, parser spans, parser fuzz/metamorphic/differential tests, committed HTML/PDF golden outputs, and the full Rust suite all passed. Direct stable-payload comparisons proved `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf` stayed byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-direct-index-20260707T2049Z/golden`.

The targeted `table_block` stage was effectively flat/noisy at 7.408 ms total and 6.101 us p95 versus 7.297 ms total and 6.121 us p95 before, while `reference_collection` improved and other parser stages drifted. The honest claim is therefore byte-preserving allocation cleanup in the table delimiter path with favorable whole-parser short-run evidence, not a statistically broad table-stage guarantee.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Base64 Byte Buffer
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T21:45:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` in release commit `1c6b387` and `.skill-loop-progress.md` in the follow-up ledger commit. HTML rendering has no separate stage ledger, but source tracing showed default self-contained HTML renders flow through `default_css -> embedded_font_css -> push_font_face -> base64_encode` for each embedded subset font.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. The lever is local and deterministic: Base64 output is ASCII bytes from a fixed table plus `=` padding, so the encoder can build a pre-sized byte buffer instead of pushing one Unicode scalar at a time into a `String`.
- HTML change: `base64_encode` now computes the exact encoded length, fills a `Vec<u8>` with the same four output bytes for each full 3-byte group, writes the same remainder padding, debug-asserts exact length and ASCII output, and converts with `String::from_utf8`. The existing known-vector test now also pins non-text/binary inputs across the one-byte, two-byte, and full-triplet paths.
- Behavior proof: output ordering, 6-bit index calculation, and padding positions are unchanged; no floating-point, RNG, time, dependency, unsafe, filesystem, process, thread, or native-runtime behavior is involved. `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture` passed, the full Rust suite passed, and representative stable artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-fnv-unroll-20260707T2128Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-html-base64-buffer-20260707T2145Z` completed successfully under an isolated `CARGO_TARGET_DIR`. In this short run, `html-large` moved from 13.036 ms p95 / 10.765 ms mean to 9.891 ms p95 / 8.855 ms mean, `html-code-heavy` moved from 2.307 ms p95 / 2.085 ms mean to 2.145 ms p95 / 1.975 ms mean, and `html-showcase` moved from 0.669 ms p95 / 0.538 ms mean to 0.596 ms p95 / 0.474 ms mean. The honest claim is byte-preserving HTML font-embedding encoder cleanup with favorable short-run HTML evidence, not a statistically broad renderer-speed guarantee.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `BlackDesert` for `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Boyle`; orchestrator review of `git show -- src/html.rs`; `cargo fmt --check`; focused `cargo test --lib html::tests::base64_encoder_matches_known_vectors -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --lib html::tests -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; `cargo check --no-default-features`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons. Rust verification used isolated `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` values to avoid stale shared-target artifacts.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE HTML ENCODER CLEANUP; this removes avoidable per-character `String::push` UTF-8 encoding work from the self-contained HTML font embedding path, preserves exact output bytes, adds no dependencies, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression remain dominant and the larger SVG/Mermaid renderer-quality objective still requires ongoing proof.

## Active Goal Continuation - Rejected PDF Decimal String Slice
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T22:04:00Z.
- Files changed this experiment: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. Serial worker `Plato` temporarily touched `src/pdf.rs` to replace the decimal digit append loops with a `std::str::from_utf8` slice append helper and to extend the related integer-writer boundary test; the orchestrator restored `src/pdf.rs` after profiling rejected the change. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-decimal-string-slice-20260707T2204Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `continue-html-base64-buffer-20260707T2145Z`, `pdf-large` was still the top scenario at 132.123 ms p95 and 131.028 ms mean. Its stage ledger showed `layout` at 226.177 ms total / 75.676 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 81.999 ms total / 27.592 ms p95, `page_stream_compression` at 52.716 ms total, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 63.157 ms total / 21.083 ms p95 across three renders.
- Opportunity matrix before test: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. The hypothesis was that `append_decimal_u64_string` and `append_decimal_usize_string` already produce ASCII digit buffers, so appending those buffers as a UTF-8 slice might reduce per-byte `String::push` overhead in PDF page-content and object writers. The implementation was byte-preserving by construction for generated decimal digits and kept the fallback path defensive.
- Result: rejected. The trial preserved every representative output byte, and focused integer-writer plus golden tests passed, but the target performance moved the wrong way. `pdf-large` regressed from 132.123 ms p95 / 131.028 ms mean to 140.864 ms p95 / 139.736 ms mean in the short gauntlet. The targeted `page_content_stream_generation` stage regressed from 81.999 ms total / 27.592 ms p95 to 87.940 ms total / 29.822 ms p95. `pdf_object_serialization_total` and `xref_trailer_writing` were effectively flat, so the minor serialization noise could not justify the slower hot page-content path.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `BlackDesert` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Plato`; focused trial-code checks `cargo test --lib pdf_writer_tests::string_decimal_and_signed_integer_writers_cover_boundaries -- --nocapture`, `cargo test --lib pdf_writer_tests::fixed_precision_pdf_number_writer_matches_legacy_format_policy -- --nocapture`, and `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `git diff --check`; full `cargo test`; short profile gauntlet `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-pdf-decimal-string-slice-20260707T2204Z`; direct stable-payload byte comparisons against `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-base64-buffer-20260707T2145Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. ## Active Goal Continuation - Single-Segment Final Width Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T22:57:19Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-single-seg-final-width-20260707T2255Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-ref-label-normalize-20260707T2240Z/`, `pdf-large` was the top scenario at 139.523 ms p95 and 138.651 ms mean. Within that scenario, `layout` dominated at 250.327 ms total and 85.299 ms p95 across three renders; `page_content_stream_generation` was 85.441 ms total / 28.948 ms p95, `page_stream_compression` was 54.451 ms total, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` was 65.784 ms total / 23.154 ms p95. Source tracing found that `build_segs_adjusted` remeasured every growing same-style text prefix to keep cross-token ligatures/kerning correct and to position later segments. A first broader attempt to defer all segment measurement preserved tests but changed committed PDF golden bytes because the old per-token f32 x-advance telescoping has observable rounding at later segment positions; that broader form was rejected and narrowed.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 2, score 4.0. The retained lever applies only when a physical line has one same-slot/same-link/same-strike segment and no justified-space extra advance. In that case there is no following segment whose x-position depends on old incremental f32 rounding, so measuring the final combined text once is byte-identical while avoiding transient prefix shaping/cache entries.
- PDF layout change: `build_segs_adjusted` now tries `build_single_adjusted_seg` first. The fast path validates that all `LineTok`s share the same style key and all `extra_advance` values are zero, concatenates the visible token text, shapes the final string once, and returns the same single `Seg` at the same left x. All multi-segment lines, link/strike/style transitions, and justified-space splits fall through to the old incremental code path unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `single_adjusted_segment_caches_only_final_shaped_text` pins the performance invariant by proving the width cache receives `fi` but not transient `f` for a same-style single segment. Existing `pdf_segments_remeasure_merged_text_after_cross_token_shaping` still pins whole-run shaping for cross-token ligatures, and `adjusted_segments_flush_justified_spaces_with_final_shaped_width` pins the fallback behavior for stretched spaces and the following segment's x-position. The committed golden-output test passed after the broader version was narrowed, and the full Rust suite passed.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-single-seg-final-width-20260707T2255Z` completed successfully under an isolated `CARGO_TARGET_DIR`. Representative stable payload artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-ref-label-normalize-20260707T2240Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The targeted `layout` stage moved from 250.327 ms total / 85.299 ms p95 to 238.009 ms total / 79.909 ms p95. `pdf-large` moved from 139.523 ms p95 / 138.651 ms mean to 137.515 ms p95 / 136.480 ms mean in this short run. `page_content_stream_generation` also moved favorably from 85.441 ms total / 28.948 ms p95 to 81.379 ms total / 27.254 ms p95, while `page_stream_compression` drifted slower from 54.451 ms total to 55.206 ms total. The honest durable claim is therefore byte-preserving removal of transient single-segment prefix shaping with favorable layout and whole-PDF short-run evidence, not a statistically broad suite-wide guarantee.

- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. The existing page-content capacity pass already walks every placed line before allocating the page buffers. Extending that pass with an exact inline-chip count lets the writer skip the later chip-background scan on pages where the count is zero, without adding another traversal or changing output order on pages where chips exist.
- Delegation: serial worker `GraySnow` implemented the bounded pass through subagent `Jason`. The orchestrator reviewed the worker diff and tightened the counter from "mono segment exists" to the writer's exact emission predicate: non-panel line, non-rule line, `F_MONO` slot, and non-empty trimmed text.
- PDF page-content change: `PageContentCapacityEstimate` now carries `mono_chips` and exposes `has_mono_chips()`. `estimate_page_content_capacity` increments the count only for segments that the inline-chip drawing loop can actually paint, and `serialize` uses that bit to bypass the chip loop when the page has none. Code panels, rules, text drawing, annotations, structure marks, quote backgrounds, table stripes, SVG drawing, compression, and object serialization are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `page_content_capacity_estimate_combines_legacy_counts` now pins a positive inline-chip page and a zero-chip page containing mono code-panel text, mono rule text, and plain body text. The test proves the skip predicate does not confuse code-panel mono text with inline-code chips and keeps the legacy buffer-capacity formulas intentional.

## Active Goal Continuation - Reference Consumed Range Stripping
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T23:52:40Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T2340Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-ref-ranges-20260707T2351Z/`, and SVG/showcase evidence under `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/showcase-mermaid-live-20260707T2344Z/` and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/showcase-render-live-20260707T2346Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh continuation profile ranked `pdf-large` first at 132.183 ms p95 / 131.244 ms mean, `parser-large` second at 18.394 ms p95 / 17.636 ms mean, and `html-large` third at 9.835 ms p95 / 8.974 ms mean. Parser stage attribution showed `reference_collection` at 10.529 ms total / 3.532 ms p95 with 109,578 counted allocations across the three-render parser scenario, making reference-definition stripping a small but concrete low-hanging parser allocation target.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 4, effort 2, score 6.0. The old collector allocated a dense `Vec<bool>` with one slot per source line, marked consumed reference-definition lines, then every stripping caller rescanned all lines to skip consumed entries. Reference definitions are discovered in forward order and normally occupy a tiny set of contiguous line runs, so storing coalesced consumed ranges preserves the same information while cutting the dense boolean allocation and per-line consumed scan.
- Parser change: `collect_link_reference_metadata` now returns coalesced `Range<usize>` values through `ConsumedReferenceLines`. `push_consumed_reference_range` merges adjacent or overlapping consumed definitions, `strip_consumed_references_with_candidate` walks only the non-consumed slices between ranges, and `strip_consumed_source_lines` applies the same range model to parser span collection. The table-boundary placeholder remains one inserted blank line per consumed run, with `consumed_reference_run_separates_tables` now checking the range start/end instead of rediscovering the run from a boolean vector.
- Behavior proof: the change preserves the forward reference scan, the first-definition-wins `BTreeMap::entry(...).or_insert(...)` policy, multiline reference definitions, table-boundary placeholders, nested blockquote/list reparsing, source-span stripping, and later reference lookup semantics. A new regression, `a_multiline_definition_between_adjacent_tables_preserves_the_table_boundary`, pins the exact case that would visibly fail if a multiline consumed range did not insert the single placeholder separating adjacent tables.
- Mermaid/showcase proof: live frankenmermaid regeneration matched the checked-in showcase SVG after rerunning with an isolated sibling-project `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` to avoid stale shared-target metadata. The current `fmd` binary rendered `examples/showcase.md` to HTML and PDF; PyMuPDF rasterized the PDF to page PNGs; visual inspection confirmed the page-2 Mermaid-derived SVG diagram was readable with sharp labels, visible edges, and sane markers, and page 3 confirmed syntax-highlighted code blocks remained visible. PDF text extraction also found the diagram/showcase labels on the rendered pages.
- Output/performance proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-ref-ranges-20260707T2351Z` completed successfully under an isolated `CARGO_TARGET_DIR`. Representative stable artifacts were byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T2340Z/golden` for `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`. The targeted `reference_collection` stage moved from 10.529 ms total / 3.532 ms p95 to 9.704 ms total / 3.293 ms p95. `parser-large` moved from 18.394 ms p95 / 17.636 ms mean to 17.837 ms p95 / 17.129 ms mean, while unrelated PDF/HTML samples were noisy in the same short run.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Lovelace`; orchestrator review of the parser diff; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges cargo test --lib refdef_paragraph_tests -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges cargo test --test parser_conformance reference -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges cargo test --test parser_spans -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges cargo test --test parser_metamorphic reference -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs`; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges-check cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges-clippy cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-ref-ranges-test cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PARSER ALLOCATION CLEANUP; this removes the dense consumed-line bitmap from reference-definition stripping while preserving exact output bytes, adding no dependencies, adding no unsafe code, and keeping WASM portability intact. ## Active Goal Continuation - Tab-Free Code Fit Measurement

- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Most source-code and Mermaid lines in the benchmark are tab-free, so the fit pass was allocating temporary strings whose bytes were identical to the original borrowed line.

Tab-free lines are measured directly as `&str`; tabbed lines still call `expand_code_tabs(line)` and measure the expanded string. The code-line order, `fold(max)` selection, width cache keys, tab expansion policy, line-number column handling, binary search, and code rendering path are otherwise unchanged.

Floating-point behavior is unchanged for tab-free lines because the measured byte sequence is the original line, which was exactly the string produced by the old no-tab `expand_code_tabs` path; tabbed lines retain the old expansion string. There is no RNG, time, dependency, unsafe code, filesystem, process, thread, native-runtime, or WASM-boundary behavior in the change.
