## Active Goal Continuation - Deflate BitWriter Capacity Hint
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T00:48:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260708T0015Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-baseline-20260708T0022Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-capacity-after-20260708T0034Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-capacity-after-100-20260708T0039Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh continuation profile ranked `pdf-large` first at 128.509 ms p95 / 128.300 ms mean, `parser-large` second at 17.931 ms p95, and `html-large` third at 9.953 ms p95. Within `pdf-large`, `layout` remained dominant at 221.929 ms total / 74.155 ms p95 across three renders, but support stages were still large enough to matter: `page_content_stream_generation` was 79.975 ms total, `pdf_object_serialization_total` was 61.610 ms total, and `page_stream_compression` was 52.950 ms total / 253.309 us p95 across 252 page streams. The standalone `compress-corpus` scenario was fifth at 4.677 ms p95.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. Serial worker `Schrodinger` identified that every fixed-Huffman deflate run started its bit writer with `Vec::new()`, then repeatedly grew while emitting page streams and compression-corpus payloads. The compressor already knows a deterministic fixed-Huffman body upper bound from the input length and, on the public `zlib_compress` path, a stored-block abort limit; using that as a capacity hint removes allocator work without changing the emitted bit sequence or the stored-vs-fixed decision.
- Compression change: `BitWriter::new` became `BitWriter::with_capacity`, and `deflate_fixed_with_limit` now initializes it with `fixed_body_capacity_hint(data.len(), abort_after_body_len)`. The hint uses `ceil((9 * input_len + 10) / 8)` as the worst-case single fixed-Huffman body size for literal emission plus the block header and end-of-block marker. When an abort limit is present, the hint caps allocation at `limit + FIXED_LIMIT_OVERSHOOT_BYTES`, where the four-byte overshoot covers one final emitted match token before the existing limit check returns the stored fallback path. Checksummed zlib headers, Adler-32, hash-chain matching, fixed/stored selection, PDF stream dictionaries, and all public APIs are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: the new unit test `fixed_deflate_capacity_hint_caps_abort_path_without_overflow` pins small-size bounds, checked-overflow behavior, and the abort-path cap. Existing compressor tests still prove stored fallback, fixed-body completion under a stored limit, external-style inflater round trips, dynamic/stored/fixed inflater support, malformed-stream rejection, length/distance table compatibility, and Adler-32 parity. Direct stable-payload comparisons proved `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf` stayed byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260708T0015Z/golden`; `pdf-large.pdf` stayed at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, and `compress-corpus.lengths` stayed at `b7dd39b697ecdbe9abb25d5983ca31d13999d2e68390879c804eb7b419ce4f33`.
- Output/performance proof: worker evidence from a short direct `pdf-large` stage sample moved `page_stream_compression` from 52.950 ms total / 253.309 us p95 to 51.382 ms total / 247.819 us p95 with the same 252 streams and same compressed output byte totals. The orchestrator's independent short whole-gauntlet sample preserved exact bytes but was noisy in the target stage (`page_stream_compression` 53.412 ms total / 257.537 us p95) and whole `pdf-large` p95 drifted to 131.315 ms while unrelated HTML/parser samples also moved; no broad whole-PDF win is claimed from that run. A longer 100-iteration post-change `compress-corpus` sample was cleaner at 4.415 ms p50, 4.475 ms p95, and 4.981 ms p99, versus the fresh continuation profile's 4.677 ms p95 and a 20-iteration pre-change baseline p95 of 5.034 ms. The honest durable claim is byte-preserving removal of avoidable deflate output reallocations with favorable focused compressor evidence, not a statistically universal end-to-end PDF latency guarantee.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Schrodinger`; orchestrator review of the `src/compress.rs` diff and capacity math; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-review cargo fmt --check`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-review cargo test --lib compress::tests`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs`; focused compression profile before and after; short profile gauntlet; direct stable-payload byte comparisons; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-review cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-review cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-review cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-review cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE COMPRESSION ALLOCATION CLEANUP; this pre-sizes the internal fixed-Huffman bitstream buffer from deterministic limits, preserves exact compressed and rendered bytes, adds no dependencies, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/serialization/compression remain dominant and the full requested optimization/SVG-completion objective is larger than this single accepted pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - Classic Xref Offset Pair Writer
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T01:10:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-xref-pair-writer-after-20260708T0051Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-capacity-after-20260708T0034Z/`, `pdf-large` remained the top scenario at 131.315 ms p95 / 130.835 ms mean. Its support-stage ledger still showed `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 62.139 ms total / 20.760 ms p95, `xref_trailer_writing` at 5.744 ms total / 1.919 ms p95 across three renders, and `page_stream_compression` at 53.412 ms total. The first investigated idea, hashing the PDF pre-trailer bytes once for both file-ID halves, was rejected because the second hash is intentionally seeded with the final first hash before scanning the same bytes and a naive simultaneous scan is not byte-equivalent.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. Serial worker `Erdos` found a safer one-lever writer cleanup in classic xref row emission: `append_xref_offset` formatted offsets by repeatedly dividing by ten into a temporary digit suffix and then looping to prepend zero padding. Normal PDF xref offsets are defined as ten-digit fields and remain below 10,000,000,000 in this renderer, so the common path can write exactly ten bytes using two-digit decimal pairs. The legacy fallback remains for larger offsets, preserving the old unpadded decimal shape.
- PDF writer change: `append_xref_offset` now uses a fixed ten-byte buffer and a 00..99 pair table for offsets below `CLASSIC_XREF_OFFSET_LIMIT`. It fills the buffer from the end in five base-100 steps and appends it directly. Offsets at or above the limit call `append_decimal_usize`, matching the previous behavior when the decimal digit count already exceeded the classic ten-digit field. Xref row spacing, object offsets, trailer contents, deterministic file ID generation, PDF object serialization order, layout, page content, compression, and public APIs are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: the focused `xref_writer_uses_classic_ten_digit_padding` test now pins `0`, `42`, `1_234_567_890`, `9_999_999_999`, and the fallback boundary `10_000_000_000`, while `xref_row_writer_preserves_pdf_spacing` still pins the complete row suffix. The trailer determinism test passed, the committed golden-output test passed, and direct comparison proved `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-capacity-after-20260708T0034Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf` with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. There is no new dependency, unsafe code, RNG, time, filesystem behavior, process use, or WASM portability change.
- Output/performance proof: a 20-iteration direct `pdf-large` profile completed successfully and proved all 20 profiled renders matched normal PDF bytes exactly. Its `xref_trailer_writing` stage was 37.938 ms total, 1.901 ms p50, and 1.930 ms p95 across 20 renders. Compared with the prior 3-render baseline of 5.744 ms total / 1.919 ms p95 and the worker's 20-render sample of 37.992 ms total / 1.933 ms p95, this is effectively flat/noise-level rather than a clean p95 win. The honest durable claim is a byte-preserving deterministic writer simplification that removes a small amount of repeated decimal-formatting work from xref emission, not a broad end-to-end PDF speedup.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Erdos`; orchestrator review of the `src/pdf.rs` diff and the rejected file-ID one-pass risk; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo fmt --check`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo test --lib xref_`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_trailer_has_deterministic_content_sensitive_file_id`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens`; 20-iteration direct `pdf-large` profile; direct `pdf-large.pdf` byte/hash comparison; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-xref-review cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PDF XREF WRITER CLEANUP; this makes classic xref offset emission fixed-width on the common path while preserving exact PDF bytes, adding no dependencies, adding no unsafe code, and keeping WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/serialization/compression remain dominant and the requested optimization/SVG-completion objective is larger than this single pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - Unified Font Slot Text References
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T01:06:46Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphrefs-after-20260708T0114Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-xref-pair-writer-after-20260708T0051Z/`, `pdf-large` remained the top scenario. In the 20-render profile, support stages included `glyph_collection_and_shaping` at 83.073 ms total / 3.650 ms p95, `heading_metadata` at 8.630 ms total / 597 us p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 522.894 ms total, `page_stream_compression` at 340.461 ms total, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 398.299 ms total. The next low-risk target was glyph-reference collection rather than the main layout algorithm.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. Serial worker `Chandrasekhar` found that `FontSlotTextRefs` stored separate `Vec<&Seg>` and `Vec<&SvgText>` collections for each font slot even though the glyph-collection stage only needed borrowed text slices. That also forced duplicate cache/shape/collect loops for normal line segments and SVG text. Unifying to one `Vec<&str>` per font slot removes five extra vectors and one duplicated shaping loop body without changing the downstream shaped-run cache keys or the text bytes being shaped.
- PDF glyph-collection change: `FontSlotTextRefs` now contains one `texts: Vec<&str>`. `collect_font_slot_text_refs` first collects all non-empty normal segment text slices by font slot, then collects all non-empty SVG text slices by font slot. The two-pass ordering deliberately preserves the old effective glyph-collection order, which was all stored segment refs followed by all stored SVG text refs for a slot. The shaping/subsetting loop now iterates `slot_refs.texts` once and uses each text slice for character collection, shaped-run cache lookup, shaping, glyph collection, and cache insertion.
- Fresh-eyes correction: the first worker patch interleaved SVG text after each line's segments. That matched the collection loop shape but not the old effective processing order, because the previous serializer consumed `slot_refs.segs` to completion before `slot_refs.svg_texts`. The orchestrator corrected the patch before acceptance and added focused coverage for the legacy order. This matters because `BTreeMap::entry(...).or_insert_with(...)` keeps the first ToUnicode source string for a ligature glyph if a future font maps multiple sequences to the same glyph id.
- Behavior proof: new focused test `font_slot_text_refs_preserve_legacy_segment_then_svg_order` pins normal segment refs before SVG text refs across multiple lines, skips empty SVG text, and keeps slot assignment for body, bold, and mono text. The committed golden-output test passed, the profiled-PDF normal-byte test passed, full tests passed, and direct comparison proved `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-xref-pair-writer-after-20260708T0051Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf` with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. There is no public API, dependency, unsafe, filesystem, process, RNG, time, or WASM portability change.
- Output/performance proof: after the corrected order-preserving patch, a 20-iteration direct `pdf-large` profile completed successfully and proved all 20 profiled renders matched normal PDF bytes exactly. Whole `pdf-large` measured 129.734 ms p50 / 132.020 ms p95. The targeted `glyph_collection_and_shaping` stage was 82.926 ms total / 3.648 ms p95 over 20 renders, versus 83.073 ms total / 3.650 ms p95 in the previous 20-render profile. This is effectively flat with a tiny favorable movement; the honest durable claim is byte-preserving reduction of internal reference-vector count and duplicated loop code, not a statistically meaningful end-to-end speedup.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass by `Chandrasekhar`; orchestrator review plus order correction; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo fmt --check`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo test font_slot_text_refs_preserve_legacy_segment_then_svg_order`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens`; 20-iteration direct `pdf-large` profile; direct `pdf-large.pdf` byte/hash comparison; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-glyphrefs-review cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PDF GLYPH-COLLECTION CLEANUP; this unifies per-slot text references into one borrowed-slice list, removes duplicated segment/SVG shaping loop code, preserves exact PDF bytes, adds no dependencies, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression/serialization remain dominant and the requested optimization/SVG-completion objective is larger than this single pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - Rejected Heading Metadata Cursor
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T03:24:00Z.
- Files changed this experiment: none retained in source. The only retained change is this ledger entry. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/heading-meta-baseline-20260708T011340Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-heading-meta-after-20260708T0315Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-heading-meta-after-rerun-20260708T0320Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphrefs-after-20260708T0114Z/`, `heading_metadata` was a small but visible PDF support stage at 8.490 ms total / 0.556 ms p95 across 20 renders, while `page_content_stream_generation` was 520.895 ms total / 26.707 ms p95.
- Hypothesis: preserve the full heading pre-scan semantics for wrapped-heading titles and duplicate-title IDs, but return ordered heading metadata and advance a page-loop cursor instead of storing metadata in a `BTreeMap<u32, HeadingMeta>` and tracking emitted outline groups with a `BTreeSet<u32>`. This looked correct because `pages_placed` preserves document line order and repeated table headers do not repeat headings.
- Result: rejected. The trial preserved exact PDF bytes and focused edge tests passed, but the performance evidence was not good enough to keep it. The first patched 20-render run kept `pdf-large.pdf` byte-identical at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, but `page_content_stream_generation` moved to 575.446 ms total / 33.962 ms p95 and whole `pdf-large` measured 140.347 ms p95. A rebuild-free rerun improved the small targeted `heading_metadata` stage slightly to 8.344 ms total / 0.539 ms p95, but `page_content_stream_generation` was still 526.609 ms total / 28.802 ms p95 and whole `pdf-large` was 145.663 ms p95. That is not a defensible accepted optimization.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker `Aristotle` did read-only baseline profiling because the reservation was active; orchestrator trial patch in `src/pdf.rs`; focused tests for duplicate heading IDs, wrapped-heading title accumulation before ID generation, and cursor non-advancement on same-group continuation/rule lines; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-heading-meta-review cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-heading-meta-review cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; two direct 20-iteration `pdf-large` profiles; direct byte/hash comparisons against `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphrefs-after-20260708T0114Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf`; source patch backed out; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` verified empty.
- Verdict: REJECTED HYPOTHESIS; avoid retrying the ordered-heading-cursor shape unless a deeper profile shows outline emission itself, not the broader page-content stream generation loop, has become a material bottleneck. The existing `BTreeMap` + `BTreeSet` path remains preferable because it is simple, byte-stable, and not measurably worse under current evidence.

## Active Goal Continuation - Rejected Single-Byte Shaped Width Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T03:48:00Z.
- Files changed this experiment: none retained in source. The only retained change is this ledger entry. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-single-width-after-20260708T0330Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-single-width-narrow-after-20260708T0339Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-single-width-narrow-rerun-20260708T0345Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Hypothesis: `Face::shaped_width` could bypass glyph-vector allocation and GSUB substitution for a one-character string because a single scalar cannot ligate or kern with a neighbor. The first trial handled all single Unicode scalars; after it measured poorly, the second trial narrowed the fast path to one-byte ASCII only so multi-character text paid only a byte-length check.
- Result: rejected. Both trial shapes preserved exact `pdf-large.pdf` bytes with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, and focused tests proved `A`, space, and hyphen matched direct glyph advances while `fi` still used the GSUB ligature path. The broad single-scalar version regressed the target stages. The narrowed ASCII version had one favorable sample (`layout` 1495.635 ms total / 80.530 ms p95 and `glyph_collection_and_shaping` 77.928 ms total / 3.554 ms p95, versus the previous 1554.153 ms / 81.473 ms and 82.926 ms / 3.648 ms), but the rebuild-free rerun regressed the same target stages (`layout` 1575.777 ms total / 85.410 ms p95 and `glyph_collection_and_shaping` 84.450 ms total / 4.220 ms p95). That instability is not enough to justify keeping branch complexity in the primitive shaping helper.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused tests `single_character_shaped_width_uses_direct_glyph_advance_only`, then after narrowing `single_byte_shaped_width_uses_direct_glyph_advance_only`; focused ligature regression `pdf_word_measurement_uses_gsub_ligature_advances`; `cargo fmt --check`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-single-width-review cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-single-width-review cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; direct profile and byte comparisons for the broad and narrowed trials; source patch backed out; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` verified empty.
- Verdict: REJECTED HYPOTHESIS; avoid retrying a single-character `Face::shaped_width` branch unless a microbenchmark or allocation profile proves single-byte cache misses dominate. The generic glyph-vector + GSUB path remains simpler and more predictable under current evidence.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Base64 Exact Fill Buffer
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T04:12:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-base64-fill-after-20260708T0355Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-base64-fill-rerun-20260708T0400Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-base64-fill-gauntlet-20260708T0405Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after the fresh continuation profile, `html-large` was the leading non-PDF/non-parser scenario at 9.953 ms p95 / 9.299 ms mean across the canonical short run. HTML renders embed deterministic subset fonts through `push_font_face -> base64_encode`, and the previous accepted Base64 pass had already moved the encoder from scalar `String::push` to an ASCII byte buffer.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The remaining local lever was to fill the exact encoded byte length directly instead of repeatedly calling `Vec::extend_from_slice` into a merely pre-capacity-reserved vector. Base64 output length is known from input length, and every output byte comes from a fixed ASCII table or `=` padding, so the direct-fill shape is deterministic and dependency-free.
- HTML change: `base64_encode` now allocates `vec![0u8; encoded_len]`, writes each four-byte group by index, writes one- and two-byte tail padding by index, and debug-asserts that the final write cursor equals `encoded_len`. The alphabet, bit slicing, padding placement, `String::from_utf8` conversion, fallback path, font subsetting, CSS ordering, public APIs, and all rendered output bytes are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `base64_encoder_matches_known_vectors` passed for empty input, every one-/two-/three-byte remainder class, and binary bytes. The committed golden-output test passed. Direct stable-payload comparison against `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260708T0015Z/golden` proved `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf` remained byte-identical; `html-large.html` stayed at SHA-256 `0ca75f7e2044f748e0ff53ee43c52442a703dfeff6d41dd06f2b4a0ad89f1389`.
- Output/performance proof: a focused 100-iteration `html-large` run measured 7.929 ms p50 / 11.086 ms p95 / 8.363 ms mean, and its rebuild-free rerun measured 7.672 ms p50 / 10.331 ms p95 / 7.975 ms mean. The canonical short gauntlet measured `html-large` at 9.270 ms p50 / 9.997 ms p95 / 8.941 ms mean, `html-code-heavy` at 1.919 ms p50 / 1.948 ms p95, and `pdf-large` at 128.215 ms p50 / 129.385 ms p95. The honest claim is byte-preserving removal of small repeated vector-extension work from HTML font embedding with favorable p50/mean focused evidence, not a statistically guaranteed p95 win.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-fill cargo test --lib base64_encoder_matches_known_vectors -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-fill cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; focused 100-iteration `html-large` profile and rebuild-free rerun; short profile gauntlet `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-gauntlet scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-html-base64-fill-gauntlet-20260708T0405Z`; direct stable-payload byte comparisons; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs`; `cargo fmt --check`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-check cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-clippy cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-test cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE HTML ENCODER CLEANUP; this writes Base64 font data into a single exact-size buffer, preserves exact output bytes, adds no dependencies, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression/serialization, parser-large, and the requested optimization/SVG-completion objective remain larger than this pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - Short Fixed Deflate Literal Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T01:51:54Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-short-after-20260708T0143Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-short-rerun-20260708T0143Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-short-gauntlet-20260708T0143Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted. A detached pre-patch comparison worktree was created at `/data/tmp/fmd-baseline-compress-short-20260708T0143Z` from committed `HEAD` solely to build an apples-to-apples baseline.
- Current profile context: the fresh continuation profile ranked `compress-corpus` as a smaller but visible scenario at 4.677 ms p95, while `pdf-large`, `parser-large`, and `html-large` remained larger. Source tracing found that `deflate_fixed_with_limit` always allocated the 32768-entry hash head table plus a per-input predecessor vector even for 0-, 1-, and 2-byte inputs. DEFLATE's minimum match length is 3, so those inputs can never use the LZ77 hash chain; the old path could only emit literals followed by EOB after paying the setup cost.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. This is not a broad document-rendering speedup by itself, but it removes an extreme allocation cliff from tiny image/stream/test payload compression and from any future call site that emits many small Flate streams.
- Compression change: after writing the fixed-Huffman final-block header and honoring the existing body-length abort check, `deflate_fixed_with_limit` now directly emits literals for inputs shorter than `MIN_MATCH`, checks the same abort limit after each literal, updates Adler-32 in the same order, emits EOB, pads the final byte, and returns. Inputs of length 3 or more still allocate and use the existing hash-chain LZ77 path unchanged.
- Behavior proof: before patching, the committed encoder produced raw fixed bodies `[3, 0]` for empty input, `[75, 4, 0]` for `a`, and `[75, 76, 2, 0]` for `ab`. The new regression `fixed_deflate_short_inputs_keep_exact_fixed_body_bytes` pins those exact bodies, confirms the zlib wrapper still chooses fixed-Huffman bodies for those inputs, checks Adler-32 equality, and round-trips through the production inflater. All 23 compressor unit tests passed, the committed golden-output test passed, and direct stable-payload comparisons proved `html-showcase.html`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `pdf-large.pdf`, `paragraph-1k.breaks`, `hyphen-corpus.points`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf` stayed byte-identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260708T0015Z/golden`.
- Output/performance proof: the broad `compress-corpus` scenario stayed byte-identical at SHA-256 `b7dd39b697ecdbe9abb25d5983ca31d13999d2e68390879c804eb7b419ce4f33`. Its 100-iteration direct runs measured 4.898 ms p95 / 4.507 ms mean and then 5.051 ms p95 / 4.501 ms mean, which is noise-level and not claimed as a broad win. The canonical short gauntlet measured `compress-corpus` at 4.559 ms p95 / 4.537 ms mean and `pdf-large` at 135.501 ms p95 / 134.160 ms mean. The targeted short-stream microbenchmark, using the same release-perf profile and 5,000,000 calls over `""`, `"a"`, and `"ab"`, moved from pre-patch samples of 17.705 s, 17.296 s, and 17.861 s to patched samples of 206.599 ms, 206.839 ms, and 204.647 ms with the same total compressed length. The honest durable claim is therefore elimination of a tiny-stream allocation cliff with exact output preservation, not an end-to-end document render speedup.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; pre-patch byte capture through a throwaway Rust stdin program linked against the clean committed library; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short cargo test --lib fixed_deflate_short_inputs_keep_exact_fixed_body_bytes -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short cargo test --lib fixed_deflate_limit -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs`; 100-iteration direct `compress-corpus` profile and rebuild-free rerun; same-profile pre/post tiny-stream microbenchmark; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short cargo test --lib compress::tests -- --nocapture`; committed golden proof `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; short profile gauntlet `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short-gauntlet scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-compress-short-gauntlet-20260708T0143Z`; direct stable-payload byte comparisons; final `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; final `cargo fmt --check`; final `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short-check cargo check --all-targets`; final `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; final `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short-clippy cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-compress-short-test cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE COMPRESSOR MICRO-PATH CLEANUP; this avoids impossible LZ77 setup for sub-three-byte fixed-Huffman inputs, preserves exact zlib/PDF/HTML output bytes, adds no dependency, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression/serialization and parser-large still dominate the system profile.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Layout Output Capacity Hint
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T02:11:44Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-out-cap-after-20260708T020721Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-out-cap-rerun-20260708T020721Z/`, and detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/fmd-baseline-layout-out-cap-20260708T020721Z` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after the short fixed-deflate pass, `pdf-large` remained the dominant scenario at 135.501 ms p95 / 134.160 ms mean in the canonical short gauntlet. Its stage evidence still showed `layout` as the top stage at 233.566 ms total / 78.195 ms p95 across three renders, and later direct 20-render evidence showed the same stage around 1.63 s total across 20 renders.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The PDF layout pass appends physical `Line` records to an initially empty vector. The profiled large document has about three laid-out lines per parsed block, so the vector grows through repeated reallocation on the hottest PDF stage even though a cheap block-count estimate is available before layout starts.
- PDF layout change: `layout` now creates the output line buffer with `Vec::with_capacity(blocks.len().checked_mul(3).unwrap_or(blocks.len()))`. The factor is only a capacity hint; line ordering, pagination, text shaping, table layout, image handling, PDF serialization, public APIs, and output bytes are unchanged. The overflow path deliberately falls back to the block count instead of using saturating multiplication, so an impossible giant input does not turn the hint into a maximum-capacity allocation request.
- Behavior proof: focused PDF profile-vs-normal and committed golden-output tests passed, and direct `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparisons against the detached baseline stayed byte-identical at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1` for both the first 20-iteration run and the rebuild-free 50-iteration rerun.
- Output/performance proof: the first apples-to-apples 20-iteration run was mixed, with baseline `pdf-large` at 134.991 ms p50 / 147.188 ms p95 / 135.910 ms mean and the patched tree at 138.224 ms p50 / 146.064 ms p95 / 137.532 ms mean. Its layout stage p95 improved from 88.807 ms to 87.295 ms, but layout total was effectively flat/slightly worse, so that sample alone was not enough. A rebuild-free 50-iteration rerun was favorable: baseline `pdf-large` measured 138.864 ms p50 / 146.825 ms p95 / 139.374 ms mean, while the patched tree measured 135.015 ms p50 / 140.492 ms p95 / 135.240 ms mean. In that rerun, the targeted `layout` stage moved from 3.999918 s total / 85.641 ms p95 to 3.989194 s total / 84.279 ms p95 across 50 renders. The honest durable claim is therefore a byte-preserving line-buffer allocation hint with favorable rebuild-free layout and whole-PDF evidence, not a statistically guaranteed win for every document shape.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-layout-out-cap-golden cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-layout-out-cap-pdftest cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture`; detached baseline worktree from committed `HEAD`; direct 20-iteration baseline and patched `pdf-large` profiles; direct stage comparisons; direct SHA-256 comparisons; rebuild-free 50-iteration baseline and patched reruns with stage and SHA-256 comparisons.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PDF LAYOUT ALLOCATION CLEANUP; this gives the hottest layout output buffer a corpus-backed initial capacity, preserves exact output bytes, adds no dependency, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page-content/compression/serialization and parser-large still dominate the system profile.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Tokenizer Slice Words
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T02:21:57Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-token-slice-after-20260708T021715Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-token-slice-gauntlet-20260708T021715Z/`, and detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/fmd-baseline-token-slice-20260708T021715Z` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after the layout output capacity hint, the profiler still recommended layout/page-content scratch and buffer work. Source tracing found `push_text_tokens` building every PDF word by repeatedly pushing chars into a temporary `String`, then moving that finished string into a `Tok`. This happens for headings, paragraphs, table cells, raw HTML text, list item leading paragraphs, and image alt fallback text before paragraph building and width measurement.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The tokenizer already scans the UTF-8 input by scalar value to apply the shared breakable-whitespace policy, so it can keep byte offsets from `char_indices()` and clone each final word directly from the original string slice. That removes incremental per-character word-buffer growth while preserving one empty payload token per breakable whitespace scalar.
- PDF tokenizer change: `push_text_tokens` now tracks `word_start`, emits `text[word_start..idx].to_string()` at each breakable whitespace boundary, pushes the same empty-payload break token as before, and emits the trailing slice once at EOF. Non-breaking spaces remain inside the surrounding word because the implementation still calls `is_breakable_whitespace`; links, strike flags, font slots, soft/hard break handling, table wrapping, line breaking, and rendered bytes are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: new focused coverage `pdf_text_tokenizer_slices_words_and_preserves_whitespace_policy` pins tab splitting, repeated spaces, empty whitespace payloads, and non-breaking space retention inside a word. Existing whitespace/segment tests `pdf_space_tokens_store_empty_payloads_but_segments_render_spaces` and `pdf_soft_break_tokens_render_one_space_but_hard_breaks_do_not` passed. Focused committed golden-output and profiled-PDF-vs-normal tests passed, and direct `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparisons against the detached baseline stayed byte-identical at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Output/performance proof: direct apples-to-apples 50-iteration `pdf-large` moved from baseline 134.991 ms p50 / 142.304 ms p95 / 135.408 ms mean to patched 133.124 ms p50 / 137.836 ms p95 / 133.321 ms mean. The targeted `layout` stage moved from 3.963979 s total / 84.251 ms p95 to 3.910792 s total / 80.283 ms p95 across 50 renders; `glyph_collection_and_shaping` moved from 212.110 ms total / 3.722 ms p95 to 195.035 ms total / 3.383 ms p95. `page_content_stream_generation` drifted slower in the same run, so the honest claim is a byte-preserving tokenizer/layout improvement with favorable end-to-end PDF evidence, not an improvement to every downstream stage. The short gauntlet passed with stable payload hashes: `pdf-large.pdf` stayed `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, `html-large.html` stayed `0ca75f7e2044f748e0ff53ee43c52442a703dfeff6d41dd06f2b4a0ad89f1389`, `compress-corpus.lengths` stayed `b7dd39b697ecdbe9abb25d5983ca31d13999d2e68390879c804eb7b419ce4f33`, and `font-subset.ttf` stayed `39b2e7428ecfcedc3df5fb15830df6ceed4b1eca6718b61928150b1754310bae`.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-token-slice-focused cargo test --lib pdf_text_tokenizer_slices_words_and_preserves_whitespace_policy -- --nocapture`; focused existing whitespace tests; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-token-slice-golden cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-token-slice-pdftest cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture`; detached baseline worktree from committed `HEAD`; direct 50-iteration baseline and patched `pdf-large` profiles; direct stage and SHA-256 comparisons; short profile gauntlet `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-token-slice-gauntlet scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-token-slice-gauntlet-20260708T021715Z`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PDF TOKENIZATION CLEANUP; this replaces incremental word-buffer growth with UTF-8-safe string slicing, preserves exact output bytes, adds no dependency, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM portability intact. ## Active Goal Continuation - Rejected Reference Collector Single-Pass Scan
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T02:31:43Z.

Because `reference_collector_plain_line_fast_path` already rejects indented code before calling this helper, the trial tracked the first non-space byte and the tail start while scanning for tabs, pipes, and `]:`, then used the same first-byte dispatch for block-open candidates.

Direct 100-iteration `parser-large` moved from baseline 17.292 ms p50 / 18.107 ms p95 / 17.333 ms mean to patched 17.575 ms p50 / 17.807 ms p95 / 17.585 ms mean: p95 was lower, but p50 and mean regressed. Focused `reference_collector_fast_path_ignores_inline_only_punctuation` and `line_classifier_distinguishes_text_from_block_openers` passed, as did full `parser_conformance` and committed `golden_output`.

- Verdict: REJECTED HYPOTHESIS; keep the existing leading-indent plus byte-scan shape for `reference_collector_needs_block_scan`. The extra state in the combined pass appears to cost more than the avoided leading-indent pass on the current generated parser corpus.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Shaped Cache HashMap
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T02:40:36Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-shaped-hash-after-20260708T023505Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-shaped-hash-gauntlet-20260708T023505Z/`, and detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/fmd-baseline-shaped-hash-20260708T023505Z` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after the PDF tokenizer slice pass, `pdf-large` still dominated. Source tracing found the per-render shaped glyph cache used `BTreeMap<String, ShapedRun>` per font slot even though the cache is lookup-only: it is populated during glyph collection, read during later drawing, and never iterated to determine object order or output bytes.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. The cache has many repeated exact segment texts (`shaped_segment_cache_hit` work_count 725,550 across the 50-render run) and only 23,750 misses. A hash table is a better fit for lookup-only reuse, and sizing each font-slot cache from `slot_texts[slot_idx].texts.len()` avoids growth churn during population. Determinism is preserved because output order comes from laid-out lines, subset char BTreeSets, object vectors, and explicit serialization order, not from shaped-cache iteration.
- PDF serialization change: `ShapedRunCache` is now `[HashMap<String, ShapedRun>; PDF_FONT_SLOT_COUNT]`, initialized with `HashMap::with_capacity(slot_texts[slot_idx].texts.len())` for each slot. Glyph collection, shaping, subset seeding, ToUnicode ligature mapping, page-content drawing, public APIs, feature gates, and rendered bytes are otherwise unchanged.
- Behavior proof: focused shaped-cache reuse coverage `pdf_reuses_shaped_segments_within_one_render_without_changing_bytes` passed, as did committed golden-output and profiled-PDF-vs-normal tests. Direct `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparisons against the detached baseline stayed byte-identical at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. The short gauntlet preserved the same stable payload hashes for `pdf-large.pdf`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Output/performance proof: direct apples-to-apples 50-iteration `pdf-large` moved from baseline 131.580 ms p50 / 139.284 ms p95 / 132.771 ms mean to patched 126.976 ms p50 / 131.876 ms p95 / 127.385 ms mean. The most direct target, `glyph_collection_and_shaping`, moved from 193.722 ms total / 3.390 ms p95 to 170.932 ms total / 3.039 ms p95 across 50 renders. The same run also showed favorable downstream samples: `layout` 3.871 s total / 80.301 ms p95 to 3.682 s total / 75.301 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` 1.358 s total / 28.293 ms p95 to 1.302 s total / 26.332 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` 1.014 s total / 21.849 ms p95 to 0.999 s total / 20.177 ms p95. The honest durable claim is faster lookup-heavy shaped-run reuse with exact output preservation; downstream stage wins are favorable samples, not a new semantic dependency.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-shaped-hash-focused cargo test --test pdf_embed_test pdf_reuses_shaped_segments_within_one_render_without_changing_bytes -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-shaped-hash-golden cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-shaped-hash-pdftest cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture`; detached baseline worktree from committed `HEAD`; direct 50-iteration baseline and patched `pdf-large` profiles; direct stage and SHA-256 comparisons; short profile gauntlet `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-shaped-hash-gauntlet scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-shaped-hash-gauntlet-20260708T023505Z`.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Incremental Page-Break Scoring
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T02:54:45Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pagebreak-after-20260708T024716Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pagebreak-gauntlet-20260708T024716Z/`, and detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/fmd-baseline-pagebreak-20260708T024716Z` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: after the shaped-cache cleanup, `pdf-large` still dominated. Source tracing found `choose_page_break` scanning the candidate range once to find `last_fit`, then scoring every candidate by recomputing `vertical_height(&lines[start..candidate])`. That made candidate scoring quadratic in the number of lines considered for each page even though the score only needs the prefix height that the loop can accumulate once.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The profiler shows pagination is already a small slice of `pdf-large`, so this is a principled micro-optimization rather than a major end-to-end win. It still removes unnecessary repeated summing from a page-builder loop that will matter more as keep/widow scoring grows.
- PDF pagination change: `choose_page_break` now accumulates `candidate_used` as it walks candidates and passes that value to `break_score_for_used_height`. `break_penalty`, fill-badness math, repeated table header handling, chosen break semantics, placed line geometry, public APIs, feature gates, and rendered bytes are otherwise unchanged. The now-unused `vertical_height` helper was removed.
- Behavior proof: new focused unit coverage `page_break_scoring_prefers_the_fullest_unpenalized_fit` pins the scoring path on a controlled page-height fixture. Focused profiled-PDF-vs-normal and committed golden-output tests passed. Direct `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparisons against the detached baseline stayed byte-identical at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. The short gauntlet preserved stable payload hashes for `pdf-large.pdf`, `pdf-showcase.pdf`, `html-large.html`, `html-code-heavy.html`, `parser-large.html`, `compress-corpus.lengths`, and `font-subset.ttf`.
- Output/performance proof: direct apples-to-apples 50-iteration `pdf-large` moved from baseline 128.945 ms p50 / 137.987 ms p95 / 130.684 ms mean to patched 130.825 ms p50 / 131.972 ms p95 / 130.710 ms mean. The p50/mean end-to-end samples are neutral-to-noisy, but the targeted `pagination` stage improved from 6.443 ms total / 118.474 us p50 / 165.413 us p95 to 3.411 ms total / 66.646 us p50 / 94.829 us p95 across 50 renders. The honest durable claim is lower page-break scoring work with exact output preservation, not a broad end-to-end throughput improvement.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservation as `NobleSnow` for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-pagebreak-unit cargo test page_break_scoring_prefers_the_fullest_unpenalized_fit -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-pagebreak-focused cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-pagebreak-golden cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens -- --nocapture`; detached baseline worktree from committed `HEAD`; direct 50-iteration baseline and patched `pdf-large` profiles; direct stage and SHA-256 comparisons; short profile gauntlet `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-pagebreak-gauntlet scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-pagebreak-gauntlet-20260708T024716Z`.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Baseline Shift Text
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T03:42:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. SVG/showcase evidence under `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-visual-20260708T0325Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current SVG context: the renderer already supports selectable SVG text, `tspan`, `dx`/`dy`, dominant-baseline, text-anchor, letter-spacing, textLength, transforms, opacity, CSS variables, and style cascade. A missing text-positioning property was `baseline-shift`, which is common for superscript/subscript labels and technical diagrams.
- SVG renderer change: `SvgStyle` now carries `baseline_shift`; presentation attributes, stylesheet rules, CSS variables, and inline style declarations parse `baseline-shift`. Supported values are `baseline`, `super`, `sub`, and numeric length/percentage values using the same unit model as SVG text spacing. `SvgText` stores the resolved point shift for each run, and both the selectable PDF text matrix and text link/clip bounding box apply it before mapping SVG coordinates to PDF coordinates. A fresh-eyes correction tightened the parser to the SVG keyword set by removing a too-lenient `none` alias for `baseline`.
- Behavior proof: new focused coverage `pdf_svg_baseline_shift_moves_selectable_tspan_text` proves `super` raises selectable text, stylesheet/CSS-var `sub` lowers it, and an inline `baseline !important` reset on a `tspan` cancels an inherited shift. Existing dominant-baseline coverage still passes, proving the two baseline mechanisms compose through the shared text matrix path.
- Mermaid/SVG integration proof refreshed this pass: `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fm-verify-showcase-20260708T0325Z scripts/verify-showcase-mermaid.sh --run-id continue-visual-20260708T0325Z` regenerated `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` from the frankenmermaid source/config and byte-compared successfully. `fmd examples/showcase.md --to pdf` rendered `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-visual-20260708T0325Z/showcase.pdf`; PyMuPDF rasterized all pages; visual inspection of `png/page-02.png` showed a legible, unclipped diagram with intact labels/arrows/dashed connector; `png/page-03.png` showed Mermaid source highlighting intact.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Heading ID Collision Writer
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T04:20:00Z.
- Files changed in this optimization entry: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `README.md` was refreshed separately in the same turn. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-20260708T0400Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-headingid-after-20260708T0420Z/`, detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/fmd-baseline-headingid-20260708T0420Z`, and SVG/showcase evidence under `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-visual-20260708T0410Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh continuation gauntlet ranked `html-large` as a top-three scenario at 13.395 ms p95 / 9.761 ms mean while recent accepted work had already covered PDF, SVG, parser, compression, and HTML font embedding. Source tracing found repeated heading-id collisions still allocated each candidate with `format!("{base}-{suffix}")` inside the collision loop.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Repeated generated headings such as `Section`, `Generated Section`, or empty headings collide predictably. The suffix is a decimal `usize` counter already tracked by the heading-id map, so the candidate string can be built with exact capacity and direct decimal writing.
- HTML change: `push_heading_id_from_inlines` now writes colliding candidates with `String::with_capacity(base.len() + 1 + decimal_len_usize(suffix))`, `push_str`, `push('-')`, and `push_usize`. The map counter remains `usize`, slug generation and tie-breaking stay unchanged, and the normal non-colliding heading path is untouched.
- README change: the public README now reflects the current `v0.3.1` release/npm status, the still-stale crates.io `0.2.0` package as checked on July 8, 2026, SVG baseline-shift text support, target-family CPU strategy for Apple Silicon and Intel/AMD, and the new HTML heading-anchor optimization without claiming unshipped SIMD.
- Behavior proof: focused heading-id, snapshot, and slug tests passed. Direct output comparison against committed `HEAD` proved `html-large.html` stayed byte-identical at SHA-256 `0ca75f7e2044f748e0ff53ee43c52442a703dfeff6d41dd06f2b4a0ad89f1389` and size `2656328` bytes for both baseline and patched renders.
- Output/performance proof: apples-to-apples 100-iteration `html-large` moved from baseline 7.435 ms p50 / 8.246 ms p95 / 7.517 ms mean to patched 7.413 ms p50 / 7.734 ms p95 / 7.507 ms mean. The honest durable claim is a small byte-preserving allocation cleanup in a repeated-heading collision path with favorable p95 evidence, not a broad HTML throughput guarantee.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Word Spacing Text
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T04:45:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-word-spacing-gauntlet-20260708T0445Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current SVG context: the renderer already supported selectable SVG text, inherited CSS/presentation `letter-spacing`, `baseline-shift`, dominant baselines, `textLength`, `tspan`, `text-anchor`, CSS variables, and inline `normal !important` resets. A remaining text fidelity gap was `word-spacing`: multi-word SVG labels could not request wider or tighter word gaps, so anchored diagram labels and adjacent tspans were measured as if only letter spacing existed.
- SVG renderer change: `SvgStyle`, `SvgStylePatch`, and `SvgText` now carry `word_spacing` alongside `letter_spacing`. Presentation attributes, stylesheet declarations, CSS variables, and inline style declarations parse `word-spacing` through the same dependency-free SVG text-spacing parser, including `normal` resets and `em`/`ex`/percent/point units. SVG text advance estimates, parent `textLength` allocation, link/clip bounding boxes, anchor adjustment, and matrix-scaled PDF width calculations now include word gap width.
- PDF text-emission change: SVG text `TJ` arrays now combine GPOS kerning, letter spacing, and word spacing. Word spacing is applied only after shaped source glyphs that correspond to ASCII space or NBSP, with those glyph ids cached once per `TJ` array when a nonzero word-spacing adjustment is active. Non-SVG paragraph/code text and zero-spacing SVG paths continue to use the same helper with zero word adjustment.
- Behavior proof: new focused coverage `pdf_svg_word_spacing_adjusts_selectable_text_and_anchor_width` proves stylesheet/CSS-var positive `word-spacing` shifts centered selectable text left by increasing measured width, positive spacing becomes a negative PDF `TJ` adjustment after a space glyph, negative spacing becomes a positive `TJ` adjustment, and an inline `word-spacing: normal !important` tspan reset cancels inherited spacing. Neighboring focused tests for `letter-spacing`, explicit `textLength`, and parent `textLength` over contiguous tspans still pass.
- Output/performance proof: committed golden-output and profiled-PDF-vs-normal tests passed. A short three-iteration perf gauntlet preserved stable generated corpus hashes: `pdf-large.pdf` stayed `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, `html-large.html` and `parser-large.html` stayed `0ca75f7e2044f748e0ff53ee43c52442a703dfeff6d41dd06f2b4a0ad89f1389`, `compress-corpus.lengths` stayed `b7dd39b697ecdbe9abb25d5983ca31d13999d2e68390879c804eb7b419ce4f33`, and `font-subset.ttf` stayed `39b2e7428ecfcedc3df5fb15830df6ceed4b1eca6718b61928150b1754310bae`. The gauntlet still ranks `pdf-large`, `parser-large`, and `html-large` as the top three hotspots, so this pass is a renderer-fidelity improvement with stable corpus proof rather than a broad throughput claim.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Text Whitespace Preservation
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T06:00:14Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated profile evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-whitespace-after-20260708T0635Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Fresh profile context: a five-iteration gauntlet before this pass still ranked `pdf-large`, `parser-large`, and `html-large` as the top in-process scenarios. A read-only SVG renderer audit then found a concrete PDF/HTML drift: browser HTML delegates embedded SVG text whitespace to the browser, but the PDF vector renderer collapsed all SVG text whitespace even when the SVG explicitly requested preserved spacing through `xml:space="preserve"` or CSS `white-space: pre`.
- SVG renderer change: `SvgStyle` now carries an inherited `SvgWhiteSpace` mode. The style cascade parses legacy `xml:space` values, presentation/CSS `white-space`, stylesheet rules, CSS variables, and inline style declarations through the same `SvgStyle`/`SvgStylePatch` machinery used for text spacing and decoration. `pre`, `pre-wrap`, and `break-spaces` preserve decoded SVG text exactly; `normal`, `nowrap`, `pre-line`, and `xml:space="default"` keep the existing collapsed-space behavior. The default collapsed path remains byte-preserving for existing SVGs unless a preservation mode is explicitly requested.
- Behavior proof: added `pdf_svg_xml_space_preserve_keeps_significant_text_spacing`, which proves default SVG text still emits three selectable glyphs for `A   B`, `xml:space="preserve"` emits all five glyphs, group inheritance preserves spacing, and `xml:space="default"` resets inherited preservation. Added `pdf_svg_white_space_pre_preserves_text_spacing_without_treating_nowrap_as_pre`, which proves stylesheet `white-space: pre` preserves repeated spaces, `nowrap` remains collapsed, inline `white-space: normal` overrides a preserving rule, and child `tspan` content inherits `pre`.
- Performance/regression proof: this pass is a fidelity improvement, not a claimed throughput win. The after-change gauntlet completed successfully and continued to rank `pdf-large` first at 135.235 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 17.043 ms p95 and `html-large` at 11.037 ms p95. Golden-output tests stayed stable, so existing committed generated HTML/PDF fixtures were unchanged by the default path.

## Active Goal Continuation - Rejected Digit Paragraph Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T07:35:00Z.
- Files changed during the experiment, then reverted after measurement: `src/parse/mod.rs` and `tests/parser_conformance.rs`. The retained file change is this `.skill-loop-progress.md` note. Generated performance evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-post-checkbox-20260708T072006Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-digit-paragraph-after-20260708T072730Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/baseline-digit-paragraph-20260708T072858Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh five-iteration gauntlet ranked `pdf-large` first, then `parser-large` second at 16.837 ms p95 / 16.208 ms mean. Parser stage evidence pointed at `block_parse_total` as the top parser stage, with `paragraph_block`, `list_block`, and table/inline work beneath it. Since previous passes had already added several broader parser and inline fast paths, this pass focused on one narrow repeated classification cost rather than rewriting the inline engine.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The paragraph loop already skips all block-interrupt checks for no-indent ASCII-letter lines. Markdown performance plans, dates, numbered headings written as prose, versions, and metric-heavy documents commonly have no-indent digit-prefixed paragraph lines that cannot interrupt a paragraph, yet they still paid for trim and block-start detector checks on every line.
- Parser experiment: `no_indent_ascii_letter_line` was temporarily broadened to `no_indent_plain_paragraph_line`, preserving the existing ASCII-letter fast path and adding a conservative digit path that skipped block-interrupt checks only when the line could not be an interrupting ordered-list marker. The source-span collector was temporarily aligned to the same helper, and a focused regression pinned ordinary digit-prefixed paragraph text, `1.` interrupts, and `01.` interrupts.
- Behavior proof passed during the experiment: the focused new regression passed, the full parser conformance suite passed, parser differential passed, parser fuzz passed, and parser spans passed. Correctness was acceptable.
- Performance proof rejected the change: apples-to-apples 60-iteration `parser-large` from a detached baseline worktree measured 16.878 ms p95 / 16.405 ms mean, while patched measured 21.761 ms p95 / 17.453 ms mean. Even if the p95 gap includes noise, the mean and p50 did not justify keeping extra digit-marker logic in the hot paragraph loop.
- Verdict: REJECTED AND REVERTED. The safe-looking digit fast path added branch work to a hot path that the canonical parser-large fixture does not exercise enough to pay back. The implementation and test were backed out; only this rejection note remains so future agents do not repeat the same speculative optimization.

## Active Goal Continuation - Rejected Table Allocator Scratch Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T07:50:00Z.
- Files changed during the experiment, then reverted after measurement: `src/pdf.rs`. The retained file change is this `.skill-loop-progress.md` note. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/baseline-table-alloc-20260708T074504Z/` and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-table-alloc-reuse-after-20260708T074621Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh `continue-current-profile-20260708T074043Z` gauntlet again ranked `pdf-large` first at 130.998 ms p95 / 130.808 ms mean, with `layout` dominating the PDF stages at 79.733 ms p95 / 397.611 ms total across five renders. The table allocator runs inside that layout stage and still allocates per-column cost vectors and per-column DP rows.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The experiment kept the same table-width dynamic-programming math and tie-breaking but reused one cost buffer plus one `next` row instead of allocating those scratch vectors per table/column.
- Behavior proof passed during the experiment: focused table allocator tests, table width-cache regression, and public PDF table tests passed. Baseline/current `pdf-large.pdf` outputs were byte-identical at SHA-256 `4224e2d46645f6337aafa352256cc049f2fc79c02bfae0936b789547e54a01df`.
- Performance proof rejected the change: apples-to-apples 30-iteration `pdf-large` moved from baseline 134.720 ms p95 / 130.015 ms mean to patched 141.275 ms p95 / 135.642 ms mean. The layout stage specifically worsened from 82.073 ms p95 / 2.340 s total to 86.002 ms p95 / 2.530 s total, even though serialization noise improved separately. The scratch reuse was therefore backed out.
- Verdict: REJECTED AND REVERTED. Keeping the precomputed per-column cost vectors is faster for this workload than rebuilding one reusable cost vector per column; future table allocator work should target algorithmic early exits or measured wrap-cost reductions, not this scratch-lifetime change.

- Current profile context: the fresh continuation gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260708T0856Z/` ranked `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.582 ms p95 / 4.558 ms mean, and PDF stage attribution showed page stream compression costing 88.981 ms total across five `pdf-large` renders. The compressor therefore remained a plausible small support-stage target after parser and font-load work.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The hypothesis was that fixed-Huffman attempts that abort into stored-block fallback could carry partial Adler-32 state and scan only the remaining input tail, rather than restarting the trailer checksum over the entire input.
- Behavior proof passed during the experiment: compressor unit tests passed, and `compress-corpus.lengths` stayed byte-identical at SHA-256 `b7dd39b697ecdbe9abb25d5983ca31d13999d2e68390879c804eb7b419ce4f33` against the pre-change baseline.
- Performance proof rejected the change: current-head baseline `compress-corpus` over 80 iterations measured 4.694 ms p95 / 4.512 ms mean. The patched run measured 4.891 ms p95 / 4.673 ms mean, and the rebuild-free rerun measured 4.861 ms p95 / 4.650 ms mean. The added checksum-state branch shape was slower on the broad corpus, so the source change was backed out.
- Verification: Agent Mail reservations as `VioletSnow` for `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused 80-iteration baseline; focused compressor unit tests during the experiment; byte-identical compression golden comparisons; focused after and rebuild-free rerun profiles; `src/compress.rs` restored to no diff; `cargo fmt --check`.
- Verdict: REJECTED AND REVERTED. Future compressor work should not repeat the stored-fallback Adler-tail state idea unless a narrower benchmark proves a call-site-specific benefit. The active broader goal remains open because PDF layout/page-content/serialization, parser work, HTML rendering, and SVG renderer breadth remain material.

- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T09:12:00Z.

Inspecting the generated `pdf-large.pdf` found 85 page streams, 13 of which had no background prelude and started directly with the body drawing operators.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. The page-content writer previously built `bg` and `body` strings for every page, then always allocated a third `stream` and copied `body` into it. For pages with an empty `bg`, the final stream bytes are exactly `body`, so the code can move `body` directly instead of allocating and copying.
- PDF writer change: the final per-page stream assembly now uses `body` by move when `bg.is_empty()`. Pages with background artifacts still use the existing `/Artifact BMC\n` + `bg` + `EMC\n` + `body` concatenation path. Mark ordering, annotation collection, structure-tree MCIDs, SVG resources, stream compression, PDF object ordering, and all emitted bytes are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: focused `profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages` and committed golden-output tests passed. The 40-iteration baseline/current `pdf-large.pdf` outputs were byte-identical at SHA-256 `4224e2d46645f6337aafa352256cc049f2fc79c02bfae0936b789547e54a01df`. The short full gauntlet validated every golden checksum, including HTML, parser, compression, font subset, paragraph, hyphenation, and both PDF outputs.
- Output/performance proof: focused 40-iteration `pdf-large` moved from 129.322 ms p50 / 133.511 ms p95 / 129.819 ms mean to 124.184 ms p50 / 126.735 ms p95 / 124.426 ms mean. The target `page_content_stream_generation` stage moved from 29.021 ms p95 / 1.110 s total to 26.821 ms p95 / 1.046 s total across 40 renders. - Verdict: PRODUCTIVE PDF PAGE-CONTENT WRITER CLEANUP. ## Active Goal Continuation - PDF ASCII Word Break Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T09:50:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-fastpath-baseline-20260708T0920Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-fastpath-after-20260708T0928Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-fastpath-after2-20260708T0936Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-ascii-word-break-profile-20260708T0945Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh continuation gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260708T0912Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 127.903 ms p95 / 126.747 ms mean, with the PDF `layout` stage still dominant at 78.771 ms p95 / 387.486 ms total across five renders. A read-only scout noticed that `flush_pdf_word` was again constructing full plain strings and character vectors before knowing whether a word could hyphenate.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0 after refinement. The initial naive restoration of the older "non-hyphenation fast path" was rejected during code review because a later correctness fix intentionally added non-hyphen separator/emergency break points for long URLs and identifiers. The accepted version preserves that long-token wrapping and only avoids work when neither dictionary hyphenation nor synthetic long-token wrapping can apply.
- PDF layout change: `flush_pdf_word` now classifies each candidate word once into byte length, character length, and ASCII-alphabetic eligibility. Short non-hyphenating words go directly to the measured word box path without constructing a concatenated string or character vector. ASCII alphabetic words that do need dictionary hyphenation now compute break points from their known character length, sharing the dictionary/emergency fill logic and avoiding a `Vec<char>` allocation that could only prove there were no separator characters. Non-ASCII, non-alphabetic, URL-like, and identifier-like long words still use the existing generic character break-point path.
- Regression targets: `short_non_hyphenating_pdf_words_stay_single_measured_boxes` pins ragged prose, short alphanumeric/punctuation words, and non-ASCII words as single measured boxes with no extra discretionary penalties. `ragged_long_pdf_words_keep_non_hyphen_break_points` pins that ragged long URL-like words still split into multiple boxes and never synthesize discretionary hyphen text. `long_pdf_words_gain_separator_and_emergency_break_points` now also proves the ASCII alphabetic fast path produces the same emergency break points as the generic `Vec<char>` path for long separator-free words.
- Rejected trial: the first implementation only added short-word gating and left ordinary ASCII hyphenation words paying the extra stats scan plus the old `Vec<char>` construction. It preserved PDF bytes but measured worse in a focused 20-iteration `pdf-large` run: baseline 134.419 ms p95 / 126.872 ms mean versus 136.786 ms p95 / 131.781 ms mean. That trial was refined before acceptance rather than recorded as a speed win.
- Output/performance proof: the accepted focused after-run `continue-pdf-word-fastpath-after2-20260708T0936Z` kept `pdf-large.pdf` byte-identical to the pre-change baseline at SHA-256 `4224e2d46645f6337aafa352256cc049f2fc79c02bfae0936b789547e54a01df` and moved focused `pdf-large` from 134.419 ms p95 / 126.872 ms mean to 127.245 ms p95 / 124.352 ms mean over 20 iterations. The final five-iteration gauntlet reported `pdf-large` at 126.262 ms p95 / 124.471 ms mean, with `layout` at 76.260 ms p95 / 371.031 ms total, `page_content_stream_generation` at 27.517 ms p95 / 137.208 ms total, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 19.949 ms p95 / 99.204 ms total.
- First-principles proof: the line breaker still sees the same `Box`, `Glue`, `Penalty`, `item_toks`, and `break_toks` semantics. Dictionary hyphenation still runs only for ASCII alphabetic words and uses the same lowercase cache keys. Long URL/path/identifier wrapping still uses the same separator and emergency break rules, and ragged policies still avoid discretionary hyphen glyphs. Rendering, tagged-PDF structure, annotations, font subsetting, object ordering, HTML output, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM/no-default portability are unchanged.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `VioletSnow`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; coordination note to `NobleSnow`; focused tests `short_non_hyphenating_pdf_words_stay_single_measured_boxes`, `ragged_long_pdf_words_keep_non_hyphen_break_points`, `long_pdf_words_gain_separator_and_emergency_break_points`, `paragraph_builder_tracks_has_boxes_without_rescanning_items`, `pdf_word_measurement`, `pdf_wraps_long_urls_instead_of_overflowing`, and `pdf_headings_stay_ragged_and_do_not_discretionary_hyphenate`; focused profiled-PDF parity test; committed golden-output test; focused baseline/current `pdf-large` release-perf runs and direct SHA-256/`cmp` comparison; final broad `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 5 --run-id continue-pdf-ascii-word-break-profile-20260708T0945Z`; final `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Tspan Sibling Boundary Space
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T10:15:47Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. The fresh profile context before this pass was `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260708T1110Z/`, which still ranked `pdf-large`, `parser-large`, and `html-large` as the top scenarios; this pass is a correctness/fidelity fix rather than a throughput claim.
- Fresh-eyes root cause: the dependency-free SVG text parser correctly normalized text nodes before child `<tspan>` elements with `normalize_svg_text_node_for_style`, preserving leading or trailing boundary spaces that separate sibling text runs. The trailing text after the final `<tspan>` accidentally used whole-element normalization instead, so `<text><tspan>A</tspan> B</text>` could emit selectable PDF text for `B` without the leading space. Browser HTML leaves SVG text rendering to the browser, but the native PDF vector path needs to preserve that boundary itself.
- Renderer change: the trailing sibling text branch in `push_svg_text_body_elements` now uses the same text-node normalization policy as earlier sibling text. Explicit `white-space: pre` / `xml:space="preserve"` behavior is unchanged because both normalization helpers decode preserved text directly in preserve mode; the change only affects default collapsed whitespace around trailing sibling text nodes.
- Behavior proof: added `pdf_svg_trailing_text_node_after_tspan_keeps_boundary_space`, which isolates the child tspan and trailing sibling text with separate fill colors and verifies the trailing selectable PDF text object emits two glyphs for ` B`, while the child tspan still emits exactly one glyph for `A`. The full `pdf_svg_` suite also passed.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `VioletSnow` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-tail-space cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_trailing_text_node_after_tspan_keeps_boundary_space -- --nocapture`; adjacent `pdf_svg_tspan`, `pdf_svg_white_space`, and `svg_text_node_normalization_preserves_boundary_space_only_for_text` tests; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-tail-space cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_ -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-tail-space-check cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-tail-space-nodefault cargo build --no-default-features`; focused committed-golden parity test; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-tail-space-clippy cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-tail-space-test cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE SVG TEXT FIDELITY FIX. This fixes a real selectable-text spacing mistake in the native SVG-to-PDF path, adds focused regression coverage, adds no dependency, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM/no-default portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because PDF layout/page-content/serialization, parser/HTML scenarios, and wider SVG/Mermaid coverage still have material remaining work.

Those strings are short, but the replacement is mechanically exact and removes allocations from SVG label decoration without changing layout, paint order, or PDF object structure.

This centralizes number formatting with the rest of the PDF writer and keeps underline, overline, and line-through geometry unchanged.
