## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Stylesheet Wrapper Selectors
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T10:30:40Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. The fresh profile context remains `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260708T1110Z/`; this pass fixes a real SVG exporter compatibility gap rather than claiming a throughput win.
- Fresh-eyes root cause: many SVG exporters wrap `<style>` contents in `<![CDATA[...]]>` or `<!-- ... -->` and sometimes insert a leading CSS comment before the first rule. The dependency-free SVG stylesheet parser used the raw bytes before `{` as the selector for both custom-property collection and normal CSS rule collection. That meant the first `:root` block or class rule could be rejected because the selector still included wrapper text instead of the actual selector.
- Renderer/parser change: selector extraction now strips common style-wrapper markers and leading/trailing CSS comments before the existing selector parser runs. The change is intentionally local: at-rules still stay at-rules, selector parsing, specificity, rule order, declaration parsing, cascade behavior, PDF writer behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM/no-default portability are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: added `pdf_svg_stylesheet_cdata_and_comment_wrappers_do_not_hide_first_rule`, which covers a CDATA-wrapped `:root` variable and an HTML/CSS-comment-wrapped first class selector in one SVG asset. Added private helper coverage `clean_svg_css_selector_wrapper_handles_exporter_wrappers` to pin the cleanup boundary and avoid accidentally treating unsupported interior CSS comments as fully parsed selectors.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `VioletSnow` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-focused cargo test clean_svg_css_selector_wrapper_handles_exporter_wrappers --lib -- --nocapture`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-focused cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_stylesheet_cdata_and_comment_wrappers_do_not_hide_first_rule -- --nocapture`; nearby stylesheet and CSS-variable tests; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-check2 cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-nodefault2 cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-clippy2 cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-svg-sweep cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_ -- --nocapture`; focused committed-golden parity test; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-svg-css-wrapper-test2 cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE SVG STYLESHEET FIDELITY FIX. This makes exported diagrams with CDATA/comment-wrapped styles render their first variables and first stylesheet rules correctly in the native SVG-to-PDF path, adds focused regression coverage, adds no dependency, adds no unsafe code, and keeps WASM/no-default portability intact. The active broader goal remains open because PDF layout/page-content/serialization, parser/HTML scenarios, and broader SVG/Mermaid coverage still have material remaining work.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Font Base64 Streaming
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T10:40:01Z.

The HTML path emits self-contained subset font CSS for every render, and the font CSS writer still base64-encoded each subset into a temporary `String` before copying that string into the final stylesheet.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. The base64 alphabet is ASCII and the final destination is already a `String`, so the encoder can append directly into the stylesheet buffer after reserving the exact encoded length. This removes one large temporary allocation and copy per emitted font face without changing font subsetting, CSS syntax, escaping, theme behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, or WASM/no-default portability.
- HTML change: `push_font_face` now computes the encoded length, reserves the final CSS capacity, and calls `push_base64_encoded` directly. The existing `base64_encode` helper is retained as a test-only wrapper over the streaming encoder so the known-vector tests keep pinning the byte format. A fresh-eyes follow-up restored a debug-only emitted-length invariant around the streaming append path.
- Behavior/performance proof: focused `html-large.html` output stayed byte-identical before and after at SHA-256 `0ca75f7e2044f748e0ff53ee43c52442a703dfeff6d41dd06f2b4a0ad89f1389`, with direct `cmp` passing. The first 80-iteration focused run moved from 8.608 ms p95 / 7.584 ms mean to 8.400 ms p95 / 7.553 ms mean. The rebuild-free rerun moved from 10.848 ms p95 / 8.242 ms mean to 10.287 ms p95 / 8.067 ms mean. The honest claim is a small allocation/copy cleanup with favorable focused evidence, not a large end-to-end renderer shift.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `VioletSnow` for `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; current-head focused `html-large` baseline; focused `base64_encoder_matches_known_vectors`; focused committed-golden parity and `default_html_embeds_deterministic_subset_font_faces`; patched release-perf build and two focused after/baseline `html-large` pairs; direct `sha256sum` and `cmp` proof for `html-large.html`; final post-assertion `cargo fmt --check`; focused encoder, golden, and subset-font smoke tests; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-check2 cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-nodefault2 cargo build --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-clippy2 cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/fmd-codex-target-html-base64-test2 cargo test`.

## Active Goal Continuation - Batch Image Byte-Limit Parity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T12:21:29Z.

- Fresh-eyes root cause: single-file renders already let callers cap explicit and auto-loaded local PNG/SVG assets with `--max-pdf-image-bytes`, but the opt-in batch renderer hard-coded a 32 MiB auto-image limit internally. That made batch less controllable for large trees and produced stale "batch PDF image limit" wording even for HTML-only auto-loaded assets.
- CLI/API change: `fmd batch` now accepts `--max-pdf-image-bytes`, `BatchOptions` carries `max_pdf_image_bytes`, and batch workers pass the configured value into the shared per-file auto-loader for both HTML data-URI embedding and PDF image/SVG drawing. The render core remains synchronous and filesystem-free; the change stays behind the native `batch` feature and adds no dependencies or unsafe code.
- Behavior proof: added `batch_auto_loaded_assets_obey_max_pdf_image_byte_limit`, which renders an HTML batch with a tiny configured image cap and proves the run exits 66, records one input failure with `error_kind:"input"`, names the auto-loaded HTML asset, includes the configured `--max-pdf-image-bytes 4` fix context, and writes no partial HTML output. Adjacent batch SVG auto-load and symlink-containment tests still pass.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `VioletSnow` for the touched files; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/cli.rs src/batch.rs tests/cli_contract.rs README.md docs/BATCH_ORCHESTRATION.md .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo check --features batch --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo clippy --features batch --all-targets -- -D warnings`; focused batch contract tests for the new byte limit, HTML SVG auto-loading, PDF SVG auto-loading, and symlink containment; full `cargo test`; full `cargo test --features batch`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE BATCH RELIABILITY FIX. This closes a real CLI/API parity gap in the native batch path and improves failure diagnostics without changing default single-file rendering, PDF bytes, HTML bytes, WASM/no-default portability, or core renderer dependencies. ## Active Goal Continuation - Self-Contained HTML SVG Remote Import Sanitization
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T12:51:43Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs`, `tests/cli_contract.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated showcase evidence under `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/html-svg-import-showcase-20260708T125132Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Fresh-eyes root cause: the previous Mermaid/showcase integration correctly embedded local SVG assets into self-contained HTML as data URIs, but a decoded frankenmermaid SVG still contained its exporter-provided Google Fonts `@import`. The URL was hidden inside the base64 payload, so plain `rg` over the HTML artifact could falsely suggest the document had no latent remote font reference.
- HTML change: SVG image assets now pass through a dependency-free sanitizer immediately before base64 data-URI emission. It removes top-level CSS `@import` statements that target `http://` or `https://` URLs from `<style>` blocks, while borrowing unchanged bytes for PNGs, non-SVG assets, SVGs without remote imports, non-UTF-8 bytes, local/non-remote CSS imports, and `@import` text inside CSS declaration strings. Image-destination safe-URL checks, MIME validation, HTML escaping, core filesystem isolation, WASM/no-default portability, dependencies, and unsafe-code policy are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: private HTML tests pin exact base64 output for a sanitized SVG payload, prove non-remote imports stay borrowed, and prove string-literal `@import` text is not stripped. The CLI file-input contract now writes a local SVG with a remote font import and asserts the emitted HTML contains the base64 of the sanitized SVG, not just any SVG data URI.
- Showcase proof: a fresh render of `examples/showcase.md` decoded the embedded SVG from `showcase.html`, confirmed the Mermaid labels such as `Markdown`, `PDF`, and `frankenmermaid` still exist, and confirmed the decoded SVG contains neither `@import` nor `fonts.googleapis`.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `TanSeal` for `src/html.rs`, `tests/cli_contract.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused private HTML tests `svg_asset_data_uri_`; focused CLI contract `html_render_auto_loads_relative_svg_assets_for_file_inputs`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs tests/cli_contract.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; feature-gated batch HTML contract `cargo test --features batch --test cli_contract batch_html_auto_loads_relative_svg_assets_for_file_inputs`; real showcase HTML render and decoded SVG payload inspection under `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/html-svg-import-showcase-20260708T125132Z/`.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Single-Segment Capacity Preflight
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T13:31:50Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/baseline-zlib-scratch-20260708T132249Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/after-zlib-scratch-20260708T132556Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/after-single-seg-len-20260708T132939Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/after-single-seg-len-rerun-20260708T133110Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.

That patch was manually removed before this pass continued. Future compressor work should not retry scratch reuse without a lower-level allocation profile that explains why the current fresh-vector path wins.
- Profile context: the focused current-head baseline still had `pdf-large` as the obvious target at 127.415 ms p95 / 122.292 ms mean. Inside it, `layout` was the largest stage at 77.355 ms p95, with `page_content_stream_generation`, `page_stream_compression`, and object serialization still material.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 4, effort 1, score 4.0. `build_single_adjusted_seg` is the hot successful fast path for same-style physical lines after paragraph breaking. It previously grew a fresh `String` without an exact capacity hint and also built a partial string before discovering a later token made the line ineligible for the single-segment path. The line tokens already expose all visible byte lengths, so a cheap preflight can validate eligibility and compute exact capacity before allocating.
- PDF layout change: `build_single_adjusted_seg` now calls `single_adjusted_seg_text_len` first. The preflight rejects nonzero extra spacing, font/link/strike changes, and style transitions before allocation, and returns the exact visible byte length for eligible same-style lines. The second pass then concatenates the same visible token text into a `String::with_capacity(text_len)` and measures the same final shaped run as before. Segment text, link/color/strike handling, task markers, justification fallback, width-cache keys, PDF bytes, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM/no-default portability are unchanged.
- Behavior/performance proof: existing focused coverage `single_adjusted_segment_caches_only_final_shaped_text` still passes and pins that the single-segment fast path measures only the final shaped text, while `profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages` still proves profiled and normal PDF bytes match. `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical before and after at SHA-256 `4224e2d46645f6337aafa352256cc049f2fc79c02bfae0936b789547e54a01df`, with direct `sha256sum` proof. The first 80-iteration after run showed favorable stage evidence despite a noisy whole-render p95: `layout` p95 77.355 -> 75.802 ms, `page_content_stream_generation` p95 28.801 -> 28.113 ms, and `serialize_total` p95 52.379 -> 50.986 ms. A rebuild-free rerun strengthened the result: whole `pdf-large` p95 127.415 -> 123.809 ms, `layout` p95 77.355 -> 75.978 ms, `page_content_stream_generation` p95 28.801 -> 27.496 ms, and `serialize_total` p95 52.379 -> 50.413 ms.

## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Repeated Code Highlight Cache
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T15:55:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-goal-profile-20260708T1519Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/baseline-blockscan-trim-20260708T1535Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/after-blockscan-trim-20260708T1535Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/baseline-html-highlight-cache-20260708T1545Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/baseline-html-highlight-cache-large-rerun-20260708T1545Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/after-html-highlight-cache-final-20260708T1545Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/after-html-highlight-cache-final-large-20260708T1545Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Rejected performance experiments: a PDF justification scratch-vector pass preserved `pdf-large.pdf` bytes but made the targeted layout stage slightly worse (`layout` total 383.447 ms -> 385.015 ms over the five-iteration gauntlet), so it was manually removed. A parser `BlockStartScan` trim-reuse pass preserved `parser-large.html` bytes exactly, but a fair 80-iteration A/B against a temporary `HEAD` source copy regressed `parser-large` from 16.756 ms p95 / 16.212 ms mean to 18.553 ms p95 / 16.653 ms mean, so it was manually removed too.
- Profile context: the fresh current-head gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-goal-profile-20260708T1519Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first, but it also showed `html-code-heavy` as a low-risk non-PDF target at 2.552 ms p95 / 2.138 ms mean. The code-heavy corpus repeats the same supported Rust fenced block 300 times; before this pass, HTML rendering re-lexed that exact same language+code pair for every occurrence.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The highlighter returns byte-offset spans into the source code, so those spans are reusable whenever both the language string and the code string are exactly equal. A one-entry per-render cache is enough for repeated generated sections and avoids adding dependencies, global state, hash maps, unsafe code, or cross-render nondeterminism.
- HTML change: `RenderState` now carries the last highlighted language, last highlighted code block, and the existing highlight span buffer as a one-entry cache. `render_block` calls `RenderState::highlight_code`; on an exact cache hit it emits the existing spans directly, and on a miss it fills the same buffer with `highlight_into` and updates the borrowed cache keys. The cache borrows from the current `Document`, so cache misses do not clone code text or copy span vectors. Unknown languages still flow through `highlight_into` and emit the same plain escaped text inside the existing `language-*` wrapper.
- Behavior/performance proof: added `repeated_supported_code_block_reuses_cached_highlight_spans` to pin the cache-hit path. Focused HTML code-block integration tests still pass for both highlighted supported blocks and unknown-language plain fallback. `html-code-heavy.html` stayed byte-identical before and after at SHA-256 `c3c3da5224822ab8fbfc4464ee786e09f45ca53d3ed84b87274522abaf4fb12f`, with direct `cmp` passing. The accepted 120-iteration code-heavy pair moved from 1.907 ms p95 / 1.862 ms mean to 1.317 ms p95 / 0.881 ms mean. A matching mixed `html-large` guard stayed byte-identical at SHA-256 `3d52ae26e73456798ca5573432b83e9f651e5fee8d161a06896d619051d5f294` and moved from 7.658 ms p95 / 7.449 ms mean to 7.480 ms p95 / 7.398 ms mean after removing the earlier clone/span-copy/precheck miss-path overhead.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `RubyFalcon` for `src/html.rs`, `tests/highlight_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `cargo test --lib repeated_supported_code_block_reuses_cached_highlight_spans`; focused `cargo test --test highlight_test code_block`; fair release-perf baseline/after profiles from a temporary `HEAD` source copy for the rejected parser trim experiment; fair release-perf baseline/after profiles for `html-code-heavy` and `html-large`; direct SHA-256 and `cmp` proof for both HTML artifacts; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE HTML HIGHLIGHTING SPEEDUP. This removes repeated lexer work for exact repeated supported code blocks while preserving exact HTML bytes and keeping the default mixed-document path flat-to-slightly-faster. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout remains the largest remaining hot path, parser-large still has material cost, and broader SVG/Mermaid quality/performance work remains larger than this pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Chained Drop-Shadow Layers
- Timestamp: 2026-07-08T17:20:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated visual evidence under `tests/artifacts/visual/goal-continue-showcase-shadow-20260708T1719Z/` is proof material only and should stay uncommitted.
- Fresh-eyes root cause: frankenmermaid-style SVG can express layered shadows as chained CSS `drop-shadow(...) drop-shadow(...)` filters. The PDF SVG renderer recognized only the first CSS function, so the vector fallback dropped the second layer even though the rest of the diagram rendered as native PDF paths and text.
- PDF SVG change: `SvgShadow` now stores a small fixed array of up to two parsed shadow layers. CSS `drop-shadow(...)` parsing walks the filter value in source order and records valid layers until the bounded array is full. The drawing path emits each shadow layer by replaying the shape path under the layer's offset/color/alpha state before painting the real SVG shape. Single `<feDropShadow>`, URL filter shadows, missing/unsupported filters, fill/stroke selection, opacity composition, paint order, markers, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM/no-default portability are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: added `pdf_svg_css_chained_drop_shadows_emit_vector_shadow_layers`, which pins two CSS shadow layers in deterministic PDF operator order, proves a CSS filter rule overrides a presentation `filter="url(#drop-shadow)"` attribute in the frankenmermaid pattern, and verifies the real fill still paints after both shadow passes. Existing single-shadow writer and SVG filter tests continue to pass.
- Visual proof: a fresh render of `examples/showcase.md` to `tests/artifacts/visual/goal-continue-showcase-shadow-20260708T1719Z/showcase.pdf` produced a 62 KiB PDF. `pdftoppm -png -r 150` yielded four pages, and manual image inspection confirmed the frankenmermaid diagram on page 2 remains readable, vector-like, correctly framed, and only subtly shadowed; pages 1, 3, and 4 retained normal typography, syntax highlighting, and final-page layout.
- Verification: Agent Mail exclusive reservations as `RubyFalcon` for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_verify_target cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_css_chained_drop_shadows_emit_vector_shadow_layers`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_verify_target cargo test --test pdf_test shadow`; focused `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_verify_target cargo test pdf_writer_tests::svg_style_operator_writers_preserve_legacy_format_shape`; `cargo fmt --check`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_verify_target cargo check --all-targets`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_nodflt_target cargo check --no-default-features`; `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_verify_target cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/tmp/franken_markdown_verify_target cargo test --quiet`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE SVG QUALITY FIX. This preserves dependency-free vector PDF rendering while matching the layered shadow idiom emitted by the current frankenmermaid showcase more closely.
